The county's fiscal year shall commence on January 1 and conclude on December 31. 
Sec. 2-142. - Disposal of county-owned equipment. 
The following is adopted by the board of commissioners to be adhered to by any and all responsible parties for the disposal of county-owned equipment: 
(1)  Any county property that is deemed as surplus will be brought before the board of commissioners for a determination as to what will be done with the property. If the property is cumbersome to move, its location will be provided to the county board of commissioners so it may view the property before making a decision of its disposal. 
(2)  When it has been determined that a piece of county property or equipment is to be sold by the board of commissioners, a minimum price that will be accepted shall be established prior to sale date. 
(3)  A county equipment/property sale date will be determined by the board of commissioners. 
(4)  Once equipment/property is deemed surplus by the county board of commissioners and a public sale date has been established, the sale shall be advertised in the official organ of the county once a week for two consecutive weeks immediately prior to the sale. 
(5)  Subsections (1), (2), (3) and (4) of this section will independently and jointly require a majority vote of the board of commissioners. 
(Res. of 6-9-1987, §§ 1—4; Res. of 9-12-1989) 
Sec. 2-143. - Drug abuse treatment and education fund. 
(a)  A special bank account shall be established at the county's deposit bank by the chair and clerk to be known as the county drug abuse treatment and education fund; 
(b)  All funds paid over to the board of commissioners by the courts or other officers charged with collecting fines and forfeited bond which has been collected, pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 15-21-100, shall be deposited into the special account known as the county drug abuse treatment and education fund; and 
(c)  The monies deposited into the county drug abuse treatment and education fund shall only be appropriated and disbursed by the board of commissioners for drug abuse treatment of citizens of the county and/or for education programs, relating to controlled substances and marijuana, which benefit the citizens of the county. 
(Res. of 9-10-1991, §§ a—c) 
Sec. 2-144. - Crime victims assistance fund. 
(a)  A special bank account shall be established at the county's deposit bank by the chair and clerk to be known as the county crime victims assistance fund; 
(b)  All funds paid over to the board of commissioners by the courts or other officers charged with collecting fines and forfeited bond which has been collected, pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 15-21-131, shall be deposited into the special account known as the county crime victims assistance fund; and 
(c)  The monies deposited into the county crime victims assistance fund shall only be appropriated and disbursed by the board of commissioners as authorized by O.C.G.A. § 15-21-132(a). 
(Res. of 9-12-1995, §§ a—c) 
Secs. 2-145—2-150. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VI. - COUNTY ISSUED PURCHASING AND/OR CREDIT CARDS 

Sec. 2-151. - Intent and scope. 
This article is intended to comply with the policy requirements of O.C.G.A. § 36-80-24 regarding the use of county issued government purchasing cards and credit cards and to include county employees in the policy requirements established in O.C.G.A. § 36-80-24. 
(Res. and Ord. of 12-3-2015; Res. and Amd. of 1-7-2016) 
Sec. 2-152. - Definitions. 
Authorized elected official means an elected official designated by public vote of the board of commissioners to use a county issued government purchasing card or credit card. 
Card Administrator means the purchasing card and credit card administrator designated by the county board of commissioners. 
County means Brantley County and/or the board of commissioners. 
County purchase card , county p-card or county credit card means a financial transaction card issued by any business organization, financial institution, or any duly authorized agent of such organization or institution, used by a county official to purchase goods, services and other things of value on behalf of the county. 
Employee means a person that works for the county for wages or a salary. 
Financial transaction card means an instrument or device as the term is defined in O.C.G.A. § 16-9-30(5). 
User agreement means the required agreement between the board of commissioners and the authorized elected officials which restricts the use of a county purchasing card or credit card. 
(Res. and Ord. of 12-3-2015; Res. and Amd. of 1-7-2016) 
Sec. 2-153. - Designated elected officials. 
The county board of commissioners ("county"), in its discretion, may authorize specific county elected officials and employees to use a county purchasing card or credit card by adoption of a resolution in a public meeting. 
No authorized elected official or employee may use a county purchasing card or credit card until and unless he or she has executed the county's purchasing card and credit card user agreement. 
The county will not make payments to any business organization, financial institution, or any duly authorized agent of such organization or institution, for amounts charged by an elected official or employee to any purchasing cards or credit cards that are not issued pursuant to this ordinance or for any purchases that are not authorized by this ordinance. 
(Res. and Ord. of 12-3-2015; Res. and Amd. of 1-7-2016) 
Sec. 2-154. - Card administrator 
The board of commissioners shall designate a county purchasing card and credit card administrator. The responsibilities of the card administrator include: 
(1)  Manage county issued purchasing cards and credit cards. 
(2)  Serve as the main point of contact for all county purchasing card and credit card issues. 
(3)  Serve as liaison to the elected officials and employees authorized to use a purchasing card or credit card, as well as to the issuer of the purchasing card or credit card. 
(4)  Provide training on card policies and procedures to the elected officials and employees authorized to use a purchasing card or credit card. 
(5)  Develop internal procedures to ensure timely payment of cards. 
(6)  Assist authorized elected officials and employees to dispute transactions when necessary. 
(7)  Establish internal procedures to ensure compliance with this ordinance, county procurement ordinances and policies, county purchasing card and credit card user agreements, applicable agreements with the business organization, financial institution, or any duly authorized agent of such organization or institution, issuing card, and state law, specifically, O.C.G.A. §§ 16-9-37 and 36-80-24. 
(8)  Document internal controls, audits and other measures to prevent and detect misuse or abuse of the cards. 
(9)  Audit and reconcile transactions monthly. 
(10)  Maintain records for at least seven years or as otherwise provided by the county's record retention policy. 
(Res. and Ord. of 12-3-2015; Res. and Amd. of 1-7-2016) 
Sec. 2-155. - Use of cards. 
(a)  Authorized purchases. County purchase cards and credit cards may be used to purchase goods and services directly related to the public duties of the authorized elected official only. All purchases are subject to the terms of this ordinance, the county purchasing card and credit card user agreement, purchasing card restrictions, county procurement policies and ordinances, and the adopted budget. 
Only authorized elected officials and employees may use a county purchase card or credit card for purchases or payments. The authorized elected official and employee shall use care to ensure that others do not have access to the card account number, expiration date and security code. 
Unless otherwise approved by the governing authority or established in the county purchasing card and credit card user agreement, the transaction limits are as follows: 
Per Transaction ..... $5,000.00 
Per Month: ..... 5,500.00 
(b)  Unauthorized purchases. County purchasing cards and credit cards shall not be used for goods and services not directly related to the official responsibilities of the authorized elected official and employee. Additionally, cards shall not be used to avoid compliance with the county's purchasing ordinances and procedures, to purchase goods and services that are not approved in the county's budget, to purchase goods and services exceeding the per transaction or per month limit, or to make purchases not in compliance with the county purchasing card and credit card user agreement. Purchases for personal goods or services are strictly prohibited. 
(c)  Receipts and documentation. Receipts, invoices and other supporting documentation of all purchases made with a county purchasing card or credit card shall be obtained and submitted to the board of commissioners office within five business days of a purchase. If an original or duplicate cannot be produced, a sworn affidavit of the authorized elected official may be substituted. The documentation must include the supplier or merchant information (i.e., name and location), quantity, description, unit price, total price, price paid without sales tax and an explanation of the purchase sufficient to show that the expense was in the performance of official county duties. 
(c)  Public records. All receipt and other documentation of purchases are public records and subject to the requirements of O.C.G.A. § 50-18-70 et seq. 
(Res. and Ord. of 12-3-2015; Res. and Amd. of 1-7-2016) 
Sec. 2-156. - Review of purchases and audit. 
Proper documentation of purchases, internal controls and other measures prevent and allow detection to misuse or abuse of county issued purchase cards and credit cards. Authorized elected officials and employees that process payments under this program shall cooperate and comply with the procedures established by the county. 
(1)  Review of purchases. All purchases shall be reviewed according to the following procedure: All purchase receipts shall be submitted to the board of commissioners office within five business days of a purchase. Shipping tickets (if any) shall be submitted to the board of commissioners office within three business days of receipt of goods. The county's card administrator, the county's financial coordinator, shall review purchase receipts with itemized statements provided by credit card companies. Any discrepancies shall be brought to the attention of the elected official or employee and if reconciliation is not made, then to the attention of the county manager. Any disputes unresolved shall be brought to the attention of the board of commissioners at a regular meeting of the board. 
(2)  Audits. The card administrator shall perform an annual review of the card program to ensure adequacy of internal policies and procedures, cardholder spending limits, monthly reconciliation procedures and documentation for transactions. Elected officials and employees shall cooperate with such review. 
(Res. and Ord. of 12-3-2015; Res. and Amd. of 1-7-2016) 
State Law reference— A process for auditing and review must be developed. O.C.G.A. § 36-80-24(c)(7). 
Sec. 2-157. - Violations. 
(a)  An elected official shall reimburse the county for any purchases made with a county issued purchase card or credit card in violation of this article or the user agreement. 
(b)  In the discretion of the county governing authority, failure to comply with the procedures outlined in this ordinance may result in: 
(1)  A warning; 
(2)  Suspension of the elected official's or employee's authority to use a county purchase card or credit card; or 
(3)  Revocation of the elected official's authority to use a county purchase card or credit card or if an employee fails to comply possible termination. 
(c)  Nothing in this article shall preclude the county governing authority from referring misuse of a purchase card or credit card for prosecution to the appropriate authorities. 
(Res. and Ord. of 12-3-2015; Res. and Amd. of 1-7-2016) 
Chapter 6 - ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGES[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference— Businesses, ch. 26. 
State Law reference— Georgia Alcoholic Beverage Code, O.C.G.A. § 3-1-1 et seq. 

Sec. 6-1. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms, and phrases, when used in this chapter shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Alcoholic beverages, distilled spirits, malt beverages, wine, retailer, retail dealer, wholesaler and wholesale dealer mean the same as set forth in O.C.G.A. § 3-1-2, as amended. 
Sheriff means the sheriff or any deputy sheriff of the county. 
(Ord. of 4-14-1998, pt. I, §§ 1, 3) 
Cross reference— Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 6-2. - Applicant criteria. 
An individual applicant must be the person who will own or manage the premises (business) where the sales of alcoholic beverages will occur. 
(Ord. of 4-14-1998, pt. II, § 1) 
Sec. 6-3. - Application for license. 
All applications for licenses for the sale of alcoholic beverages shall be made in person at the office of the clerk of the board of commissioners and shall be accompanied by a completed form or forms furnished for this purpose by the clerk, which application shall contain the following information: 
(1)  Full name, address and telephone number of the applicant; if the owner of the subject business is a partnership or corporation, the name and addresses of each partner or the name and address of each principle stockholder must be shown; 
(2)  Location or address of the place of business at which the applicant will engage in the retail sale of alcoholic beverages if and when permission to do so is granted by the board of commissioners and a license is issued; 
(3)  All applicants shall list in their application the name, home address, home telephone number and present place of employment of the person who will be employed to be the manager of the place of business for which the license is requested, if other than the applicant. No one shall be allowed to serve in a supervisory and/or managerial position who has, within five years immediately prior to the filing of the application, entered a plea of guilty, a plea of nolo contendere, or shall have suffered any conviction of a felony or any crime involving moral turpitude or involving alcohol control laws of the state or the United States; or of any other state. Thereafter, if any person other than the person listed in the application as manager shall be employed as manager, the name, address, and telephone number of the new manager shall be furnished to the clerk of the board of commissioners within five days from the date of employment of the new manager; and 
(4)  Such other information as the clerk of the board of commissioners, under the direction of the board of commissioners, may from time to time require. 
The applicant shall set forth in detail, under oath, such information as may be required. 
(Ord. of 4-14-1998, pt. II, § 2-A) 
Sec. 6-4. - Prerequisite to issuance of license; fingerprinting. 
(a)  Issuance to individuals. At the time any application for a license for the sale of alcoholic beverages under this chapter is filed at the office of the clerk of the board of commissioners and as a prerequisite to the issuance of any license hereunder, the applicant shall have a complete set of his fingerprints made by the sheriff or his designee, which shall be forwarded to the state crime information center who shall search his files for a period of five years immediately preceding the date of such application for any instance of criminal activity, and the state crime information center shall submit the results of such search to the county board of commissioners. 
(b)  Issuance to firm or corporation. If the license is to be issued to a firm or corporation, fingerprints shall be made by the sheriff or his designee and forward for investigation as set forth in subsection (a) of this section for all persons who will serve in a supervisory and/or managerial position with respect to the sale of malt beverages. If the firm or corporation changes the person in such supervisory and/or managerial positions during any year, and designate such functions to a person who has not previously been responsible for such functions referred to as new person, then such firm or corporation shall notify the clerk of the board of commissioners, in writing, of the change in such supervisory and/or managerial personnel, giving the name, address of the new person, his address, the effective date of the change and shall furnish the clerk with the fingerprints of the new person. The notification and furnishing of the fingerprints shall be within five regular business days of the office of the board of commissioners. Should the fingerprints or investigation of the new person reveal that he is objectionable, the clerk of the board of commissioners shall notify the licensee immediately, upon the receipt of such notice, the new person shall not serve in such capacity with the licensee until authorized by the commissioners. The licensee may appeal such objections to the commissioners within three days of the receipt of notice, by delivering written notice of the appeal of the clerk of the board of commissioners. As soon as possible, the commissioners will hear evidence on the appeal, but the new person shall not serve in such capacity until and unless authorized by the commissioners. 
(Ord. of 4-14-1998, pt. II, § 2-B) 
Sec. 6-5. - Publication of notice. 
The applicant for a license for the sale of alcoholic beverages shall cause a notice to appear in the official organ of the county, for two weeks, once each week, that an application for a license has been made. The notice shall contain the name of the applicant, the address, location, of the premises from where sale will occur, and the date and time when the application will be considered by the board of commissioners. The clerk of the board of commissioners shall prepare the notice for the publication; the applicant shall bear all cost of publication. The notice shall not be required for the renewal of any existing license. 
(Ord. of 4-14-1998, pt. II, § 3) 
Sec. 6-6. - Moral character of applicants. 
All applicants for licenses for the sale of alcoholic beverages shall be of good moral character or such persons' applications shall not be considered; and in no event shall any license be granted to any person where any of the individuals, or any of the corporate officers, directors or majority stockholder, have, within five years immediately prior to the filing of the applications, entered a plea of guilty, a plea of nolo contendere, or shall have suffered any conviction of a felony or crime involving moral turpitude or involving alcohol control laws of the state, or the United States; or any other state. Should any licensee, partner, officer, director or a majority stockholder of a licensed corporation, after a license has been granted, be convicted or plead guilty or nolo contendere to felony or to a crime involving moral turpitude or to a violation of any laws of the United States or of the state relating to alcohol, the licenses issued to such licensee shall stand revoked and canceled. 
(Ord. of 4-14-1998, pt. II, § 4) 
Sec. 6-7. - Considerations of extenuating circumstances. 
The board of commissioners shall consider any extenuating circumstances which may reflect favorably or unfavorably on the applicant, application, or the proposed location of the business. If, in the board's judgment, circumstances are such that the granting of the license would not be in the best interest of the general public, such circumstances may be grounds for denying the application. In considering an application, the commissioners shall consider the following factors before making any decision on an application: 
(1)  Is there any statutory prohibition of the law of the state against the issuance of such a license to such person at such location? 
(2)  Is the proposed location primarily a residential neighborhood or business neighborhood? 
(3)  Are there schools, churches and numerous dwelling houses in the immediate vicinity of the proposed license site? 
(4)  Are there other alcoholic beverages retail sales licensed premises in the immediate neighborhood of the proposed site? 
(5)  Would the issuance of such a license be compatible to the neighborhood as it is now constituted? 
(6)  Would the issuance of such a license in such location tend to diminish the property values of the adjoining lands? 
(Ord. of 4-14-1998, pt. II, § 5) 
Sec. 6-8. - Proposed location; prohibitions. 
(a)  Sales near churches and schools prohibited. No application for a license to sell alcoholic beverages shall be approved where the proposed location is within 1,000 feet of a church, school or college campus, or school grounds teaching subjects commonly taught in the public schools of the state. In determining compliance with this section, the distance shall be determined by measuring in the most direct route of travel on the ground and shall be measured in the following manner: 
(1)  From the front door of the structure from which beverage alcohol is sold or offered for sale; 
(2)  In a straight line to the nearest public sidewalk, walkway, street, road or highway; 
(3)  Along such public sidewalk, walkway, street road or highway by the nearest route; 
(4)  To the front door of the building, or to the nearest portion of the grounds, whichever is applicable under the appropriate statute. 
(b)  Consumption on premises of sale prohibited. No application for a license to sell alcoholic beverages which may be consumed on the premises of the sale shall be approved where the proposed location is within 600 feet of any house which is occupied or regularly occupied. 
(c)  Sales near existing retail package liquor stores prohibited. No application for a license for a new retail package liquor store, application for a license for the sale of distilled spirits, or the relocation of an existing retail package liquor store shall be approved if there is located within 500 yards of the proposed new location of an existing licensed retail package liquor store (licensed dealer of distilled spirits). 
(Ord. of 4-14-1998, pt. II, §§ 6-A—6-C; Ord. of 1-7-2016) 
Sec. 6-9. - Licenses and duties of licensees. 
(a)  No alcoholic beverages may be sold in the county except under a license issued in accordance with this chapter. 
(b)  Licenses for the retail sale of alcoholic beverages shall be of the following types: 
(1)  For the sale of malt beverages and wine only; or 
(2)  For the sale of distilled spirits, malt beverages and wine. 
(c)  No license for the sale of distilled spirits, malt beverages and/or wine shall be transferable, and in the event a licensed business is sold or closed, the licensee must immediately surrender his license to the sheriff. All licenses shall be issued to specific persons and shall be applicable to and valid with respect only to the business location referred to in such license. 
(d)  All licenses shall expire upon and be of no validity after December 31 next after their issuance. 
(Ord. of 4-14-1998, pt. III, §§ 1—4) 
Sec. 6-10. - Authorization of approved licenses. 
(a)  All licenses for the sale of alcoholic beverages approved, authorized and issued under this chapter shall authorize the retail sale of distilled spirits, malt beverages and/or wines either for off-premises consumption only or for on-premises consumption, provided, however, there shall be no license issued for the sale of on-premises consumption of distilled spirits. 
(b)  All licenses approved, authorized and issued on and after the effective date of the ordinance from which this chapter is derived shall be plainly and conspicuously marked either for off-premises consumption only, or for on-premises consumption. 
(c)  All licenses approved, authorized and issued on and after the effective date of the ordinance from which this chapter is derived for retail supermarkets, grocery stores, quick food outlets or other similar retail stores and for a package/liquor store shall be plainly and conspicuously marked for off-premises consumption only. 
(d)  All licenses approved, authorized and issued on and after the effective date of the ordinance from which this chapter is derived for beer parlors, lounges or other similar establishments shall be plainly and conspicuously marked for on-premises consumption. 
(Ord. of 4-14-1998, pt. III, §§ 5—8) 
Sec. 6-11. - Intention of licensing authority. 
It is the intention of the licensing authority in the adoption of the ordinance from which this chapter is derived to prohibit the consumption of alcoholic beverages on the premises of any retail outlet under the authority of any license for the sale of alcoholic beverages held under subsection 6-10(c) and to permit the consumption of any malt beverages or wines on the premises of any retail outlet under the authority of any license held under subsection 6-10(d). 
(Ord. of 4-14-1998, pt. III, § 9) 
Sec. 6-12. - Compliance of licensee with rules and regulations. 
(a)  Each licensee for the sale of alcoholic beverages under this chapter shall comply with all applicable rules, regulations, laws and statutes of the state, and shall in addition thereto or in furtherance thereof: 
(1)  Prohibit the sale, serving or consumption of alcoholic beverages in automobiles or other vehicles, or anywhere outside the main building or accessory thereto in which the business of such licensee is operated, except drive-in windows; and 
(2)  Strictly adhere to the laws of the state, respecting the sale of alcoholic beverages to persons under the age of 21 years, intoxicated persons or habitual abusers of alcoholic beverages. 
(b)  A licensee for on-premises consumption shall not permit a minor, a person under the legal age of majority as defined by the general assembly of the state, presently being the age of 18 years, to be on or about the licensed premises. 
(c)  It shall be unlawful for any licensee to allow or require a person in his employment under 18 years of age to dispense, serve, sell or take orders for alcoholic beverages; provided, however, that the provisions of this section shall not prohibit persons under 18 years of age, who are employed in supermarkets, convenience stores, or drugstores, from selling or handling malt beverages or wine which are sold for consumption off the premises. 
(Ord. of 4-14-1998, pt. III, § 10) 
Sec. 6-13. - License fees. 
(a)  For the license year commencing January 1, 1998, and ending December 31, 1998, and for each license year thereafter until changed by action of the board of commissioners, there is hereby levied and imposed a special privilege and license fee, and an excise tax in the amount equal to the total of sections 6-14—6-15. 
(b)  The license fees provided for in sections 6-13—6-15 shall be paid in full prior to the issuance of any license authorized by this chapter. 
(c)  No license shall be issued unless the applicant therefor shall have fully paid all license fees and ad valorem taxes due the county. 
(d)  All licenses granted shall expire on December 31 each year. All licenses granted shall be for the calendar year and a full license fee shall be paid for any license issued. There shall be no proration of any license fee. There shall be no refund made upon the revocation or suspension of any license. 
(Ord. of 4-14-1998, pt. III, §§ 11, 14, 19, 20) 
Sec. 6-14. - Annual license fee upon each retail distilled spirits, malt beverages and/or wine dealer. 
(a)  License fee upon each retail malt beverages and wine dealer for on-premises consumption of $270.00 payable at the time the license is issued. 
(b)  License fee upon each retail malt beverage and wine dealer for off-premises consumption only of $270.00 payable at the time the license is issued. 
(c)  License fee upon each retail dealer of distilled spirits for off-premises consumption only of $1,470.00 payable at the time the license is issued. 
(Ord. of 4-14-1998, pt. III, § 11 ) 
Sec. 6-15. - License fee and tax upon each wholesale dealer. 
(a)  There is hereby imposed a license fee of $100.00 for any wholesale dealer with a place of business located in the county, and an excise tax in the following amounts: 
(1)  For malt beverages, an amount as set forth in O.C.G.A. § 3-5-80, or as such section may be from time to time amended by the general assembly of the state. 
(2)  For distilled spirits, excluding fortified wine, and/or wine by the package, an amount of $0.22 per liter and a proportionate tax at the same rate on all fractional parts of a liter. 
All wholesalers and distributors of distilled spirits, malt beverages and/or wine wholesaling and/or distributing such commodity in the county shall add the amount of tax to be collected thereon, computed as provided in this section, to the invoice of sale to any and all retailers in the county, outside any municipality located therein, and remit the amount of such tax so computed to be due to the county directly to the office of the board of commissioners, less the sum of five percent of such tax which is hereby allowed for the collection of such tax. Such wholesalers and/or distributors shall furnish the clerk of the board of commissioners copies of all such invoices together with the amount of tax so collected at the time of payment of such taxes which shall be made and filed with the clerk on or before the tenth day of each and every month. The records of wholesalers and/or distributors shall be made available periodically to a duly authorized agent of the county for inspection and confirmation of the taxes collected as provided in this section. 
(b)  No wholesale dealer of distilled spirits, malt beverages and/or wine shall sell, ship or deliver any distilled spirits, malt beverages and/or wine to a retail dealer in the county out of the corporate limits of any municipality located therein without having first complied with all procedures, acts and doings as prescribed and required by this chapter. 
(Ord. of 4-14-1998, pt. III, § 13) 
Sec. 6-16. - Sales outside corporate limits prohibited. 
It shall be a violation of this section for any retail dealer or any wholesale dealer of distilled spirits, malt beverages and/or wine to own, hold, possess, sell or distribute any distilled spirits, malt beverages and/or wine in the county out of the corporate limits of any municipality located therein, without being in compliance with all the terms of this chapter. 
(Ord. of 4-14-1998, pt. III, § 15) 
Sec. 6-17. - Engage in business. 
The privilege to engage in the business of a retail dealer or wholesale dealer of distilled spirits, malt beverages and/or wine shall, in no event, be granted to any person except by the issuance of a license for the sale of alcoholic beverages as provided in this chapter and such privilege shall be held and enjoyed by the licensee only so long as such licensee shall comply with the requirements of this chapter and promptly pay all fees and/or taxes which are provided in this chapter. 
(Ord. of 4-14-1998, pt. III, § 16) 
Sec. 6-18. - Violations. 
Any violation of this chapter by a retail or wholesale distilled spirits, malt beverages and/or wine dealer shall be deemed as sufficient grounds for the revocation of the license issued for sale of alcoholic beverage to the violator by the board of commissioners and for the refusal thereafter to issue again any license to such violator under this section. 
(Ord. of 4-14-1998, pt. III, § 17) 
Sec. 6-19. - False statements; revocation of license. 
The making of any statement on an application for a license for the sale of alcoholic beverages required by this chapter which shall be later found to be false shall constitute grounds for revocation of such license. 
(Ord. of 4-14-1998, pt. III, § 18) 
Sec. 6-20. - Prohibition of sales. 
(a)  No alcoholic beverages shall be sold between the hours of 12:00 midnight on Saturday night until the hour of 6:00 a.m. on Monday morning. 
(b)  No alcoholic beverages shall be sold between the hours of 2:00 a.m. and 8:00 a.m. on any day by a holder of a for on-premises consumption license. 
(c)  No alcoholic beverages shall be sold on Christmas day. 
(d)  Alcoholic beverages may be sold at any time not specifically prohibited in this section. 
(Ord. of 4-14-1998, pt. IV, §§ 1—4) 
Sec. 6-21. - Inspections and licensee's responsibility. 
(a)  Inspection of premises. The business premises of a holder of a license for the sale of any alcoholic beverages, including outbuildings, shall be opened to inspection at any and all times by the sheriff. 
(b)  Retail dealer responsible for on-premises consumption. No retail dealer for the sale of malt beverages and/or wines shall allow such malt beverages and/or wines to be consumed on his premises unless such dealer has a license for on-premises consumption. Any retail dealer with a license for off-premises consumption only shall be held responsible for such consumption by his customers or other parties. 
(c)  Copy of ordinance on premises. All holders of a license for the sale of alcoholic beverages shall keep a copy of the ordinance from which this chapter is derived on his premises and instruct any person working there with respect to the terms in this chapter and each licensee and person selling such beverages shall at all times be familiar with the terms of such ordinance. 
(Ord. of 4-14-1998, pt. V, §§ 1—3) 
Sec. 6-22. - Revocations and suspensions. 
(a)  The performance of any act prohibited in this chapter or the failure to perform any act required hereby, as well as the violation of any law, state or federal, relating to the sale of alcoholic beverages shall constitute grounds for revocation of a license. 
(b)  A license for the sale of malt beverages and wine may be temporarily suspended, and the place of business closed if it has a for on-premises consumption license, upon receipt of evidence by the commissioners from the sheriff of any violation of this chapter. 
(c)  The sheriff or his lawful deputies shall be authorized, if at any time, the licensee shall be found in violation of this chapter in violation of any of the state and federal laws or regulations, to pick up the license and present to the clerk of the board of commissioners with a written report stating the violation. 
(1)  The licensee shall have the right to call for a hearing within ten days or such other time as the commissioners shall designate. Should a hearing be so called for, the hearing must be held within 72 hours of requesting it, exclusive of Sundays. If a hearing is not held within such time, then the license shall be returned until further action by the commissioners. 
(2)  The owner or employees shall cease to sell malt beverages and /or wine until the matter is concluded. 
(Ord. of 4-14-1998, pt. VI, §§ 1—2-B) 
Sec. 6-23. - Length of suspension. 
Any license for the sale of any alcoholic beverages may be suspended for a definite length of time. 
(Ord. of 4-14-1998, pt. VI, § 3) 
Sec. 6-24. - Revocation of license. 
(a)  Notice of revocation. No license shall be revoked unless the licensee has been given at least three days written notice, in person or by registered mail, of the intention of the board of commissioners to take such action. Such notice shall specify the time, place and purposes of the hearing and a statement of the charges upon which the commissioners propose to take action. At such hearings conducted by the commissioners, the licensee shall have the right to appear in person and with an attorney, and the sheriff, county attorney or the commissioners, as well as the licensee shall have the right to present evidence relating to the question as to whether or not a violation, as set forth in section 6-18, has occurred, as well as evidence relating to any extenuating or mitigating circumstances. 
(b)  Consideration of evidence. After consideration of such evidence, the board of commissioners shall, by a majority, determine whether the license shall be revoked; or whether the license shall be suspended for a definite length of time not to exceed one-half of the remaining license year. 
(c)  Hearing. If the licensee does not desire a hearing before the board of commissioners or fails to appear, the sheriff shall be authorized to then permit the owner to dispose of the merchandise within a ten-day period under the supervision of the sheriff. The merchandise may not be sold in bulk only. 
(Ord. of 4-14-1998, pt. VI, §§ 4—6) 
Sec. 6-25. - Signs. 
(a)  Display of notice. The holder of a license for the retail sale of distilled spirits, malt beverages and/or wine shall post in a conspicuous place in his place of business a notice with letters not less than four inches in height which shall be clearly visible to all customers entering the establishment as follows: "Sale of Alcoholic Beverages to Persons under the age of 21 is Strictly Prohibited". 
(b)  Advertising by use of signs. Retail dealers of alcoholic beverages may advertise the sell of such beverages by use of signs only under the following conditions: 
(1)  There shall be only one sign at a business establishment, which sign may be doubled-faced; 
(2)  The maximum dimensions for any sign shall be four feet in height and six feet in width; 
(3)  A sign may be lighted; 
(4)  All signs advertising alcoholic beverages must be located on premises of the establishment selling such beverages; and 
(5)  No sign or display or advertisement or information regarding the prices of any alcoholic beverages may be located in any window or other place visible from outside the licensed premises. 
(Ord. of 4-14-1998, pt. VII, §§ 1, 2) 
Sec. 6-26. - Violations prosecuted in the magistrate court. 
Any person who shall violate any of the sections of this chapter or who shall assist another in evading or avoiding payment of the fees and/or taxes imposed by this chapter shall be cited for evading or avoiding payment and tried in the magistrate court of the county in accordance with the provisions of state law for violations of county ordinances. Upon conviction, a sentence may be imposed by the magistrate of a fine not to exceed $1,000.00 and/or incarceration in the county jail of not more than 60 days. 
(Ord. of 4-14-1998, pt. VII, § 5) 
Sec. 6-27. - Grandfathering in of certain premises. 
No application for a license for the sale of alcoholic beverages or for renewal shall be denied by reason of closeness to a church, school, residence or other business licensed to sell packaged liquor at retail as required under subsection 6-8(a), if a license for the subject business premises had been granted prior to the adoption of the ordinance from which this chapter is derived in reliance on the prior alcoholic beverages licensing ordinance of the county, and the subject premises remained licensed without interruption. Further, no application for a license or for renewal shall be denied by reason that a house, school or church has been erected within the prohibited distance after the licensed establishment was opened, and it continued in operation without interruption. 
(Ord. of 4-14-1998, pt. VII, § 5) 
Sec. 6-28. - Display of license. 
Each person holding a license for the sale of alcoholic beverages issued pursuant to this chapter shall display the license prominently at all times on the premises for which the license is issued. 
(Ord. of 4-14-1998, pt. VII, § 6) 
Sec. 6-29. - Denial of renewal for adverse conditions. 
Should a licensee for the sale of alcoholic beverages engage in acts or conduct or permit such acts or conduct to occur on his business that creates a continuing public disturbance, traffic congestion and/or obnoxious loud noise, from or on his business premises, then the board of commissioners shall give special attention to any renewal application and make a careful review of any complaints relating to the operation of the business. Should the board of commissioners find there has been just and substantial complaints made with or by the sheriff, the licensee shall be warned and informed to eliminate the adverse conditions existing on, at or around the licensed premises. After receiving a warning, should the licensee fail to eliminate the adverse conditions, the board of commissioners shall be authorized to refuse to renew a license to such licensee or to such licensed premises. 
(Ord. of 4-14-1998, pt. VII, § 7) 
Chapter 10 - AMUSEMENTS AND ENTERTAINMENT[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference— Businesses, ch. 26. 
State Law reference— Exchange of free replay for anything of value unlawful, O.C.G.A. § 16-12-35(e); Amusement Ride Safety Act, O.C.G.A. § 25-15-50 et seq.; authority to license, tax and regulate billiard rooms, O.C.G.A. § 43-8-2; state licensing of coin-operated amusement machines, O.C.G.A. § 50-27-70 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 10-1—10-30. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - ADULT ENTERTAINMENT[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference— Giving of massages in place used for lewdness, prostitution or masturbation for hire, O.C.G.A. § 16-6-17; employee solicitation of patrons for drinks on premises unlawful, O.C.G.A. § 3-3-42; restriction of adult bookstores and movie houses to certain areas, O.C.G.A. § 36-60-3. 

Sec. 10-31. - Findings. 
(a)  The board of commissioners, based on common knowledge, investigation, and experience derived from other local government jurisdictions, believes that adult entertainment establishments as defined in section 10-33, if unregulated, will likely lead to an increase in illegal sexual activities, drug and alcohol offenses, disorderly conduct, and other criminal activity. 
(b)  Adult entertainment establishments sometimes are fronts for or operated by persons associated with criminal activities and the need to scrutinize such establishments is thereby enhanced in order to prevent the use of adult entertainment establishments for unlawful purposes. 
(c)  The law enforcement resources available for responding to problems associated with or created by adult entertainment establishments are limited and are best conserved by regulating and licensing adult entertainment establishments and those associated with them. 
(d)  The public health, safety, welfare and convenience require that adult entertainment establishments and their locations, operations, and employees be regulated and licensed in order to reduce the potential for harm, and preserve the quality of urban life in residential and business areas of the community. 
(e)  It has been shown that the location of adult entertainment establishments in close proximity to each other adversely affects property values, causes an increase in crime and encourage residents and businesses therein to move elsewhere. 
(f)  It is the duty of the board of commissioners to preserve the public health, safety, and welfare of the county, its residents, and the character of its neighborhoods and developments. 
(Ord. of 2-20-1997) 
Sec. 10-32. - Purpose. 
The purpose of this article is to regulate certain types of businesses to the end that the many types of criminal activities frequently engendered by such businesses and the adverse effect on property values and on the public health, safety, and welfare of the county, and on its citizens and property, and on the character of its neighborhoods and development will be curtailed. This article is intended to represent a balancing or competing interests: reduced criminal activity and protection of the neighborhoods and development through the regulation of adult entertainment establishments versus any legally protected rights of adult entertainment establishments and patrons. This article is not intended to allow or license any business, establishment, or activity which would otherwise be unlawful. 
(Ord. of 2-20-1997, § 1) 
Sec. 10-33. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms, and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Adult entertainment establishment means the premises on which defined establishments operate or defined activities occur shall constitute adult entertainment establishments: 
(1)  Adult business means: 
a.  Any business or establishment to which the public or any portion thereof is permitted which is conducted exclusively for the patronage of adults and as to which minors are specifically excluded from patronage thereat either by law or by the operators of such business or establishment; 
b.  Any business or establishment to which the public or any portion thereof is permitted where employees or patrons expose specified anatomical areas or engage in specified sexual activities; or 
c.  Any other business or establishment to which the public or any portion thereof is permitted which offers its patrons services or entertainment characterized by an emphasis on matter depicting, describing, discussing or relating to specified sexual activities or specified anatomical areas. 
(2)  Lingerie modeling studio means a business or establishment to which the public or any portion thereof is permitted and of which the primary business activity consists of persons exhibiting or modeling lingerie or similar undergarments and characterized or distinguished by an emphasis on specified sexual activities or specified anatomical areas. 
Chairman means the chairman of the board of commissioners. 
Church means a place where persons regularly assemble for religious worship. 
Conviction means adjudication of guilty, plea of guilty, plea of nolo contendere or the forfeiture of a bond when charged with a crime, but shall not include a discharge under provisions of what is commonly called the state First Offender Act (O.C.G.A. § 42-8-60 et seq.). 
Distance and measurement means the measurement in lineal feet from the center of any door of customer entry of the proposed premises of an adult entertainment establishment, or if not on ground level, then the beginning point for measuring the distance shall be the point of ground level determined by measuring from the center of any door of customer entry perpendicular to the ground level, to the nearest property line of any church, library, school, college, public park, residence, or hospital. A radius shall be measured from the center of any door of customer entry of the proposed premises to the nearest property line of any church, library, school, college, public park, residence or hospital. 
Employee means any person engaged to provide or in fact providing services for an adult entertainment establishment to patrons on a regular basis whether for legal consideration or otherwise. Independent contractors, such as entertainers, shall be considered an employee for the purpose of this article. 
Good moral character. A person is of good moral character according to this article if such person has not been convicted of a felony, any crime not a felony if it involves moral turpitude, or a drug-related, alcohol-related, or sex-related crime in the past ten years. 
Minor, for the purposes of this article, means any person who has not attained the age of 18 years. 
Park means any lands or facility owned, operated, controlled or managed by a county, city, state or federal government or any governmental entity or agency in and upon which recreational activities or places are provided for the recreation and enjoyment of the general public. 
Residence means a house, apartment, mobile home, boardinghouse or roominghouse, duplex, or other multifamily housing for human dwelling, or any properties owned therefor. 
School means state, county, city, church or other schools, public or private, that teach the subjects commonly taught in the common schools of this state, and vocational schools, colleges, post high school learning centers, kindergartens and day care centers for persons of all ages. 
Specified anatomical areas means and includes the following: 
(1)  Less than completely and opaquely covered human genitals, pubic region, or anus; or female breast below a point immediately above the top of the areola; or 
(2)  Human male genitalia in a discernible turgid state, even if completely and opaquely covered. 
Specified sexual activities means and includes the following: 
(1)  Actual or simulated sexual intercourse, oral copulation, anal intercourse, oral anal copulation, bestiality, direct physical stimulation of unclothed genitals, flagellation or torture in the context of a sexual relationship, or the use of excretory functions in the context of a sexual relationship, and any and all of the following sexually oriented acts or conduct: sodomy, cunnilingus, fellation, lesbianism, or homosexuality; 
(2)  Clearly depicted human genitals in a state of sexual stimulation, arousal or tumescence; 
(3)  Use of human or animal ejaculation, sodomy, oral copulation, coitus, or masturbation; 
(4)  Fondling of the human genitals, pubic region, buttocks or female breast so as to arouse or excite the sexual desires of the partner; 
(5)  Sexually oriented torture; or 
(6)  Fondling or other sexual contact with an animal so as to arouse or excite the sexual desires of a partner. 
(Ord. of 2-20-1997, § 2) 
Cross reference— Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 10-34. - Regulations. 
The following regulations apply to all adult entertainment establishments as described in this article and located within the unincorporated areas of the county: 
(1)  It shall be unlawful for a licensee to employ, admit or permit the admission of minors within a licensed premises. 
(2)  It shall be unlawful for any person to sell, barter or give to any minor any service, material, device or thing sold or offered for sale by an adult entertainment establishment. 
(3)  Notwithstanding subsections (1) and (2) of this section, an adult entertainment establishment operating in an unincorporated area of the county on the date of the adoption of the ordinance from which this article is derived shall not be required to meet the distance requirements set forth in this section as the distance requirement pertains to such location for so long as the licensee holds a legally recognized and perfected property right to use and possess such location as of the date of filing of an application for adult entertainment license or renewal thereof, but only if such legal right as to such location was vested at the time of the adoption of the ordinance from which this article is derived, and such vested legal right has continued without the necessity of act or consent to renew, continue or extend such applicant's property right by applicant or other party holding a superior legal property right in such location. 
(4)  No adult entertainment establishment shall be located within the following distances as defined and measured: 
a.  Within 1,000 feet of any single-family or multifamily residence or within 1,000 feet of any parcel of land which is zoned for single-family or multifamily uses or purposes; 
b.  Within 1,000 feet of a church, school, governmentally owned or operated building, library, civic center, public park, hospital, nursing home or community club; 
c.  Within 1,000 feet of another adult entertainment establishment; 
d.  Within 1,000 feet of an establishment selling alcoholic beverages. 
(5)  No adult entertainment establishment licensee shall employ or contract with any person to provide services or perform in the establishment who is a person not permitted for employment pursuant to this article. 
(6)  An adult entertainment establishment licensee shall maintain and retain for a period of two years the names, addresses, dates of birth and social security numbers of all employees. 
(7)  An adult entertainment establishment shall be closed between 12:00 midnight and 8:00 a.m., Monday through Saturday, on Sunday, and on Christmas Day. 
(8)  No booth, screen, partition or other obstruction shall be permitted within the interior of any adult entertainment establishment so as to prevent a clear view throughout the premises, except for separate offices, kitchens, restrooms, or the areas not frequented by patrons. 
(9)  No premises for an adult entertainment establishment shall have any interior connections or doors with any other place of business. 
(10)  No adult entertainment establishment shall be operated such that the activity on the interior of the premises is visible from the exterior of the premises. 
(11)  No licensee shall permit the use of alcoholic beverages of any kind to be sold, possessed or consumed in or on the premises. 
(12)  No licensee shall permit the use of illegal drugs or illegally controlled substances of any kind to be allowed, permitted, used, possessed or sold, and no gambling shall be allowed or permitted in or on the premises. 
(13)  No licensee shall permit an employee to expose for public view his or her specified anatomical areas in a lewd and obscene fashion. 
(Ord. of 2-20-1997, § 3) 
Sec. 10-35. - Additional regulations applicable to adult dancing establishments, erotic entertainment/dance establishments and lingerie modeling studios. 
The following additional regulations apply to adult dancing establishments, erotic entertainment/dance establishments and lingerie modeling studios (referred to in this section as adult dance establishments): 
(1)  All live dancing and entertainment shall occur on a platform intended for that purpose which is raised at least two feet from the next highest level of the remainder of the floor. 
(2)  No live dancing or entertaining shall occur closer than ten feet from any patron. 
(3)  No dancer, entertainer or employee shall fondle or caress any patron and no patron shall fondle or caress any dancer, entertainer or employee, so as to arouse or excite the sexual desires of a patron. 
(4)  No patron shall directly pay or give any gratuity to any dancer or entertainer. 
(5)  No dancer or entertainer shall solicit or accept any pay or gratuity directly from any patron nor shall any patron pay or give any gratuity to any dancer or entertainer. 
(6)  All areas of the licensed premises shall be fully lighted at all times when open for business, which shall mean illumination equal to 3.5 footcandles per square foot. 
(7)  No licensee shall permit any employee to use artificial devices or inanimate objects to depict any of the prohibited activities described in this section. 
(8)  No licensee shall permit an employee to insert an object into her vagina or her or his anal orifice, except for personal hygiene or necessity. 
(9)  No licensee shall permit an employee to engage in actual or simulated genital masturbation. 
(10)  No licensee shall permit a male employee to exhibit an unclothed erect penis. 
(11)  No licensee shall permit an employee to engage in or simulate bestiality. 
(12)  No licensee shall permit an employee to engage in actual or simulated sexual activity with any other person. 
(13)  No licensee shall permit an employee to sit upon or straddle the leg, lap or body of any patron, therein or to engage in or simulate sexual activity while touching or being touched by any patron. 
(14)  No licensee shall permit or allow a patron to participate in any act or activity upon the licensed premises which an employee is prohibited from performing. 
(Ord. of 2-20-1997, § 4) 
Sec. 10-36. - License required. 
It shall be unlawful for any person or legal entity to engage in, conduct or carry on, in or upon any premises within the unincorporated area of the county any of the adult entertainment establishments defined in this article, without a license to do so. No license so issued shall condone or make legal any activity thereunder if such activity is deemed illegal or unlawful under the laws of the state or the United States. 
(Ord. of 2-20-1997, § 5) 
Sec. 10-37. - Operation of unlicensed premises unlawful. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to operate an adult entertainment establishment unless such business shall have a currently valid license or shall have made proper application for renewal within the time required under this article, which license shall not be under suspension or permanently or conditionally revoked. 
(Ord. of 2-20-1997, § 6) 
Sec. 10-38. - Application for license. 
(a)  Application fee. Any person or legal entity desiring to obtain a license to operate, engage in, conduct or carry on any adult entertainment establishment shall make application to the board of commissioners. Prior to submitting such application, a nonrefundable fee, established by resolution of the county, shall be paid to the clerk of the county to defray, in part, the cost of investigation and report required by this article. Such fee is hereby established in the amount of $250.00. 
(b)  Application does not authorize certain conduct. The application for a license does not authorize the engaging in, operation of, conduct of or carrying on of any adult entertainment establishment. 
(c)  Terms and conditions. All licenses shall be a mere grant of privilege to carry on such business during the term of the license subject to all the terms and conditions imposed by this article and related laws, applicable sections of this article and other ordinances and resolutions of the county relating to such business. 
(d)  Front of license. All licenses shall have printed on the front these words: "This license is a mere privilege subject to be suspended and revoked under the provisions of the Ordinances of Brantley County." 
(e)  Separate license for each location. A separate license shall be required for each place of business. 
(f)  License issuance. Where the applicant: 
(1)  Is a corporation, any license shall be applied for by and shall be issued to the corporation and either: 
a.  The majority shareholder; or 
b.  A person employed full time in a managing capacity by the corporation. 
(2)  Is a partnership, any license shall be applied for by and shall be issued to the partnership and either: 
a.  The managing general partner; or 
b.  A person employed full time in a managing capacity by the partnership. 
(3)  Is a sole proprietor, any license shall be applied for by and shall be issued to the sole proprietor if he is working full time in a managing capacity on the premises, and, if not, then to the sole proprietor and a person employed full time in a managing capacity by the sole proprietor. 
For purposes of this subsection, the term "managing capacity" means the president or chief executive officer or managing or general partner of a corporation or partnership, or a person who has responsibility for management of the operations at the location to be licensed and who is a full-time employee of the corporation, partnership, proprietor, or other ownership entity. 
(Ord. of 2-20-1997, § 7) 
Sec. 10-39. - Application contents; supporting documents. 
(a)  Application and forms. Application for license shall be written and on forms supplied by the office of the board of commissioners. Such application shall state the name, address, social security number and date of birth of the applicant, and the nature and character of the business to be carried on. 
(b)  If applicant is a corporation. If the applicant is a corporation, the name of the corporation shall be set forth exactly as shown in its articles of incorporation or charter, together with the state and date of incorporation, the social security numbers of each of its current officers and directors as well as all stockholders holding more than five percent of the outstanding shares of the corporation. If the applicant is a partnership, whether general or limited, the applicant shall set forth the name, residence address, dates of birth and social security numbers of the partners. If one or more or the partners is a corporation, this subsection pertaining to corporations shall apply. 
(c)  Address. Address of the premises to be licensed. 
(d)  Name of owner; lease information. The name of the owner of the premises and, if leased, a copy of the lease agreement. 
(e)  Filing of plat of premises. A plat, filed in triplicate, by a registered land surveyor, licensed by the state, showing the location of the proposed premises is not inconsistent with section 10-34(4) which provide that no adult entertainment establishment shall be located within 1,000 feet of any residential premises, parcel of land which is zoned for multifamily or single-family use or purposes; within 1,000 feet of any parcel of land upon which a church, school, governmental building simultaneously owned and occupied by such government, library, civic center, neighborhood public park or neighborhood playground is located; within 1,000 feet of any parcel upon which another establishment regulated or defined in this article is located; or within 1,000 feet of any establishment selling alcoholic beverages. 
(f)  Information of parties with financial interest. The name, address, social security number and date of birth of any and all persons who have a financial interest of any type in the entity which is applying for the license. 
(g)  Other information required. Any other information reasonably required by the codes department of the county in verifying the right of the applicant to obtain a license. 
(h)  Multiple individuals; agent. Should the requirements of this article dictate that more than one individual and/or entity apply for a license issue to such applicants, then all such applicants shall, on such application, designate the name, address and telephone number of an individual resident of the county, to act as an agent for all applicants/licensees for the purpose of receiving communications and notices under this article. Proof of delivery to the agent shall be conclusive proof of receipt by the licensees of such notice, process or information. 
(i)  Completeness of application. Each application must be complete in its entirety before being accepted by the county for filing and processing. 
(j)  Renovations and improvements of premises. All applicants for licenses as to any premises which is to be subsequently renovated or improved shall furnish in triplicate plans and renderings of the premises as it is to exist at the time of opening. Any premises to be constructed or renovated prior to opening shall be constructed, renovated or built so as to be equal to and compatible with the surrounding neighborhood or better. The premises shall comply with all building, health and similar county codes. 
(k)  Verification of application. Each application for an adult entertainment establishment license shall be verified and acknowledged under oath to be true and correct by: 
(1)  The individual, if the applicant is an individual; 
(2)  The manager or general partner, if a partnership; 
(3)  The president of the corporation, if a corporation; 
(4)  The chief administrative official, if any other organization or association. 
(Ord. of 2-20-1997, § 8) 
Sec. 10-40. - Notice of intent to engage in business. 
(a)  Publication of advertisement. All applicants for adult entertainment establishment licenses shall give notice that application has been filed and of the purpose of making such application by publication of an advertisement once a week for four consecutive weeks prior to the date of consideration of the application by the board of commissioners in the newspaper in which legal advertisements are published. The first advertisement shall not appear more than 40 days prior to the date of such consideration. 
(b)  Size of advertisement. The advertisement shall be of type not smaller than ten point capital and lower case and shall be at least a two-inch column. The advertisement shall appear on the same days as legal advertisements are regularly published, but not among the generally published legal ads. 
(c)  Information in notice. The notice shall contain a particular description of the location of the proposed business, the name of the applicant, the date, time and place of hearing, and a statement that any legal objections to the issuance must be made at or prior to the time of hearing, and, if prior to the time of hearing, must be in writing and received by the office of the board of commissioners on or before the date and time of hearing. 
(d)  Proof of notice. Applicants shall provide proof of such notice by providing the board of commissioners, at the time of the hearing on license issuance, the affidavit of the publisher of the newspaper in which such notice was published, which affidavit shall reflect the content of the notice and the dates of publishing. 
(e)  Sign upon location of business. The applicant shall cause to be placed upon the location of the proposed business a sign stating the following: "Brantley County Adult Entertainment License Applied for. A hearing before the Board of Commissioners of Brantley County shall be held on the _______day of __________. All interested persons take notice." The sign shall be at least 18 inches by 24 inches in size and shall face toward all public streets, sidewalks or other public property which adjoins the location so as to be clearly visible by persons using such public area. The sign shall be posed on the property from the date of the first publication of the legal advertisement through the date of consideration by the board of commissioners. 
(Ord. of 2-20-1997, § 9) 
Sec. 10-41. - Application; investigation; issuance. 
The chairman of the board of commissioners or his designee shall have a reasonable time not to exceed 30 days to investigate the application for an adult entertainment establishment and the background of the applicant. Upon completion of the investigation and after holding a public hearing, the board of commissioners shall issue the license if it is determined that: 
(1)  The application conforms in all respects to the provisions of this article. 
(2)  The applicant has not made a material misrepresentation in this application. 
(3)  The applicant has fully cooperated in the investigation of his application. 
(4)  The applicant, if an individual, or any officers or directors or shareholders holding more than five percent of the outstanding shares of the corporation, if the applicant is a corporation, or any partners, including limited partners, if the applicant is a partnership, has not been convicted in a court of competent jurisdiction of any crime involving sexual assault, sexual battery, prostitution, rape, sexual offenses against children, unnatural sex acts, public indecency, or any other sex act, whether attempted or consummated, prohibited by law for which: 
a.  Less than two years have elapsed since the date of conviction or the date of release from confinement imposed for the conviction, whichever is the later date, if the conviction is of a misdemeanor offense; 
b.  Less than five years have elapsed since the date of conviction or the date of release from confinement for the conviction, whichever is the later date, if the conviction is a felony offense; 
c.  Less than five years have elapsed since the date of the last conviction or the date of release from confinement for the last conviction, whichever is the later date, if the convictions are of two or more misdemeanor offenses or combination of misdemeanor offenses occurring within any 24-month period. 
(5)  The applicant, if an individual, or any officers or directors or shareholders holding more than five percent of the outstanding shares of the corporation, if the applicant is a corporation, or any of the partners, including limited partners, if the applicant is a partnership, has not, during the past ten years, had an adult entertainment establishment license or other similar license or permit denied or revoked in this county or any other local governmental jurisdiction located in or out of this state prior to the date of application. 
(6)  The building, structure, equipment, or location of such business, as proposed by the applicant, would comply with all applicable distance provisions of this article and would qualify to receive a certificate of occupancy. 
(7)  The applicant is at least 21 years of age. 
(8)  On the date the business for which a license is required commences and thereafter, there will be a responsible person on the premises to act as manager at all times during which the business is open. 
(9)  Notwithstanding subsections (1)—(8) of this section, no license shall be issued to an applicant if within 12 months immediately preceding the filing of an application one or more of the following shall have occurred: 
a.  The same applicant for a license or renewal has been rejected for any location, if such rejection was based upon the applicant's failure to meet the terms of this article applicable to the applicant as opposed to rejection for reasons related to the location itself. 
b.  The location has been rejected for any applicant. 
c.  The applicant has withdrawn, without providential cause, an application at any time within seven days immediately preceding the time and date set for the hearing before the board of commissioners unless at least one year shall have expired from such withdrawal. 
d.  The one year waiting period will not apply where the applicant shall apply for a new location which has not been rejected within the preceding 12 months, except if the applicant has had an application for another location rejected within the preceding 12 months because of lack of qualifications of the applicant. 
(10)  Notwithstanding subsections (1)—(9) of this section, no license shall be issued until an annual license fee, established by resolution of the county and prorated on a calendar year basis, is paid to the county clerk. The annual license fee is hereby resolved to be $3,000.00. 
(Ord. of 2-20-1997, § 10) 
Sec. 10-42. - License renewal. 
Licenses for adult entertainment establishments shall be renewed on a calendar year basis provided that the licensee continues to meet the requirements set out in this article. The renewal fee for the adult entertainment establishment license shall be established by resolution of the board of commissioners. The renewal fee is hereby resolved to be $3,000.00. Renewal applications shall be submitted by November 15 of each year prior to January 1 of the year for which such license is requested. 
(Ord. of 2-20-1997, § 11) 
Sec. 10-43. - License nontransferable. 
No adult entertainment establishment license may be sold, transferred or assigned by a licensee, or by operation of law, to any other person. Any such sale, transfer or assignment, or attempted sale, transfer or assignment, shall be deemed to constitute a voluntary surrender of such license and such license shall thereafter be null and void; provided and excepted, however, that if the licensee is a partnership or corporation, and one or more of the partners or shareholders, as the case may be, should die, one or more of the surviving partners or shareholders who were partners or shareholders at the time of issuance of the license may acquire, by purchase or otherwise, the interest of the deceased partner or shareholder without affecting a surrender or termination of such license and in such case, the licensee shall immediately notify the office of the board of commissioners. An adult entertainment establishment license issued to a corporation shall be deemed terminated and void when either any outstanding stock of the corporation is sold, transferred or assigned after the issuance of a license, or any stock authorized but not issued at the time of the granting of a license pursuant to this article is thereafter issued and sold, transferred or assigned. 
(Ord. of 2-20-1997, § 12) 
Sec. 10-44. - Change of location. 
No adult entertainment establishment licensee shall change the location of the establishment without obtaining a new license. 
(Ord. of 2-20-1997, § 13) 
Sec. 10-45. - Change of name. 
No adult entertainment establishment licensee shall advertise, operate, conduct, manage, engage in, or carry on an adult entertainment establishment under any name other than his name and the name of the business as specified on his license. 
(Ord. of 2-20-1997, § 14) 
Sec. 10-46. - Modification of licensed premises. 
After issuance of any adult entertainment establishment license, no change in the location of the building within the premises, customer entry locations, or other changes shall be made which would affect compliance with any distance or other requirement of this article. 
(Ord. of 2-20-1997, § 15) 
Sec. 10-47. - License; refusal. 
If the chairman or his designee, following investigation of the applicant for an adult entertainment establishment license, deems that the applicant does not fulfill the requirements as set forth in this article, he shall so notify the applicant of such decision in writing and the basis thereof. Any such decision shall be final unless appeal is filed to the board of commissioners by any aggrieved party on or before ten days of the date of the decision. A hearing by the board of commissioners of the appeal shall occur within 30 days of its filing at a regular or special meeting of the board. 
(Ord. of 2-20-1997, § 16) 
Sec. 10-48. - Suspension of license. 
The chairman of the board of commissioners may suspend an adult entertainment establishment license for a period of 180 days if he determines that the licensee or an employee has violated any section of this article. If the chairman deems a license suspension appropriate, he shall so notify the licensee of such decision in writing and the basis thereof. Such suspension shall take effect ten days following the licensee's notification unless an appeal is filed with and to the board of commissioners by the aggrieved party on or before ten days of the date of receipt by the aggrieved party of the decision. A hearing by the board of commissioners of the appeal shall occur within 30 days of its filing in a regular or special meeting of the board. Enforcement of the suspension shall be stayed pending the board's ruling on the licensee's appeal. 
(Ord. of 2-20-1997, § 17) 
Sec. 10-49. - Revocation. 
(a)  The chairman of the board of commissions may revoke a license for an adult entertainment establishment if a cause for suspension occurs and the license has been suspended within the past 12 months. 
(b)  The chairman may also revoke a license if he determines that: 
(1)  A licensee gave false or misleading information in the material submitted during the application process. 
(2)  A licensee or an employee knowingly operated the sexually oriented business during a period of time when the licensee's license was suspended. 
(3)  A licensee or an employee has knowingly, allowed any act of sexual intercourse, sodomy, or copulation, masturbation, or other illegal sexual conduct to occur in or on the licensed premises. 
(4)  The owner or operator of the licensed establishment knowingly allowed a person under 18 years of age to enter the establishment. 
(c)  If the chairman deems a license revocation appropriate, he shall so notify the licensee of such decision in writing and the basis thereof. Such revocation shall take effect ten days following the chairman's serving of his written decision upon the licensee unless an appeal is filed with and to the board of commissioners by the aggrieved party on or before ten days of the date of receipt by the aggrieved party of the decision of the chairman. A hearing by the board of commissioners on the decision shall occur within 30 days of its filing in a regular or special meeting of the board. Revocation shall continue for a one-year period from the date revocation becomes effective. 
(Ord. of 2-20-1997, § 17(a), (b)) 
Sec. 10-50. - Appeal procedure. 
An applicant for an adult entertainment establishment license or licensee who has timely filed an appeal with the board of commissioners as allowed by this section shall be entitled to a hearing before the board of commissioners. At the time set for the hearing, the board of commissioners shall receive all relevant testimony in evidence from county staff or interested parties, and from the licensee or employee. In all hearings pursuant to this article, the following procedures shall apply: 
(1)  The chairman of the board of commissioners shall read or cause to be read the charges and specifications against the charged party. He shall then read or cause to be read any response filed by the charged party. 
(2)  The board of commissioners shall hear the evidence upon the charges and specifications as filed against the charged party and shall not consider any additional evidence beyond the scope of the charges and may exclude evidence which is purely cumulative. 
(3)  The order of proof shall be as follows: The county representative shall present his evidence in support of the charges; the charged party shall then present his evidence. Evidence of each party may be supported by submission of pertinent documents. Each party shall be allowed to present pertinent rebuttal evidence. 
(4)  The charged party and county may be represented by counsel, and may present, examine and cross examine witnesses. Additionally, the board of commissioners may interrogate all parties and witnesses to obtain necessary information. 
(Ord. of 2-20-1997, § 17(c)) 
Sec. 10-51. - Violations and penalties. 
(a)  Any person violating this article shall be punishable as provided in section 1-12. 
(b)  Should any license be revoked or suspended, all signs indicating such businesses conducted on the premises shall be removed from the premises during the period of revocation or suspension. 
(c)  The violation of provisions of this article by any person may be enjoined by instituting appropriate proceedings for injunction in any court of competent jurisdiction. Such action may be maintained notwithstanding that other adequate remedies at law exist. 
(Ord. of 2-20-1997, § 17(d)) 
Sec. 10-52. - Service of notice. 
(a)  Any notice required to be given under this article to any applicant for an adult entertainment establishment license, licensee or employee may be given either by personal delivery or by certified United States Postal Service postage prepaid, return receipt requested, addressed to the most recent address as specified in the application for license/permit, or such updated address which may have subsequently been provided in writing to the county clerk. Notices mailed as described in this section shall be deemed given on the second day subsequent to their deposit in the United States Postal Service. 
(b)  It shall be the duty of each applicant, licensee and employee to furnish notice to the county clerk in writing of any change of mailing address. 
(Ord. of 2-20-1997, § 17(e)) 
Sec. 10-53. - Employment. 
(a)  Approval for employment. 
(1)  A permit to work in or be employed by an adult entertainment establishment shall be required for all employees. For the purpose of this article, independent contractors whose main purpose is to provide entertainment or other services to patrons, including but not limited to dancers and waitresses, employed or hired by an adult entertainment establishment shall be considered as employees and shall be licensed as employees, regardless of the business relationship with the owner or licensee of any adult entertainment establishment. 
(2)  No person requiring a permit may be employed by or work in an establishment until such person has filed an application, paid the fee for and obtained a work permit from the county clerk.
