(a)  Practitioners as described in O.C.G.A. Practitioners of professions as described in O.C.G.A. § 48-13-9(c)(1)—(18) shall elect as their entire occupation tax one of the following: 
(1)  The occupation tax based on the number of employees as set forth in section 22-32. 
(2)  A fee of $25.00 per practitioner who is licensed to provide the service, such tax to be paid at the practitioner's office or location. This election is to be made on an annual basis and must be done by January 31 of each year. 
(b)  Practitioners exclusively practicing for a government. Any practitioner whose office is maintained by and who is employed in practice exclusively by the United States, the state, a municipality or county of the state, instrumentalities of the United States, the state, or a municipality or county of the state shall not be required to obtain a license or pay an occupation tax for that practice. 
(Ord. of 12-12-1995, § 9) 
Sec. 26-39. - When tax due and payable; effect of transacting business when tax delinquent. 
(a)  Each such occupation tax shall be for the calendar year unless otherwise specifically provided. The registration and occupation tax shall be payable January 1 of each year and shall, if not paid by March 31 of each year, be subject to penalties for delinquency as prescribed in this article. On any new profession, trade, or calling begun in the county in 1996, or succeeding years thereafter, the registration and tax shall be due immediately upon beginning business. A ten-percent penalty shall be imposed if the tax levied in this article has not been paid within 90 days of its due date. The tax registration provided for in this article shall be issued by the clerk of the board of commissioners and if any person whose duty it is to obtain a registration shall, after such registration or occupation tax becomes delinquent, transact or offer to transact, in the county, any of the kind of profession, trade, or calling subject to this article without having first obtained such registration, such offender shall, upon conviction, be punished by fine and/or imprisonment as provided in section 26-52. 
(b)  In addition to the remedies in subsection (a) of this section, the tax may be collected in the same manner as provided by law for tax executions. The clerk of the board of commissioners is authorized to issue executions against the delinquent taxpayer as provided O.C.G.A. § 48-13-26(a). 
(Ord. of 12-12-1995, § 10) 
Sec. 26-40. - Businesses operated for charitable purposes. 
No business on which an occupation tax is levied by this article shall be exempt from the registration or tax on the grounds that such business is operated for a charitable purpose, unless 50 percent or more of the entire proceeds from the business are devoted to such purpose. 
(Ord. of 12-12-1995, § 11) 
Sec. 26-41. - Liability of officers and agents; registration required; failure to obtain: 
All persons subject to the occupation tax levy pursuant to this article shall be required to obtain the necessary registration for the business as described in this article, and in default thereof the officer or agent soliciting for or representing such business, the persons shall be subject to the same penalty as other persons who fail to obtain a registration. Every person commencing business in the county after January 1 of each year shall likewise obtain the registration provided for in this article before commencing such business; and any person transacting, or offering to transact in the county, any of the kinds of businesses, trades, professions, or occupation without first having so obtained such registration shall be subject to penalties provided in section 26-52. 
(Ord. of 12-12-1995, § 12) 
Sec. 26-42. - Businesses not covered by this article. 
The following businesses are not covered by this article but may be assessed an occupation tax or other type of tax pursuant to the provisions of other general laws of the state or by local law: 
(1)  Those businesses regulated by the state service commission. 
(2)  Those electrical service businesses organized under O.C.G.A. tit. 46, ch. 3. 
(3)  Any farm operation for the production from or on the land of agricultural products, but not including agribusiness. 
(4)  Cooperative marketing associations governed by O.C.G.A. § 2-10-105. 
(5)  Insurance companies governed by O.C.G.A. § 33-8-8 et seq. 
(6)  Motor common carriers governed by O.C.G.A. § 46-7-15. 
(7)  Those businesses governed by O.C.G.A. § 48-5-355 (Businesses that purchase carload lots of guano, meats, meal, flour, bran, cottonseed, or cottonseed meal and hulls.) 
(8)  Agricultural products and livestock raised in the state governed by O.C.G.A. § 48-5-356. 
(9)  Depository financial institutions governed by O.C.G.A. § 48-6-93. 
(10)  Facilities operated by a charitable trust governed by O.C.G.A. § 48-13-55. 
(Ord. of 12-12-1995, § 13) 
Sec. 26-43. - License duration. 
Each license issued under this article shall be valid for the calendar year in which issued. 
(Ord. of 12-12-1995, § 14) 
Sec. 26-44. - Transfers prohibited. 
No tax registration certificate issued under this article shall be transferable; and no registration certificate shall be exchanged for a registration certificate for a different type of business. 
(Ord. of 12-12-1995, § 15) 
Sec. 26-45. - Application. 
(a)  Every person subject to the tax levied under this article shall, on or before January 31st of each year, or prior to engaging in said business, file with the Clerk of the Brantley County Commission or her designed representative, an application for a county business and occupation tax registration certificate. 
(b)  Every person subject to the tax shall make application for said registration certificate on forms provided by the county, setting forth, at a minimum, the following information: 
(1)  Name of business/occupation; 
(2)  Location of the business/occupation office; 
(3)  Exact nature of business/occupation for which a registration certificate is requested; and 
(4)  A copy of a picture identification document issued by a state or federal agency, such as a driver's license, identifying the applicant thereon. 
(Ord. of 12-12-1995, § 16; Ord. of 12-14-2004, § 1) 
Sec. 26-46. - Veterans. 
Persons who can qualify for a state veterans free license under O.C.G.A. § 43-12-1 must secure such license from the state and present such license to the county clerk, who will honor such license and issue a county business and occupation tax registration certificate without requiring payment of the tax and mark the registration certificate "Exempt from tax." 
(Ord. of 12-12-1995, § 17) 
Sec. 26-47. - Displaying registration certificate. 
All persons having paid the tax required by this article shall exhibit the business and occupation tax registration certificate, or receipt therefor, issued them by the county clerk in a conspicuous place in the office or quarters of such establishment or place of business. 
(Ord. of 12-12-1995, § 18) 
Sec. 26-48. - Location of business. 
(a)  Registration certificate location. Registration certificates granted under this article shall not authorize the holder of such certificate to exercise or carry on the trade, business, or profession named therein at any other place than that mentioned in the registration certificate. 
(b)  Change of location. Upon removal of any taxpayer from the premises at which the trade, business, or profession identified on the registration certificate was authorized to be conducted, it may and shall be lawful for the county clerk, by endorsement upon such registration certificate, to authorize the taxpayer, removing to any other location, to carry on the trade, business or profession under such certificate. 
(Ord. of 12-12-1995, §§ 19, 20) 
Sec. 26-49. - Refund to discontinued business. 
When the tax fixed by this article has been paid during the first half of the calendar year and the person paying such tax discontinues the business during the first half of the calendar year, the county clerk may refund one-half of such year's tax, provided all other license fees and other taxes owed by the taxpayer to the county have been paid, and provided application therefor is made within 30 days after discontinuing the business. 
(Ord. of 12-12-1995, § 21) 
Sec. 26-50. - Restrictions. 
No person shall be issued a the county business and occupation tax registration certificate as provided for in this article, who is required to hold a license issued by the state to engage in the business profession or trade for which the person seeks to engage in, or is required to obtain health permits, or any other such regulatory permit or license, unless the person has a valid and current state license, or show evidence that all regulatory requirements have been met and attaches a copy of the application. Any revocation or suspension of a person's state license or permit will cause an immediate termination or suspension of such person's registration certificate issued by the county. 
(Ord. of 12-12-1995, § 22) 
Sec. 26-51. - Enforcement. 
The sheriff of the county, the deputies thereto, constables and all other law enforcement officers and the county clerk shall be authorized to issue citations to violators of this article. 
Such citation shall state the time and place at which the accused is to appear for trial, shall identify the offense with which the accused is charged, shall be signed by the officer who completes and services it, and the original shall be filed with the court. 
(Ord. of 12-12-1995, § 23) 
Sec. 26-52. - Penalty. 
Any person violating any provisions of this article shall, upon conviction, be punished as provided in section 1-12. 
(Ord. of 12-12-1995, § 24) 
Sec. 26-53. - Court proceedings. 
(a)  Violations of this article shall be tried upon citation as described in section 26-51 and may be tried with or without a prosecuting attorney as well as upon accusations. The county attorney shall serve as prosecuting attorney. 
(b)  Violations of this article shall be tried in the magistrate court of the county, and shall be tried in accordance with the O.C.G.A. § 15-10-60 et seq. 
(c)  Nothing in this article shall prevent the commissioners of the county from bringing any civil action to present, correct or abate any violation of this article. No penalty or remedy prescribed in this article shall be considered exclusive of any other remedy, but shall be available in addition to any other penalty or remedy by law. 
(d)  Each violation of this article shall constitute a separate offense. 
(Ord. of 12-12-1995, § 25) 
Sec. 26-54. - Applications of provisions to prior ordinance. 
This article does not repeal or affect the force of any part of any ordinance heretofore passed where taxes or fees levied under such prior ordinance have not been paid in full. So much and such parts of ordinances heretofore and hereinafter passed as provided for the issuing and enforcing of execution for any tax or assessment required by such ordinances, or that imposed fines or penalties for the nonpayment of such tax, or for failure to pay regulatory fees provided for in such ordinance, or failure to comply with any other provisions thereof, shall continue and remain in force until such tax, fee, or assessment shall be fully paid. 
(Ord. of 12-12-1995, § 26) 
Sec. 26-55. - Requirement of public hearing before tax increase. 
After January 1, 1996, the board of commissioners shall conduct at least one public hearing before adopting any ordinance or resolution which will increase the rate of occupation tax as set forth in this article. 
(Ord. of 12-12-1995, § 27) 
Secs. 26-56—26-90. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - DEALERS IN PRECIOUS METALS AND GEMS; PAWNSHOPS[3] 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
Editor's note— An ordinance adopted April 9, 2015, in effect, repealed art. III, §§ 26-91—26-96 and enacted a new art. III as set out herein. Former art. III pertained to similar subject matter and derived from an ordinance adopted November 14, 1995. 
State Law reference— Duties of purchasers of gold bullion, gold dust, etc., see O.C.G.A. § 12-4-120 et seq.; Junk dealers, see O.C.G.A § 43-22-1 et seq.; Dealers in precious metals and gems, see O.C.G.A. § 43-37-1 et seq.; Dealers in used watches, see O.C.G.A. §43-491 et seq.; Liens - Pawnbrokers, factors, bailees, etc., see O.C.G.A. §44-14-400 et seq.; and Liens - Jewelers, see O.C.G.A. § 44-14-430 et seq. 

Sec. 26-91. - Definitions. 
For the purposes of this chapter, the following words and terms shall have the meanings respectively ascribed to them: 
Dealer in precious metals and gems means any person, whether as owner, agent or employee, who engages in the business of purchasing precious metals or gems or articles containing any precious metal or gem, including coins, from members of the general public for resale to brokers, dealers or melters. 
Electronic reporting system means a computer based system, as specified by the sheriff, which is designed to record and transmit data and information electronically. 
Gems means any precious or semi-precious stone which is cut and polished. 
Goods means every species of tangible personal property. 
Pawnbroker means any person, whether as owner, agent or employee, engaged in whole or in part in the business of lending money on the security of pledged goods, or in the business of purchasing tangible personal property on the condition that it may be redeemed or repurchased by the seller for a fixed price within a fixed period of time, or in the business of purchasing tangible personal property from persons or sources other than manufacturers or licensed dealers as part of or in conjunction with the business activities described in this section. 
Pawnshop means any person, whether as owner, agent or employee, engaged in whole or in part in the business of lending money on the security of pledged goods, or in the business of purchasing tangible personal property on the condition that it may be redeemed or repurchased by the seller for a fixed price within a fixed period of time, or in the business of purchasing tangible personal property from persons or sources other than manufacturers or licensed dealers as a part of or in conjunction with the business activities described in the section. 
Person means an individual, partnership, corporation, joint venture, trust, association, or other legal entity however organized. 
Precious metals means, gold, silver or platinum or any metal containing gold, silver or platinum. 
(Ord. of 4-9-2015; Amd. of 2-4-2016) 
Sec. 26-92. - Jurisdiction and penalty for violation. 
Any person who shall violate any of the provisions of this article as amended shall be punished upon conviction in the Magistrate Court of Brantley County. 
(Ord. of 4-9-2015; Amd. of 2-4-2016) 
Sec. 26-93. - License required. 
It shall be unlawful for a buyer of precious metals and gems to engage in such business within the county without first obtaining a license in compliance with the provisions of this chapter. 
(Ord. of 4-9-2015; Amd. of 2-4-2016) 
Sec. 26-94. - Application for license. 
Applicants for a license pursuant to this chapter shall file with the county clerk a written application under oath, signed by the applicant if an individual, or by all partners if a partnership, or by the president of the corporation, and showing the following: 
(1)  The name of the person having the management or supervision of the applicant's business during the time that it is proposed that it will be carried on within the county; the local address of such person while engaged in such business; the permanent address of such person; the capacity in which such person will act, that is, whether as proprietor, agent or otherwise; the name and address of the person on whose account the business will be conducted, if any; and, if a corporation, the name of the state in which the corporation is located; 
(2)  The place within the county where it is proposed to conduct the applicant's business, and the length of time during which it is proposed that such business will be conducted; 
(3)  Credentials from the person for which the applicant proposes to do business, authorizing the applicant to act as representative; and 
(4)  Such other reasonable information as to the identity and character of the person having the management or supervision of the business and the manner of doing business as the county commissioners may deem proper in order to fulfil the purpose of this chapter in the protection of the public interest. 
(Ord. of 4-9-2015; Amd. of 2-4-2016) 
Sec. 26-95. - Posting of license. 
The license issued pursuant to this chapter shall be posted conspicuously and prominently in the place of business named therein. If the applicant desires to do business in more than one place within the county, separate licenses shall be purchased and issued for each place of business, and shall be posted conspicuously and prominently in each place of business. 
(Ord. of 4-9-2015; Amd. of 2-4-2016) 
Sec. 26-96. - License fee. 
License under this chapter shall pay a license fee of $250.00 for each calendar year or portion of a year in which the licensee engages in business within the county. For each business location in addition to one, the licensee shall pay an additional license fee of $250.00 for each calendar year or portion of a year in which the licensee conducts business at such additional location. 
(Ord. of 4-9-2015; Amd. of 2-4-2016) 
Sec. 26-97. - Revocation of license. 
(a)  The license issued pursuant to this chapter may be revoked by the board of commissioners and its designated hearing officer, the county manager, after notice and hearing, for any of the following causes: 
Any fraud, misrepresentation or false statement contained in the application for license; 
(1)  Any fraud, misrepresentation or false statement made in connection with any purchase transaction; 
(2)  Failure to maintain the daily record as required in this chapter; 
(3)  Any other violation of this chapter; or 
(4)  Conducting the business licensed under this chapter in any unlawful manner or in such a manner as to constitute a breach of the peace or to constitute a menace to the health, safety or general welfare of the public. 
(b)  Notice of hearing for revocation of a license shall be given in writing, setting forth specifically the grounds of the complaint and the time and place of the hearing. The notice shall be served on the licensee by handing the notice personally to the person in charge of the licensee's business, or by mailing the notice, postage prepaid, to the licensee, at his/her last known address, at least five days prior to the date set for the hearing. 
(Ord. of 4-9-2015; Amd. of 2-4-2016) 
Sec. 26-98. - Records and information to be recorded. 
Every person or business engaged as a pawnbroker, pawnshop, or dealer in precious metals and gems within the unincorporated areas of the county shall secure from every personal from whom he or she receives any goods, except used books, whether by purchase or through pledge, trade, pawn or exchange, the following: 
(1)  Government-issued photo identification card, such as a driver's license, military identification card, state identification card or passport; 
(2)  The name, address, telephone number, race, sex, height, weight, date of birth, and a social security or driver's license number; 
(3)  A digital photograph clearly showing a frontal view of the subject's face. Each digital image shall be labeled with the date and time of the transaction and stored in such a manner that they are safe from corruption. If the same subject makes additional transactions within 30 days of the original transaction; provides the same governmental issued photo identification card as mentioned above; and the subject's appearance has not materially changes, a new digital photograph shall not be required until a transaction is made after 30 days from the original transaction; 
(4)  A complete and accurate description of the goods acquired, and a digital photograph or image of the goods acquired including the following information, if available: 
a.  Brand name; 
b.  Model number; 
c.  Manufacturer's serial number; 
d.  Size; 
e.  Color, as apparent to the untrained eye; 
f.  Precious metal type, weight, and content if known; 
g.  Gemstone description, including the number of stones; 
h.  In the case of firearms, the type of actions, caliber or gauge, number of barrels, barrel length, and finish; 
i.  Any other unique identifying marks, numbers or letters; 
j.  The date and time of transaction. 
(5)  The pawnbroker, pawnshop, and dealer in precious metals and gems shall maintain the above information and digital photographs or images for a period of three years and make the same available to law enforcement personnel upon request. 
(6)  The pawnbroker, pawnshop, and dealer in precious metals and gems shall require the seller to sign a statement verifying that the seller is the rightful owner of the goods or is entitled to sell, consign, or trade the goods. 
(7)  This section shall not apply to the receipt of used books or pawn transactions commonly known as "title pawn" transactions where the pawnbroker takes possession of a motor vehicle certificate of title, takes a security interest in the motor vehicle certificate of title, and retains physical possession of the vehicle certificate of title for the entire length of the pawn transaction. 
(Ord. of 4-9-2015; Amd. of 2-4-2016) 
Sec. 26-99. - Report to sheriff; required format. 
(a)  Every pawnbroker, pawnshop, and dealer in precious metals and gems located within the county shall make a computer-generated daily report, in such format as prescribed by the sheriff, of all transactions that occurred during the 24-hour period ending at 9:00 p.m. on the date of the report. A report shall be made each day prior to 11:59 p.m. for each day the operator or dealer transacts business. If an operator or dealer is closed, or does not otherwise engage in any transactions on a particular day, a report indicating "no transactions" shall be filed for that day. Daily reports shall be filed electronically by posting a law enforcement web site designated by the sheriff. When technological problems prevent posting the daily report electronically, a printed, typed or legibly handwritten report shall be delivered to the sheriff's department in lieu thereof. 
(b)  This section shall not apply to the receipt of used books or pawn transactions commonly known as "title pawn" transactions where the pawnbroker takes possession of a motor vehicle certificate of title; takes a security interest in the motor vehicle certificate of title, and retains physical possession of the vehicle certificate of title for the entire length of the pawn transaction. 
(Ord. of 4-9-2015; Amd. of 2-4-2016) 
Sec. 26-100. - Hold period; sheriff holds. 
(a)  Any pawnbroker, pawnshop, in precious metals and gems, or person operating under a license granted pursuant to this chapter who takes good or pawn or who buys goods, taking full title thereto, shall hold the goods so taken in pawn for at least 30 days before disposing of the goods by sale, transfer, shipment or otherwise. 
(b)  The county sheriff's department, or any other law enforcement agency, has the authority to place property that is the subject of the sheriff's department or law enforcement investigation on "sheriffs hold". In that event, the county sheriff's department, or other law enforcement agency, shall notify the pawnbroker, pawnshop, or dealer in precious metals and gems of the need for a "sheriff or other law enforcement hold" and identify all property subject to the "said hold". Upon notification, it shall be the responsibility of the pawnbroker, pawnshop, or dealer in precious metals and gems to maintain the subject property until such time as the property is released from "sheriff or other law enforcement hold" status or the property is confiscated as evidence. 
(Ord. of 4-9-2015; Amd. of 2-4-2016) 
Sec. 26-101. - Unlawful acts. 
It shall be unlawful for pawnbroker, pawnshop, dealer in precious metals and gems or person operating under a license granted pursuant to this chapter to commit any of the following acts: 
Fail to make an entry of any material matter in the daily record of said business; Make any false: 
(1)  Entry in the daily record of said business; 
(2)  Falsify, obliterate or destroy the daily record of said business or remove the daily record from the place of business; 
(3)  Refusal to allow the county sheriff's department or duly authorized law enforcement officer to inspect the daily record of said business or any goods in the possession of said business during the ordinary hours of business or at any reasonable time; 
(4)  Fail to comply with this article as amended in any other material way; or 
(5)  Fail to comply with the ordinance of November 14, 1995, not otherwise amended as herein set out. 
(Ord. of 4-9-2015; Amd. of 2-4-2016) 
Sec. 26-102. - Enforcement. 
The county sheriff, the deputies thereof, constables, and all other law enforcement officers shall be authorized to issue citations to violators of any provision of this article, as amended. Such citations shall state the time and place at which the accused is to appear for trial, shall identify the offense with which the accused is charged, shall have an identifying number by which it shall be filed with the county magistrate court, shall indicate the identity of the accused and the date of service, shall be signed by the officer who completes and serves it. 
(Ord. of 4-9-2015; Amd. of 2-4-2016) 
Sec. 26-103. - Penalty. 
(a)  Any person violating this article, as amended or any provision hereof upon conviction, shall be punished as follows: By a fine of not more than $1,000.00 or imprisonment in the county jail for up to 60 days, or both. 
(b)  No person accused of violating this article shall be arrested prior to trial, but any person who fails to appear for trial shall be arrested thereafter on the warrant of the Magistrate Court of Brantley County and required to post a bond for his future appearance. 
(Ord. of 4-9-2015; Amd. of 2-4-2016) 
Sec. 26-104. - Court proceedings. 
(a)  Violations of this article shall be tried upon citation as described in section 26-102 of this amended article and may be tried with or without a prosecuting attorney as well as upon accusations. The county attorney shall serve as prosecuting attorney. 
(b)  Violations of this article shall be tried in the Magistrate Court of Brantley County, and shall be tried in accordance with the O.C.G.A., Chapter 15-10. 
(c)  Each violation of this article shall constitute a separate offense. 
(Ord. of 4-9-2015; Amd. of 2-4-2016) 
Secs. 26-105—26-130. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - SHOOTING GALLERIES AND FIREARM RANGES[4] 

Footnotes: 
--- (4) --- 
State Law reference— Discharge of firearm near public highway or street, O.C.G.A. § 16-11-103; discharge of firearm on property of another, O.C.G.A. § 16-11-104; Georgia Firearms and Weapons Act, O.C.G.A. § 16-11-120 et seq. 

Sec. 26-131. - Findings. 
(a)  The board of commissioners, based on common knowledge, investigation, and experience derived from other local government jurisdictions, believes that shooting galleries and firearm range establishments as defined in this article, if unregulated, would likely have an adverse impact upon adjacent property and the health, safety and welfare of the citizens of the county. 
(b)  The county's law enforcement resources available for responding to problems generally associated with unregulated shooting galleries and firearm ranges are limited and are best conserved by regulating such operations. 
(c)  The protection of the public's health, safety, welfare and property interest require that shooting galleries and/or firearm range establishments, their locations and operations be regulated in order to reduce the potential for harm, and preserve the quality of life in residential and business areas of the community. 
(d)  It is the duty of the board of commissioners to preserve the public health, safety, and welfare of the county, its residents, and the character of its neighborhoods and developments. 
(e)  The laws of the state authorize a county governing authority to adopt rules and regulations for the protection of the health, safety, welfare and property of its citizens, and O.C.G.A. § 48-13-9 authorizes a local government to require a regulated business to pay a regulatory fee. 
(Ord. of 8-17-1999) 
Sec. 26-132. - Purpose. 
The purpose of this article is to regulate certain types of businesses to the end that the adverse effect on the public health, safety, and welfare of the county, and on its citizens and property, and on the character of its neighborhoods and development will be curtailed, and to impose a regulatory fee on such regulated businesses. This article is intended to represent a balancing of competing interests for the protection of people and property through the regulation of shooting galleries and firearm ranges versus any legally protected rights of such operations and its patrons. This article is not intended to allow or license any business, establishment, or activity which would otherwise be unlawful. 
(Ord. of 8-17-1999, § 1) 
Sec. 26-133. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms, and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Chairman means the chairman of the board of commissioners. 
Church means a place where persons regularly assemble for religious worship. 
Conviction means an adjudication of guilty, plea of guilty, plea of nolo contendere or the forfeiture of a bond when charged with a crime, but shall not include a discharge under provisions of what is commonly called the state First Offender Act (O.C.G.A. § 42-8-60 et seq.). 
Distance and measurement mean the measurement in lineal feet from any part of the proposed premises of a shooting gallery or firearm range establishment to the nearest property line of any church, library, school, college, public park, residence, or hospital. A radius shall be measured from the property line of the proposed premises of such establishment to the nearest church, library, school, college, public park, residence or hospital, to include any parking lot, garage or outbuilding associated with such premises. 
Employee means any person engaged to provide or in fact providing services for a shooting gallery or firearm range to patrons whether for legal consideration or otherwise. 
Firearm means any legally possessed hand held weapon from which a shot or bullet is expelled (fired) by explosive force, i.e., a rifle, pistol or shotgun. 
Good moral character. A person is of good moral character according to this article if such person has not been convicted of a felony, any crime not a felony if it involves moral turpitude, or a drug-related, alcohol-related, or sex-related crime in the past ten years. 
Minor for the purposes of this article means any person who has not attained the age of 18 years. 
Park means any lands or facility owned, operated, controlled or managed by a county, city, state or federal government or any governmental entity or agency in and upon which recreational activities or places are provided for the recreation and enjoyment of the general public. 
Residence means a house, apartment, mobile home, boardinghouse or roominghouse, duplex, or other multifamily housing, presently being used or that is regularly occupied by or used for human dwelling. 
School means any state, county, city, church or other schools, public or private, that teach the subjects commonly taught in the common schools of this state, and vocational schools, colleges, post high school learning centers, kindergartens and day care centers for persons of all ages. 
Shooting gallery and firearm range mean an area or business establishment designated and operated by a person for the sport shooting of firearms at a designated target or otherwise for the payment of a fee, membership, contribution, or dues or by invitation of an authorized person, or any area so designated regardless of the terms of admission thereto. 
(Ord. of 8-17-1999, § 2) 
Cross reference— Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 26-134. - Regulations. 
The following regulations apply to all shooting galleries and/or firearm ranges as described in this article and located within the unincorporated areas of the county: 
(1)  It shall be unlawful for a licensee to employ minors or any person that is not of good moral character in a licensed premises. 
(2)  It shall be unlawful for a licensee to admit or permit the admission of any person under the age of 14 years within a licensed premises. 
(3)  No shooting gallery or firearm range establishment shall be located within the following distances as defined and measured: 
a.  Within 1,000 feet of any single-family or multifamily residence or within 1,000 feet of any parcel of land which may be zoned for single-family or multifamily uses or purposes; 
b.  Within 1,000 feet of a church, school, governmentally owned or operated building, library, civic center, public park, hospital, nursing home or community club; 
c.  Within 1,000 feet of another shooting gallery or firearm range establishment; 
d.  Within 1,000 feet of an establishment selling alcoholic beverages. 
(4)  The minimum standards for the operation of a safe shooting gallery or firearm range approved, adopted or established by the National Rifle Association (NRA), as from time to time amended, are hereby established and set as the minimum requirements to be in place for the operation of a shooting gallery or firearm range in the unincorporated area of the county. No shooting gallery or firearm range establishment shall be granted a license that does not have in place and meet the minimum standards for such an operation. In addition to the minimum standards required for the operation of a shooting gallery or firearm range, the licensee must post conspicuously in the shooting area a list of shooter's safety rules for patrons to see, which must include the following rules: 
a.  No person shall have a loaded weapon anywhere about the firing range or premises, except at a clearly marked loading and firing area. 
b.  No person shall stand or sit about the premises with a loaded weapon in his possession unless actually in the designated firing zone. 
c.  There shall be no person under the age of 18 years on the premises without a parent, guardian or designated supervising person over the age of 21 years. 
d.  No person shall consume alcoholic beverages or illegal substances on the licensed premises and any person suspected of being under such influence shall not be permitted on the premises. 
(5)  No shooting gallery or firearm range establishment licensee shall employ or contract with any person to work or provide any services in such establishment who is a person not permitted for employment pursuant to this article. 
(6)  A shooting gallery and/or firearm range establishment shall be closed between 9:00 p.m. and 8:00 a.m. Monday through Saturday, and from 12:00 midnight through 11:59 a.m. and after 9:00 p.m. on Sundays. 
(7)  No licensee shall permit the use of alcoholic beverages of any kind to be sold, possessed or consumed in or on the premises, or permit anyone who appears to be under the influence such alcoholic beverages to come upon or remain on the premises. 
(8)  No licensee shall permit the use of any illegal drugs or illegally controlled substances of any kind to be allowed, permitted, used, possessed or sold in or on the premises, or permit anyone who appears to be under the influence of such drugs to come upon or remain on the premises. 
Notwithstanding subsections (1) and (2) of this section, a shooting gallery or firearm range establishment operating in an unincorporated area of the county on the date of the adoption of the ordinance from which this article was derived shall not be required to meet the distance requirements set forth in this section as the distance requirement pertains to such location for so long as the licensee holds a legally recognized and perfected property right to use and possess such location as of the date of filing of an application for a shooting gallery or firearm range license or renewal thereof, but only if such legal right as to such location was vested at the time of the adoption of the ordinance from which this article was derived and such vested legal right has continued without the necessity of act or consent to renew, continue or extend such applicant's property right by applicant or other party holding a superior legal property right in such location. 
(Ord. of 8-17-1999, § 3) 
Sec. 26-135. - License required. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to engage in, conduct or carry on, in or upon any premises within the unincorporated area of the county any shooting gallery or firearm range business or activity as defined in this article without a license to do so. No license so issued shall condone or make legal any activity thereunder if such activity is deemed illegal or unlawful under the laws of the state or the United States. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for any person to operate a shooting gallery or firearm range establishment unless such business shall have a currently valid license or shall have made proper application for renewal within the time required thereof under this article, which license shall not be under suspension or permanently or conditionally revoked. 
(Ord. of 8-17-1999, § 4, 5) 
Sec. 26-136. - Application for license. 
(a)  Any person desiring to obtain a license to operate, engage in, conduct or carry on a shooting gallery or firearm range establishment shall make application to the board of commissioners. Prior to submitting such application, a nonrefundable fee, established by resolution of the county, shall be paid to the clerk of the county to defray, in part, the cost of investigation and report required by this article. Such fee is hereby established in the amount of $150.00. 
(b)  The application for license does not authorize the engaging in, operation of, conduct of or carrying on of any shooting gallery or firearm range establishment. 
(c)  All licenses shall be a mere grant of privilege to carry on such business during the term of the license subject to all the terms and conditions imposed by this article and related laws, applicable provisions of this article and other ordinances and resolutions of the county relating to such business. 
(d)  All licenses shall have printed on the front these words: "This license is a mere privilege subject to be suspended and revoked under the provisions of the Ordinances of Brantley County." 
(e)  A separate license shall be required for each place of business. 
(f)  Where the applicant: 
(1)  Is a corporation, any license shall be applied for by and shall be issued to the corporation and either: 
a.  The majority shareholder; or 
b.  A person employed full time in a managing capacity by the corporation; 
(2)  Is a partnership, any license shall be applied for by and shall be issued to the partnership and either: 
a.  The managing general partner; or 
b.  A person employed full time in a managing capacity by the partnership; 
(3)  Is a sole proprietor, any license shall be applied for by and shall be issued to the sole proprietor if he is working full time in a managing capacity on the premises, and, if not, then to the sole proprietor and a person employed full time in a managing capacity by the sole proprietor. 
For purposes of this subsection, the term "managing capacity" means the president or chief executive officer or managing or general partner of a corporation or partnership, or a person who has responsibility for management of the operations at the location to be licensed and who is a full-time employee of the corporation, partnership, proprietor, or other ownership entity. 
(Ord. of 8-17-1999, § 6) 
Sec. 26-137. - Application contents; supporting documents. 
(a)  Application for a shooting gallery of firearm range establishment license shall be written and on forms supplied by the office of the board of commissioners. Such application shall state the name, address, social security number and date of birth of the applicant, and the nature and character of the business to be carried on. 
(b)  If the applicant is a corporation, the name of the corporation shall be set forth exactly as shown in its articles of incorporation or charter, together with the state and date of incorporation, the social security numbers of each of its current officers and directors as well as all stockholders holding more than five percent of the outstanding shares of the corporation. If the applicant is a partnership, whether general or limited, the applicant shall set forth the name, residence address, dates of birth and social security numbers of the partners. If one or more of the partners is a corporation, the provisions of this subsection pertaining to corporations shall apply. 
(1)  Address of the premises to be licensed. 
(2)  The name of the owner of the premises and, if leased, a copy of the lease agreement. 
(3)  A plat, filed in duplicate, by a registered land surveyor, licensed by the state, showing the location of the proposed premises is not inconsistent with the provisions contained in section 26-134(3) which provide that no shooting gallery or firearm range establishment shall be located within 1,000 feet of any residential premises, parcel of land which is zoned for multifamily or single-family uses or purposes; within 1,000 feet of any parcel of land upon which a church, school, governmental building simultaneously owned and occupied by such government, library, civic center, neighborhood public park or neighborhood playground is located; within 1,000 feet of any parcel upon which another establishment regulated or defined under this article is located; or within 1,000 feet of any establishment selling alcoholic beverages. 
(c)  Should the requirements of this article dictate that more than one individual and/or entity apply for a license issue to such applicants, then all such applicants shall, on such application, designate the name, address and telephone number of an individual resident of the county, to act as agent for applicants/licensees for the purpose of receiving communications and notices under this article. Proof of delivery to the agent shall be conclusive proof of receipt by a licensee of such notice, process or information. 
(d)  Each application must be complete in its entirety before being accepted by the county for filing and processing. 
(e)  All applicants for licenses as to any premises which is to be subsequently renovated or improved shall furnish in duplicate plans and renderings of the premises as it is to exist at the time of opening. The premises shall comply with all building, health and similar county codes, as well as meet the minimum standards for a shooting gallery or firearm range as set forth in the standards established by the National Rifle Association, and such standards, as they may be amended from time to time, are incorporated in this article by reference. 
(f)  Each application for a shooting gallery or firearm range establishment license shall be verified and acknowledged under oath to be true and correct by the following persons: 
(1)  The individual, if the applicant is an individual; 
(2)  The manager or general partner, if a partnership; 
(3)  The president of the corporation, if a corporation; 
(4)  The chief administrative official, if any other organization or association. 
(Ord. of 8-17-1999, § 7) 
Sec. 26-138. - Notice of intent to engage in business. 
(a)  All applicants for licenses for a shooting gallery or firearm range establishment shall give notice that application has been filed and of the purpose of making such application by publication of an advertisement once a week for two consecutive weeks prior to the date of consideration of the application by the board of commissioners in the newspaper in which legal advertisements are published. The first advertisement shall not appear more than 20 days prior to the date of such consideration. The advertisement shall be of type not smaller than ten point capital and lower case and shall be at least a two-inch column. The advertisement shall appear on the same days as legal advertisements are regularly published, but not among the published legal ads. 
(b)  The notice shall contain a particular description of the location of the proposed business, the name of the applicant, the date, time and place of hearing, and a statement that any legal objections to the issuance must be made at or prior to the time of hearing, and, if prior to the time of hearing, must be in writing and received by the office of the board of commissioners on or before the date and time of hearing. 
(c)  Applicants shall provide proof of such notice by providing the board of commissioners, at the time of the hearing on license issuance, the affidavit of the publisher of the newspaper in which such notice was published, which affidavit shall reflect the content of the notice and the dates of publishing. 
(d)  The applicant shall cause to be placed upon the location of the proposed business a sign stating the following: "The County Shooting Gallery or Firearm Range License Applied for. A hearing before the Board of Commissioners of Brantley County shall be held on the ____________ day of ____________ ____________ . All interested persons take notice." The sign shall be at least 18 inches by 24 inches in size and shall face toward all public streets, sidewalks or other public property which adjoins the location so as to be clearly visible by persons using such public area. The sign shall be posed on the property from the date of the first publication of the legal advertisement through the date of consideration by the board of commissioners. 
(Ord. of 8-17-1999, § 8) 
Sec. 26-139. - Application; investigation; issuance. 
The chairman of the board of commissioners or his designee shall have a reasonable time not to exceed 30 days to investigate the application for a shooting gallery or firearm range establishment. Upon completion of the investigation and after holding a public hearing, the board of commissioners shall issue the license if it is determined that: 
(1)  The application conforms in all respects to this article. 
(2)  The applicant has not made a material misrepresentation in this application. 
(3)  The applicant has fully cooperated in the investigation of his application. 
(4)  The applicant, if an individual, or any officers or directors or shareholders holding more than five percent of the outstanding shares of the corporation, if the applicant is a corporation, or any partners, including limited partners, if the applicant is a partnership, has not been convicted in a court of competent jurisdiction of any crime involving a firearm for which: 
a.  Less than two years have elapsed since the date of conviction or the date of release from confinement imposed for the conviction, whichever is the later date, if the conviction is of a misdemeanor offense; 
b.  Less than five years have elapsed since the date of conviction or the date of release from confinement for the conviction, whichever is the later date, if the conviction is a felony offense; 
c.  Less than five years have elapsed since the date of the last conviction or the date of release from confinement for the last conviction, whichever is the later date, if the convictions are of two or more misdemeanor offenses or combination of misdemeanor offenses occurring within any 24-month period. 
(5)  All buildings, structures, protective berms or other required protective structures, or location of such business, as proposed by applicant, comply with this article. 
(6)  The applicant is at least 21 years of age. 
(7)  On the date the business for which a license is required commences and thereafter, there will be a responsible person on the premises to act as manager at all times during which the business is open. 
(8)  Notwithstanding subsections (1)—(7) of this section, no license shall be issued to an applicant if within 12 months immediately preceding the filing of an application one or more of the following shall have occurred: 
a.  The same applicant for a license or renewal has been rejected for any location, if such rejection was based upon the applicant's failure to meet the terms of this article applicable to the applicant as opposed to rejection for reasons related to the location itself. 
b.  The location has been rejected for any applicant. 
c.  The applicant has withdrawn, without providential cause, an application at any time within seven days immediately preceding the time and date set for the hearing before the board of commissioners unless at least one year shall have expired from such withdrawal. The one year waiting period will not apply where the applicant shall apply for a new location which has not been rejected within the preceding 12 months, except if the applicant has had an application for another location rejected within the preceding 12 months because of lack of qualifications of the applicant. 
(9)  Notwithstanding subsections (1)—(8) of this section, no license shall be issued until an annual license fee, established by resolution of the board of commissioners and prorated on a calendar year basis, is paid to the county clerk. The annual license fee is hereby resolved to be $250.00 until otherwise set. 
(Ord. of 8-17-1999, § 9) 
Sec. 26-140. - License renewal. 
Licenses for a shooting gallery and/or firearm range establishment shall be renewed on a calendar year basis provided that the licensee continues to meet the requirements set out in this article. The renewal fee for the license shall be established by resolution of the board of commissioners. The renewal fee is hereby resolved to be $250.00. Renewal applications shall be submitted by November 15 of each year prior to January 1 of the year for which such license is requested. 
(Ord. of 8-17-1999, § 10) 
Sec. 26-141. - License nontransferable. 
No shooting gallery or firearm range establishment license may be sold, transferred or assigned by a licensee, or by operation of law, to any other person. Any such sale, transfer or assignment, or attempted sale, transfer or assignment, shall be deemed to constitute a voluntary surrender of such license and such license shall thereafter be null and void; provided and excepted, however, that if the licensee is a partnership or corporation, and one or more of the partners or shareholders, as the case may be, should die, one or more of the surviving partners or shareholders who were partners or shareholders at the time of issuance of the license may acquire, by purchase or otherwise, the interest of the deceased partner or shareholder without affecting a surrender or termination of such license and in such case, the licensee shall immediately notice the office of the board of commissioners. A shooting gallery or firearm range establishment license issued to a corporation shall be deemed terminated and void when either any outstanding stock of the corporation is sold, transferred or assigned after the issuance of a license, or any stock authorized but not issued at the time of the granting of a license pursuant to this article is thereafter issued and sold, transferred or assigned. 
(Ord. of 8-17-1999, § 11) 
Sec. 26-142. - Changes and modifications. 
(a)  Change of location. No licensee shall change the location of the shooting gallery or firearm range establishment without obtaining a new license. 
(b)  Change of name. No licensee shall advertise, operate, conduct, manage, engage in, or carry on any shooting gallery or firearm range establishment under any name other than his name and the name of the business as specified on his license. 
(c)  Modification of licensed premises. After issuance of any license, no change in the physical location of the shooting activity within the premises shall be made which would affect compliance with any distance or other requirement of this article. 
(Ord. of 8-17-1999, §§ 12—14) 
Sec. 26-143. - License; refusal. 
If the chairman of the board of commissioners or his designee, following investigation of the applicant for a shooting gallery or firearm range establishment license, deems that the applicant does not fulfill the requirements as set forth in this article, he shall notify the applicant of such decision in writing and the basis thereof. Any such decision shall be final unless appeal is filed to the board of commissioners by any aggrieved party on or before ten days of the date of the decision. A hearing by the board of commissioner of the appeal shall occur within 30 days of its filing at a regular or special meeting of the board. 
(Ord. of 8-17-1999, § 15) 
Sec. 26-144. - Suspension. 
The chairman of the board of commissioners may suspend a shooting gallery or firearm range establishment license for a period not to exceed 180 days if he determines that the licensee or an employee has violated any section of this article. If the chairman deems a license suspension appropriate, he shall notify the licensee of such decision in writing and the basis thereof. Such suspension shall take effect ten days following the licensee's notification thereof unless an appeal is filed with and to the board of commissioners by the aggrieved party on or before ten days of the date of receipt by the aggrieved party of the decision. A hearing by the board of commissioners of the appeal shall occur within 30 days of its filing in a regular or special meeting of the board. Enforcement of the suspension shall be stayed pending the board's ruling on the licensee's appeal. 
(Ord. of 8-17-1999, § 16) 
Sec. 26-145. - Revocation. 
(a)  Revocation for suspension. The chairman of the board of commissioners may revoke a license for a shooting gallery or firearm range establishment if a cause for suspension occurs and the license has been suspended within the past 12 months. 
(b)  Revocation for various determinations. The chairman may also revoke a license if he determines that: 
(1)  A licensee gave false or misleading information in the material submitted during the application process. 
(2)  A licensee or an employee knowingly operated the business during a period of time when the licensee's license was suspended. 
(3)  The owner or operator of the licensed establishment knowingly allowed a person under 14 years of age to enter the establishment. 
(4)  The owner or operator of the licensed establishment knowingly allows or permits a person under 18 years of age to work or perform services within the licensed establishment. 
(c)  Notification; hearing. If the chairman deems a license revocation appropriate, he shall so notify the licensee of such decision in writing and the basis thereof. Such revocation shall take effect ten days following the chairman's serving of his written decision upon the licensee unless an appeal is filed with and to the board of commissioners by the aggrieved party on or before ten days of the date of receipt by the aggrieved party of the decision of the chairman. A hearing by the board of commissioners on the decision shall occur within 30 days of its filing in a regular or special meeting of the board. Revocation shall continue for a one year period from the date revocation becomes effective. 
(d)  Appeal procedure. An applicant or licensee who has timely filed an appeal with the board of commissioners as allowed by this article shall be entitled to a hearing before the board of commissioners. At the time set for the hearing, the board of commissioners shall receive all relevant testimony in evidence from county staff or interested parties, and from the licensee or employee. In all hearings pursuant to this article, the following procedures shall apply: 
(1)  The chairman of the board of commissioners shall read or cause to be read the charges and specifications against the charged party. He shall then read or cause to be read any response filed by the charged party. 
(2)  The board of commissioners shall hear the evidence upon the charges and specifications as filed against the charged party and shall not consider any additional evidence beyond the scope of the charges and may exclude evidence which is purely cumulative. 
(3)  The order of proof shall be as follows: The county representative shall present his evidence in support of the charges; the charged party shall then present his evidence. Evidence of each party may be supported by submission of pertinent documents. Each party shall be allowed to present pertinent rebuttal evidence. 
(4)  The charged party and county may be represented by counsel, and may present, examine and cross examine witnesses. Additionally, the board of commissioners may interrogate all parties and witnesses to obtain necessary information. 
(e)  Removal of signs. Should any license be revoked or suspended, all signs indicating that such businesses conducted on the premises shall be removed from the premises during the period of revocation or suspension. 
(Ord. of 8-17-1999, § 17) 
Sec. 26-146. - Service of notice. 
(a)  Any notice required to be given under this article to any applicant, licensee or employee of a shooting gallery or firearm range establishment may be given either by personal delivery or by certified United States Postal Service, postage prepaid, return receipt requested, addressed to the most recent address as specified in the application for license/permit, or such updated address which may have subsequently been provided in writing to the county clerk. Notices mailed shall be deemed given on the second day subsequent to their deposit in the United States Postal Service. 
(b)  It shall be the duty of each applicant, licensee and employee to furnish notice to the county clerk in writing of any change of mailing address. 
(Ord. of 8-17-1999, § 18) 
Sec. 26-147. - Violations and penalties. 
(a)  Any person violating the sections of this article shall be punishable by fine not to exceed $1,000.00 per violation, or by imprisonment for a period not to exceed six months, or by both such fine and imprisonment. 
(b)  No person accused of violating this article shall be arrested prior to trial, but any person who fails to appear for trial shall be arrested thereafter on the warrant of the magistrate, and required to post bond for his future appearance. 
(c)  Violations of this article shall be tried upon citations which shall be issued to an alleged violator of any sections of this article. Such citation shall state the time and place at which the accused is to appear for trial, shall identify the offense with which the accused is charged, shall have an identifying number by which it shall be filed with the court, shall indicate the identity of the accused and the date of service, and shall be signed by the representative of the county who completes and serves it. The citation may be served by certified mail, return receipt requested. 
(d)  Citations issued under this article may be tried without a prosecuting attorney, however, in the event the prosecuting attorney is needed, the county attorney shall serve as the prosecuting attorney. 
(e)  Violations of this article shall be tried in the magistrate court of the county, and shall be tried in accordance with the O.C.G.A. § 15-10-60 et seq. 
(f)  Nothing in this article shall prevent the board of commissioners or any other aggrieved party from bringing any civil action for injunction, or other proceedings to present, correct, or abate any violation of this article or other state or federal law. No sanction, penalty or remedy prescribed herein shall be considered exclusive of any other remedy, but shall be available in addition to any other sanctions, penalty or remedy provided by law. 
(g)  Each violation of this article shall constitute a separate offense. 
(Ord. of 8-17-1999, § 19) 
Secs. 26-148—26-170. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - TIMBER OPERATIONS[5] 

Footnotes: 
--- (5) --- 
Editor's note— An ordinance adopted June 9, 2009, §§ I—VII, did not specify manner of inclusion; hence, codification as Art. V, §§ 26-171—26-176 was at the editor's discretion. 

Sec. 26-171. - Title. 
This article shall be known as the "Brantley County Timber Operations Ordinance." 
(Ord. of 6-9-2009, § I) 
Sec. 26-172. - Definitions. 
As used in this article, the terms: 
(1)  Board means the Board of Commissioners of Brantley County, or their successors in office, being the governing authority of Brantley County. 
(2)  County means the unincorporated area of Brantley County, Georgia. 
(3)  Timber means pine, cypress and hardwood trees and trees of every size, species and description. Also, for purposes of this article, "timber" includes such trees after harvesting and while being transported as logs or in shorter lengths. 
(4)  Timber operations means purchasing and/or cutting and harvesting timber in Brantley County, or transporting such timber from the site at which it was cut; or the moving of equipment to and from the site of such cutting. 
(5)  Timber operator means any person, firm or corporation engaged in commercial timber operations, whether engaged in one or all of said activities described in subsection (4) above. It shall not include persons cutting or transporting timber solely for noncommercial personal use or firewood. 
(Ord. of 6-9-2009, § II) 
Sec. 26-173. - Permit. 
(a)  Permit required. No timber operator shall engage in the timber operations in the unincorporated area of Brantley County without first obtaining a permit to conduct such operations as provided herein; provided, however, employees of a timber operator shall not be required to obtain separate permits for activities within the scope of such employment if their employer has obtained a valid permit for such activities; and provided further, that an independent contractor transporting timber for another timber operator shall not be required to obtain a separate permit if the timber operator for whom he is transporting timber has obtained a valid permit for such timber operations at the same location. 
(b)  Place of filing. The application for permit shall be signed by the applicant and filed with the Office of the Board of Tax Assessors for Brantley County, and forms shall be available at such office. The chief appraiser or his designee at said office of the Brantley County Tax Assessor shall review the application and issue the permit if all required information is provided. Completed application forms may be faxed or e-mailed to said office, and if the applicant provides his fax number, the permit may be faxed back to the applicant. 
(c)  Application for permit. The application for permit shall be in the form prescribed by the board of commissioners from time to time and shall contain the following information: 
(1)  The name, address and telephone number of the applicant, timber operator or timber purchaser. 
(2)  If the applicant or timber operator intends to engage another or other contractor(s) to harvest or transport the timer, the application shall also include the name, address and telephone number of each such contractor or harvester. 
(3)  The name, address and telephone number of the owner of the real property on which the applicant/purchaser/timber operator will perform the timber operations. 
(4)  The location of the real property on which the applicant/purchaser/timber operator will engage in timber operations (to include the tax map and the parcel number). 
(5)  The roads in Brantley County upon which motor vehicles will travel in transporting such timber and in transporting the equipment to be used in the timber operations. 
(6)  The dates cutting operations are expected to commence and end. 
(d)  Incomplete applications. Incomplete applications will not be accepted and will be returned to the applicant. 
(e)  Other laws. In addition to the provisions of this article, the applicant for a permit shall comply with all state and federal regulations pertaining to its timber operations, including payment of all applicable ad valorem tax on the timber. 
(f)  Cost. No fee shall be charged for filing the application or issuing the permit. 
(g)  Separate applications. Applicants must file a separate application and receive a separate permit for each timber cutting operation and each separate landowner. 
(Ord. of 6-9-2009, § III) 
Sec. 26-174. - Notice to timber operators. 
The county board of tax assessors shall mail or deliver a copy of this article to all timber operators and other persons whom the board has knowledge of or can identify as persons or businesses which cut, harvest or transport trees or timber on or from lands in Brantley County. A notice as to the adoption of this article shall be published in the newspaper for two weeks and made known to as many persons as possible dealing with timber in this county. 
(Ord. of 6-9-2009, § V) 
Sec. 26-175. - Application/permit numbers. 
Each application filed shall be assigned a number consisting of the year and quarter of year of filing, followed by a number representing the order in which that application was filed in that year. (For example: The first application filed in the first quarter of 2009 would have a number of "2009-1-1"). 
The permit number will be the same number as the application number. 
(Ord. of 6-9-2009, § VI) 
Editor's note— The permit application referenced above has not been set out, but may be reviewed at the county offices. 
Sec. 26-176. - Violations; penalties. 
Any timber operator who shall willfully fail to comply with this article shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. The violation of the article shall be tried in the Magistrate Court of Brantley County, Georgia, and upon conviction, the timber operator shall be punished by fine not to exceed $1,000.00. Each day the violation continues shall constitute a separate offense. 
(Ord. of 6-9-2009, § VII) 
Secs. 26-177—26-200. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VI. - JUNKYARDS[6] 

Footnotes: 
--- (6) --- 
Editor's note— An ordinance adopted June 8, 2010, §§ 1—9, 11, did not specify manner of inclusion; hence, codification as Art. VI, §§ 26-201—26-210 was at the discretion of the editor. 

Sec. 26-201. - Title. 
This article shall be known as the "Brantley County Junkyard Ordinance" and is hereby enacted by the board of commissioners. 
(Ord. of 6-8-2010, § 1) 
Sec. 26-202. - Purpose. 
This article prescribes rules and regulations relating to the exercise of effective control of junkyards in the unincorporated areas of Brantley County, Georgia, adjacent to or within 1,000 feet of a residential area, church or public school, or located on primary residential roads or streets. 
(Ord. of 6-8-2010, § 2) 
Sec. 26-203. - Definitions. 
The following terms as used in this article, shall have the following meaning unless the context requires otherwise: 
Automobile graveyard means any establishment which is maintained or used for storing, buying, or selling wrecked, scrapped, ruined or dismantled motor vehicles or motor vehicle parts. 
Board of commissioners shall mean the Brantley County Board of Commissioners. 
County road means any road, street or highway which is a portion of a county road or secondary state road system. 
Establish means to construct, build, raise, assemble, place, affix, create or in any way bring into existence. 
Junk means old or scrap copper, brass, batteries, paper, trash, rubber, debris, waste; junked, dismantled, or wrecked automobiles, or parts thereof; or iron, steel, and other old scrap ferrous or nonferrous material. 
Junkyard means any establishment which is maintained or used for storing, buying, or selling junk or for an automobile graveyard; and the term shall include scrap processing establishments. 
Maintain means to allow to exist. 
Nonconforming junkyard means any junkyard which was lawfully established and in existence for ____________ ( ____________ ) years, holds a valid Brantley County Business License and any part of junkyard located within 1,000 feet of any residence, church or public school, except: 
(1)  Those which are screened by natural objects, plantings, fences, or other appropriate means so as not to be visible to a residence, church or public school or otherwise removed from sight; and 
(2)  Those located within an unzoned industrial area, which area shall be determined from actual land use as defined by the board of commissioners; and 
(3)  Those not visible from the main traveled way of well traveled county roads or from secondary state highways; and 
(4)  Those not located within close proximity to an established residential subdivision, and does not use residential roads or streets to access their property. 
Person means any individual, firm, agency, company, association, partnership, business trust, joint stock company, body politic or corporation. 
Screening means the use of any vegetative planting, fencing, ornamental wall of masonry, or other architectural treatment or device, earthen embankment, or a combination of any of these which will effectively hide from view any deposit of junk from a residence, church or public school, within a distance of 1,000 feet, on a yearround basis. Screening does not include the use of junk. 
Unlawful junkyards means any junkyard which comes into existence after the adoption of this article. 
(1)  Which is located within 1,000 feet of the nearest residence, church or public school and is not screened by natural objects, plantings, fences, or other appropriate means so as to be visible from the residence, church or public school; or 
(2)  Is located within an unzoned industrial area of the unincorporated area of the county; and 
(3)  Is visible from the well-traveled county roads or secondary state highways in the unincorporated area of the county; and 
(4)  Is located on a primarily residential road in the unincorporated area of the county. 
Visible means capable of being seen without visual or optical aid by a person of normal visual acuity. 
Zone of control means all areas within the boundaries of this county which are adjacent to and within 1,000 feet a residential area, church or public school within Brantley County. 
(Ord. of 6-8-2010, § 3; Amd. of 4-7-2016) 
Sec. 26-204. - Policy. 
In carrying out the purpose of this article: 
(1)  Every effort shall be made to screen nonconforming junkyards which are to be continued as on-going businesses. 
(2)  Nonconforming junkyards are to be relocated only as a last resort. 
(Ord. of 6-8-2010, § 4) 
Sec. 26-205. - Measurement of distance. 
Distance from the edge of a residential property, church or public school line shall be measured horizontally along a straight line. 
(Ord. of 6-8-2010, § 5) 
Sec. 26-206. - Screening. 
(a)  Responsibility for screening. 
(1)  Any junkyard lawfully in existence [on] effective date of this article, which is within 1,000 feet of the nearest residence, church or public school. 
(2)  Junkyards established subsequent to adoption of this article by Brantley County Board of Commissioners in non-industrial areas within 100 feet of a residence, church or public school must provide for adequate screening located between the junkyard and residences, churches or public schools and at the expense of the person owning the junkyard. Screening provided by such owner must be in compliance with this article and of a type approved by the board of commissioners. Those junkyards which are established subsequent to the adoption of this article and located within zones of control and which cannot be adequately screened shall be relocated at the owner's expense. 
(b)  Every effort shall be made to screen nonconforming junkyards where they are to be continued as on-going businesses. Screening may be accomplished by use of natural objects, landscaping, plantings, fences, and other appropriate means, including relocating inventory on site to utilize an existing natural screen or a screenable portion of the site. 
(c)  Where screening is used, it must, upon completion of the screening project, effectively screen the junkyard from the residential areas, churches or public schools on a yearround basis, and be compatible with the surroundings. 
(Ord. of 6-8-2010, § 6) 
Sec. 26-207. - Nonconforming junkyards. 
For the purposes of this article, a discontinued junkyard is any junkyard which was operated as a business enterprise in the past and where the proprietor is retaining the inventory for the present but not actively engaged in buying or selling junk. 
(1)  The nonconforming junkyard may continue as long as it is not extended, or changed in use. Once a junkyard has been made conforming, the subsequent placement of junk so that it may be seen, above or beyond a screen, or if the junk otherwise becomes visible, said junkyard shall then be treated the same as the establishment of a new junkyard. 
(2)  A nonconforming junkyard must have been in lawful existence and operation on adoption of this article, and may continue to exist and operate (1) as long as it continues to be lawfully maintained, (2) is not extended or enlarged, (3) is not substantially changed in use, or (4) is not located on a primary residential street or road. 
(3)  In order for a junkyard to continue as a nonconforming junkyard, there must be existing property rights in the junkyard and junk affected by this article. A junkyard may not continue to exist if it has been abandoned, destroyed, or voluntarily discontinued. Brantley County shall consider the following criteria as the minimum criteria which must exist and must be applied before any determination can be made by the board of commissioners that a junkyard or junk has been abandoned: 
a.  The junkyard has not operated or conducted business for one year or more; or 
b.  The junkyard is in need of substantial repair or maintenance; or 
c.  The junkyard owner cannot be found or determined after a diligent search has been made by a building inspector as verified by his affidavit which shall set forth all the steps taken and attempts made to locate and determine said owner. 
(Ord. of 6-8-2010, § 7) 
Sec. 26-208. - Unlawful junkyards. 
The Brantley County Code Enforcement Department, through its designated representatives shall inspect junkyards periodically to insure that they are being operated in accordance with the applicable laws, rules and regulations pertaining to junkyard control, and shall require that all screening materials be maintained in such a manner as to accomplish the objective of this article. If the inspection discloses that a junkyard is being operated in violation of this article, the owner shall be informed in writing, sent by registered mail, stating the violation and instructing him to make the corrections within 60 days from the date of the letter. 
(Ord. of 6-8-2010, § 8) 
Sec. 26-209. - Screening criteria. 
(a)  [Plan for screening.] Plan for screening of junkyards established after the adoption of this article. 
(1)  The screening shall be located on the owner's land and not on any part of the public land. 
(2)  The screen shall be in place prior to the time the junk is deposited. 
(3)  At no time after the screen is established shall the junk be stacked high enough to be visible above the screen. No junk shall be placed outside of the screened areas. 
(4)  Fences must be located in such a manner as to not be hazardous to the traveling public. 
(5)  The construction of fences shall be uniform and no patchwork type of construction shall be permitted. 
(6)  When fences are painted, the paint used shall be of a color so as to blend into the environs of the area. 
(b)  Acceptable fencing materials. Acceptable fencing shall include fences of steel or other metals, durable woods such as heart cypress, redwood, or other wood treated with a preservative, or walls of masonry. Some of the types acceptable are: 
(1)  Chain link type with aluminum, steel, plastic, or wooden slat inserts. 
(2)  Wooden types of basket weave, palisade, louver, or other suitable design. 
(3)  Walls of masonry including plain or ornamental concrete block, block, brick, stone, or other suitable masonry material. 
(4)  An earth wall, if properly designed, grassed, and landscaped. 
Note: The above types of fencing and walls appearing in subparagraphs (b)(1), (2), (3), and (4) above are given for examples only. Any other design of fencing constructed of other materials may be submitted to the board of commissioners for consideration. 
(c)  Plant material. 
(1)  All plant material shall be predominantly evergreen and approved by the board of commissioners. 
(2)  The minimum size of plant material at the time of planting shall be as follows: 
a.  Large trees deciduous: 1″—1½″ caliper (Maples, Sycamore, Sweetgum). 
b.  Small trees: 4′—5′ in height (Hawthorn, Crepe Myrtle, etc.). 
c.  Evergreen trees: 4′—5′ in height (Pinus, Magnolia, etc.). 
d.  Evergreen shrubs: 2½′—3′ in height (including Elaeaqnus, Abelia, etc.). 
(d)  Maintenance. The owner or owners of any junkyard shall maintain the screening established initially, doing such painting and repairs to keep any fences, walls or other structural material in good appearance. Plant material shall be watered, cultivated, or mulched, and given any required maintenance including spraying for insect control, to keep the planting in a good healthy condition. Dead or destroyed plant material will be removed immediately and shall be replaced during the next spring or fall planting season. 
The replacement plants shall be at least as large as the initial planting. 
(e)  Junkyards screened. The owner or owners of any junkyard lawfully in existence on the adoption of this article, and which has been screened from view may not extend the deposit of junk beyond such screening so as to be visible from the main traveled way of the highway or a residence, church or public school. Any such extension shall be screened by the owner at his own expense and such screening shall be subject to these rules and regulations. Piling of junk above planned height of screening established by the department is prohibited. 
(Ord. of 6-8-2010, § 9) 
Sec. 26-210. - Violations and penalties. 
(a)  Any person, firm, corporation or agent who shall violate a provision of this article, or failure to comply therewith, or with any requirements thereof, shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. Each such person shall be considered guilty of a separate offense for each and every day or portion thereof during which any violation of any of the provisions of the junkyard article is committed or is continued. 
(b)  Any violation of this article shall be governed by O.C.G.A. § 15-10-62 and O.C.G.A. § 15-10-63. The Brantley County Building Inspector may file accusations pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 15-10-62 upon the approval of such actions by the chairman of the Brantley County Board of Commissioners. 
(Ord. of 6-8-2010, § 11) 
Secs. 26-211—26-219. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VII. - SPECIAL EVENTS 

Sec. 26-220. - Required. 
Except as otherwise provided in this article, a special events permit shall be required for the activities of this article. A "special event" is defined for purposes of this chapter as any organized activity involving 150 or more participants having as its purpose entertainment, recreation, charitable promotion or fundraiser, recreation and/or education, such as a festival or celebration, foot or vehicle race, parade or march, rally or assembly which takes place on a public road, street, sidewalk or right-of-way, or occurs on private property.
