ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 66-1. - Road abandonment guidelines. 
(a)  Application. Application for county road or easement closing/abandonment shall be made to the county clerk on an application provided by Brantley County. The applicant shall outline the nature of the request and specify the anticipated follow-on use of the road or easement for which the request is made. The applicant shall provide a plat that shows the road or easement for which the application is being filed. The plat shall be prepared by a land surveyor registered by the State of Georgia. 
(b)  Review. The county clerk will coordinate the review of the request with the county manager, county attorney and the road department. 
If the county manager determines that the application does not meet the criteria for abandonment because the road in question still has substantial useful purpose, the process will stop. The county manager will notify the applicant of the decision in writing within ten days. The applicant may appeal the county manager's decision to the board of commissioners by filing a written notice of such appeal with the county manager within ten days of the date of his decision. The board of commissioners may either uphold the manager's decision or direct him to proceed with a public hearing. The applicant shall be notified in writing of the decision by the county manager within ten days. 
If the county manager finds that the application meets the criteria of these guidelines, an advertisement will be sent to the official organ of the county, once a week for two weeks, advising that a public hearing will be held to determine whether the proposed abandonment has "ceased to be used by the public or no longer serves any useful public purpose". The county clerk will notify, by return receipt requested mail, all effected property owners who own property adjacent to the proposed road to be abandoned, of the public hearing. 
(c)  Determination by the county commission. If the board of commissioners approves the abandonment, the county attorney will prepare a deed and file it for recording with the clerk of superior court if the identity of the grantee for such a deed is clear. The submitted plat may require a revision if the board of commissioners places conditions on the approved abandonment. The applicant will bear the cost of any required plat modifications. Only after the deed recording by the county attorney is the action final. The original deed (if any) will be mailed to the applicant(s) by the county clerk. 
No application for abandonment may be made, or considered, if any portion of the property sought to be abandoned has been the subject of an abandonment application filed, or considered by the Brantley County Board of Commissioners, within the immediate preceding two years. 
(d)  Fee. Any request submitted under this provision shall be accompanied by a $350.00 cashier's check, a non-refundable application fee. The applicant may withdraw the application or request a postponement of the hearing date once, by submitting a written request, at least seven calendar days prior to the date set for the public hearing. If a postponement is requested, the applicant will bear the additional administrative charges (advertising and administrative costs). 
(Ord. of 7-13-2010) 
Editor's note— An ordinance adopted July 13, 2010, did not specify manner of inclusion; hence codification as § 66-1 was at the discretion of the editor. 
Secs. 66-2—66-30. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - ROAD ACCEPTANCE STANDARDS[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
Editor's note— Amend. of 2-23-2006, arts. 1—10 amended art. II its entirety to read as herein set out. Former art. II, §§ 66-31—66-33, pertained to similar subject matter, and derived from Res. of 3-12-2002, §§ 1—3, Amend. of 8-13-2002 and Ord. of 1-27-2004. 
State Law reference— Regulation of maintenance and use of public roads generally, O.C.G.A. § 32-6-1 et seq. 

Sec. 66-31. - Acceptance of roads by the county. 
(a)  The county will only accept a street/road that is/are within a subdivision development or a new road created to a subdivision development that are designed and created to the standards as set forth in this article, and paved to the standards of a residential subdivision as established by the Georgia Department of Transportation at the time the county is requested to accept said street/road as a part of the county's road system. Provided, however, a road to a subdivision development will not be considered a new road and within the provisions of this article if the principle portion of the road existed prior to the subdivision development which adjoins said road, should the county consent to or authorize a limited or minimal shifting or realignment of said road or the right-of-way thereof. 
(b)  The county will only accept an unpaved road/street that has been constructed in compliance with the design standards for an unpaved road/street as set forth in this article. 
(Amend. of 2-23-2006, art. 1) 
Sec. 66-32. - Definition of a subdivision development. 
A subdivision as referred to in this article shall be the division of a parcel of land into two or more parcels of land or building sites. 
(Amend. of 2-23-2006, art. 2) 
Sec. 66-33. - Road/street right-of-way title transfer. 
(a)  The county will only accept the transfer/conveyance of ownership of the right-of-way for a new road/street by means of a warranty deed that names Brantley County, Georgia, as the grantee and properly describes the subject right-of-way of a road/street; and when the party desiring to transfer/convey the ownership of said right-of-way provides the county with a title opinion from an attorney licensed to practice law in the state, which states: i) that the offering party has good and marketable title to the said right-of-way property, ii) that all taxes have been paid on the property to the current year, and iii) that there are no liens, encumbrances, easements or leases affecting the subject property. 
(b)  In addition, any road or street for which acceptance by the county is sought, must be shown and delineated on a plat of survey prepared by a state registered land surveyor, and the plat must also have the following certification thereon signed and stamped by a state professional engineer, to-wit: 
Certification 
It is hereby certified that the public road/street infrastructure dedicated to Brantley County, Georgia, as shown and delineated on this plat was constructed in accordance with a design prepared by the undersigned following the principles and practices of sound engineering and for compliance with the road/street standards established by Brantley County; and that all road/street infrastructure shown hereon actually exist, unless clearly marked on the plat as "Future", and that the materials used in the construction of said road/street conform to the current Georgia Department of Transportation material specifications; and that all engineering and all permitting requirements of Brantley County and/or the State of Georgia have been complied with. 
This the ____________ day of ____________ , ____________ . 
;ul=_;;daterule; 
;ul=_;  Georgia P.E. No.: ____________ 
(c)  No deed to the county for the conveyance of road right-of-way shall be considered accepted by the county, and recorded among the deed records of the county by the clerk of court unless the deed has inscribed on the face thereof the following: "The road right-of-way described in this indenture was accepted by Brantley County, Georgia, by action of the board of commissioners in a meeting held on ____________ (date of the meeting)"; with the signature of the clerk of the board of commissioners being placed immediately below the aforestated acceptance statement. 
(Amend. of 2-23-2006, art. 3; Amend. of 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 66-34. - Continuance of existing street pattern. 
The arrangement of roads/streets in a subdivision development should provide for the alignment with, or the continuation of, or the appropriate projection of existing streets in the surrounding areas as shown on the county road map. All new roads/streets must be named in accordance with the Brantley County Addressing Ordinance. All road name signs and stop signs must be purchased by the party offering the right-of-way to the county and in place before a new road/street shall be made a part of the county's road system. 
(Amend. of 2-23-2006, art. 4) 
Sec. 66-35. - Minimum right-of-way requirements. 
(a)  The right-of-way for all new unpaved roads shall be a minimum of 80 feet, 40 feet right and left of the roadbed centerline; except a minor road shown not to have the potential to be upgraded to a collector road may have a minimum of 60 feet right-of-way, 30 feet right and left of the roadbed centerline. 
(b)  The right-of-way for any road/street in a subdivision development or required to be paved before same will be accepted by the county, shall have a minimum of 60-foot right-of-way, 30 feet right and left of the roadbed centerline. 
(Amend. of 2-23-2006, art. 5) 
Sec. 66-36. - Cul-de-sac requirements. 
Culs-de-sac, shall follow these minimum standards: 
(1)  A vehicular turnaround at the closed end of the road/street shall have an outside radius of: not less than 40 feet on a paved street and not less than 50 feet on a dirt street. 
(2)  A vehicular turnaround at the closed end of the road/street shall have an inside radius of: not less than 12 feet and not greater than 28 feet on a paved road. 
(3)  A vehicular turnaround at the closed end of the road/street shall have a right-of-way radius of not less than 55 feet with a roadside ditch that is less than one foot in depth, 60 feet with a one to two foot deep roadside ditch, 65 feet with a two to three foot deep roadside ditch and if there is a ditch of three feet or greater in depth the right-of-way radius is to be determined by the county road superintendent. 
(4)  Exception: Culs-de-sac designed with traffic islands shall have a maximum inside pavement radius of 36 feet and a minimum outside pavement radius of 50 feet. In no case shall the travel lane around the traffic island be less than 14 feet in width. The right-of-way radius shall be a minimum of 60 feet. 
(5)  Temporary dead-end streets: Temporary dead-end streets, which are stub streets designed to provide future access to proposed developments, require temporary easements for a turnaround of the nature described under culs-de-sac. 
(Amend. of 2-23-2006, art. 6) 
Sec. 66-37. - Design standards for unpaved street/road. 
All unpaved streets/roads shall be designed and constructed in accordance with the following minimum specifications and standards: 
(1)  Minimum right-of-way required where roadside ditches are required shall be 80 feet, 40 feet right and left of the roadbed centerline. 
(2)  Roadbed width shall be a minimum of 30 feet, 15 feet right and left of the centerline with a minimum crown of six inches to centerline. Travel lanes shall have a minimum width of 22 feet, 11 feet right and left of the centerline with grassed shoulders with a maximum ratio of 6:1. Roadside ditches shall have a flat bottom with a minimum width of four feet. All back slopes where required will consist of a minimum slope ratio of 3:1. 
(3)  The top six inches of all travel lanes shall be compacted to a minimum 95 percent standard proctor density. The developer at the request of the county shall supply test reports. Also stabilization requirements of travel lanes shall be based on the county road superintendent's recommendation as to the type and amount. The recommendation shall be based on considering the type of soils, drainage, estimated traffic volumes and types and surrounding topography. 
(4)  Test for compaction shall be located no more than 500 feet apart and staggered to right and left and on centerline. 
(Amend. of 2-23-2006, art. 7) 
Sec. 66-38. - Drainage plans and requirement for subdivision developments. 
Curbs, inlets, swales, ditches, pipes, etc., shall be engineered and constructed as required to accommodate stormwater run-off quantities. The development engineer shall submit calculations and elevations, which support the proposed improvements to the county road superintendent for his approval. Material requirements for pipe culverts shall be: 
(1)  Reinforced concrete pipes or high-density polyethylene (HDPE) shall be required for all culverts. The use of HDPE shall require a minimum of one and one-half foot of cover. 
(2)  No metal culverts shall be allowed. 
(3)  The minimum diameter for pipe culverts shall be 15 inches. 
(4)  All material shall conform to the current Georgia Department of Transportation material specifications. 
(Amend. of 2-23-2006, art. 8) 
Sec. 66-39. - Culverts to be located for drainage along an unpaved road/streets. 
All culverts to be installed for drainage or to access property from an unpaved road/street that is to be a part of the county's road systems must be installed in compliance with the county's ordinance that requires the installation of property access culverts. 
(Amend. of 2-23-2006, art. 9) 
Sec. 66-40. - Requirement for any new road/street or property access driveway that joins a state highway. 
The Georgia Department of Transportation (GDOT) must approve all access roads or drives for property joining a state highway. The applicant/developer must comply with all requirements of the GDOT, and evidence of such approval must be submitted to the county with any offer of a new road to the county which intersects with a state highway. 
(Amend. of 2-23-2006, art. 10) 
Sec. 66-41. - Requirements for traffic control devices. 
Street name markers and such signs, signals and pavement markers, as needed for safety purposes as determined by the county manager and/or the county public works director, or their designated representative, shall be provided and installed in accordance with the Manual of Uniform Traffic Control Devices, of the Georgia Department of Transportation. All traffic control devices shall be provided by the developer of the road and installed by the county's public works department prior to final inspection and acceptance of the road by the county. 
(Amend. of 6-10-2008, Art. 11) 
Secs. 66-42—66-60. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - RIGHTS-OF-WAY 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 66-61. - Prohibited acts. 
No person shall in any manner or way use any part or portion of the right-of-way of a county road for the purpose of fueling or refueling of aerial application fertilizers nor engage in any act related thereto. The use of a county road right-of-way for such a purpose is specifically prohibited. 
(Ord. of 10-8-2002, § 1) 
Sec. 66-62. - Penalties. 
(a)  Any person violating this article, or any provision hereof, shall, upon conviction, be punished by a fine of not less than $250.00 and not more than $1,000.00, and/or a sentence of one to 60 days in the county jail. The magistrate court shall have authority to permit the sentenced party to perform community service in lieu of payment of that portion of a fine imposed above $250.00 at the rate of $6.00 per hour; however, this would not include any statutory imposed fine add-ons. The performance of such community service shall be in compliance with such conditions as the magistrate may order. 
(b)  No person accused of violating this article shall be arrested prior to trial, but any person who fails to appear for trial shall be arrested thereafter on the warrant of the magistrate, and required to post bond for his future appearance. 
(c)  Violations of this article shall be tried upon citations which shall be issued to an alleged violator of any provisions of this article. Such citation shall state the time and place at which the accused is to appear for trial, shall identify the offense with which the accused is charged, shall have an identifying number by which it shall be filed with the court, shall indicate the identity of the accused and the date of service, and shall be signed by the representative of the county who completes and serves it. The citation may be served by certified mail, return receipt requested. 
(d)  Citations issued under this article may be tried without a prosecuting attorney; however, if the prosecuting attorney is needed, the county attorney shall serve as the prosecuting attorney. 
(e)  Violations of this chapter shall be tried in the magistrate court of the county, and shall be tried in accordance with the O.C.G.A. § 15-10-60 et seq. 
(f)  Nothing in this article shall prevent the board of commissioners from bringing any civil action for injunction, or other proceedings to abate any violation of this article or other state or federal law. No sanction, penalty or remedy prescribed in this section shall be considered exclusive of any other remedy, but shall be available in addition to any other sanctions, penalty or remedy provided by law. 
(g)  Each violation of this article shall constitute a separate offense. 
(Ord. of 10-8-2002, § 2) 
Secs. 66-63—66-75. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - PROPERTY ACCESS CULVERTS 

Sec. 66-76. - Prohibited acts. 
(a)  No person, partnership, corporation or organization of any kind may proceed over, go through or across any road drainage structure, to specifically include a drainage ditch running parallel with the road, to gain access to his/her/its property situated adjacent to a county road, by way of any motorized vehicle, without having first installed in or across such drainage structure a property access culvert, also known as a driveway culvert, in compliance with the requirements of this division. 
(b)  No person, partnership, corporation or organization of any kind may install a property access culvert or place any object of any kind in the right-of-way of any county road, which includes a road's drainage system, in order to gain access to his/her/its property situated adjacent to a county road, without having first obtained from the county a permit for such installation in accordance with the requirements of this division. 
(Ord. of 8-11-2003, § 1; Ord. of 9-3-2015) 
Sec. 66-77. - Permit for installation of property access culvert in county road right-of-way. 
Upon application in compliance with the requirements of this division, the county shall issue a permit to any person, partnership, corporation or such other organization that is the owner of property situated adjacent to a county road for the placement of a property access culvert in the county's road right-of-way. No permit shall be issued except as expressly authorized under the provisions of this division. 
(Ord. of 8-11-2003, § 2; Ord. of 9-3-2015) 
Sec. 66-78. - Permit application, application fee and issuance of permit. 
(a)  Any person or legal entity desiring to obtain a permit to install a property access culvert shall make application to the county board of commissioners in the form as established by clerk of this board. 
(b)  The permit application shall contain, at a minimum, the name, address and telephone number of the applicant; the name and address of the owner of the property to be accessed, if different from the applicant; the property's tax map parcel number; the county road off which the subject property will be accessed; the anticipated use of the property to be accessed, i.e., private residence; multiple residences; commercial; industrial, etc.; the general location of where applicant desires to locate the access culvert with a drawing or sketch of the property and the date the use of the culvert will begin. 
(c)  The application shall be reviewed by the county, with such necessary inspection of the subject road and property, to determine the appropriate size, material and location for the property access culvert, so that same will accommodate proper drainage in order to avoid damage to the road structure and unnecessary flooding of surrounding properties. The county shall complete its review in a timely manner, and then a permit shall be issued which shall set forth the following: 
• The name(s) of the party to whom the permit is granted. 
• The location of where the property access culvert is to be installed. 
• The size (length and diameter) and material specifications of the culvert to be installed. 
(Ord. of 8-11-2003, § 3; Ord. of 9-3-2015) 
Sec. 66-79. - Minimum culvert specifications. 
No property access culvert shall be installed which is not at least 20 feet in length, 15 inches in diameter. 
(Ord. of 8-11-2003, § 4; Ord. of 11-15-2005, § 1; Amend. of 11-15-2005, § 1; Ord. of 9-3-2015) 
Sec. 66-80. - Installation of property access culverts on county roads. 
Property access culverts on the right-of-way of a road which is a part of the county's road system will be installed by the county. 
(Ord. of 8-11-2003, § 5; Ord. of 11-15-2005, § 1; Amend. of 11-15-2005, § 1; Ord. of 9-3-2015) 
Sec. 66-81. - Replacement of existing property access culverts on county roads. 
When, in the opinion of the county's road superintendent, it has been determined that an existing property access culvert located in the right-of-way of a county road has been damaged or otherwise worn to the extent that it is a danger to the motoring public or incapable of accommodating proper drainage in order to prevent damage to the road or flooding of surrounding properties, then the county shall replace such culverts. 
(Ord. of 8-11-2003, § 6; Ord. of 9-3-2015) 
Sec. 66-82. - Payment of cost for the installation of a property access culverts by the county. 
The cost of a culvert will be determined by the length and diameter of the pipe. The citizens will pay the county's actual cost of the culvert. 
(Ord. of 8-11-2003, § 8; Amend. of 11-15-2005, § 1; Ord. of 9-3-2015) 
Note— Formerly § 66-83. 
Sec. 66-83. - Penalties. 
(a)  Any person violating this division, or any provision hereof, upon conviction, shall be punished as follows: 
By a fine of not less than $75.00 and not more than $250.00. The magistrate court shall have authority to permit the sentenced party to perform community service in payment of that portion of a fine imposed above $250.00 at the rate of $7.25 per hour; however, this would not include any statutory imposed fine add-ons. The performance of such community service shall be in compliance with such conditions as the magistrate may order. 
(b)  No person accused of violating this division shall be arrested prior to trial, but any person who fails to appear for trial shall be arrested thereafter on the warrant of the magistrate, and required to post bond for his future appearance. 
(c)  Violations of this division shall be tried upon citations which shall be issued to an alleged violator of any provisions of this division. Such citation shall state the time and place at which the accused is to appear for trial, shall identify the offense with which the accused is charged, shall have an identifying number by which it shall be filed with the court, shall indicate the identity of the accused and the date of service, and shall be signed by the representative of the county who completes and serves it. Said citation may be served by certified mail, return receipt requested. 
(d)  Citations issued hereunder may be tried without a prosecuting attorney, however in the event the prosecuting attorney is needed the county attorney shall serve as the prosecuting attorney. 
(e)  Violations of this chapter shall be tried in the magistrate court of Brantley County, Georgia, and shall be tried in accordance with the Official Code of Georgia, Chapter 15-10. 
(f)  Nothing in this division shall prevent the county board of commissioners from bringing any civil action for injunction, or other proceedings to abate any violation of this division or other state or federal law. No sanction, penalty or remedy prescribed herein shall be considered exclusive of any other remedy, but shall be available in addition to any other sanctions, penalty or remedy provided by law. 
(g)  Each violation of this division shall constitute a separate offense. 
(Ord. of 8-11-2003, § 9; Amend. of 11-15-2005, § 1; Ord. of 9-3-2015) 
Note— Formerly § 66-84. 
Secs. 66-84—66-100. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - MAILBOX LOCATIONS 

Sec. 66-101. - Prohibited acts. 
No person, partnership, corporation or organization of any kind, may use any portion of the right-of-way of any road that is a part of the county's road system to install or locate a receptacle (mail box) for receiving items delivered by the U.S. Postal Service (mail) unless same is located and installed in accordance with the county's approved mail box location plan. 
(Ord. of 2-10-2004, § 1) 
Sec. 66-102. - The county's approved mail box location plan. 
The county's approved mail box location plan governing the location and use of the right-of-way of a county road to locate and install a receptacle for receiving items delivered by the U.S. Postal Service (mail) is attached hereto and incorporated herein by reference, same being hereby adopted and established in Brantley County, Georgia. 
(Ord. of 2-10-2004, § 2) 
Sec. 66-103. - Replacement of an existing mail box located on the right-of-way of a county road that does not comply with the county's approved mail box location plan. 
When, in the opinion of the county's road superintendent, it has been determined that a mail box, which existed prior to the adoption of this division, that is situated in the right-of-way of a county road and was not located in accordance with the county's approved mail box location plan, is a danger to the motoring public or is interfering with the county's maintenance of said road, including the road's drainage system, then the owner of the property that receives mail in such mail box shall be notified, in writing, by registered mail and the posting of such notice on any occupied structure on the property, of the problem posed by the mail box, and given 30 days to relocate and install a mail box that is in compliance with the county's approved mail box location plan, at the property owner's expense. Should the property owner fail or refuse to remove the existing mail box after such 30 days, then the county shall cause the removal of the existing mail box from the county's right-of-way and notify the delivering post office of said action. 
(Ord. of 2-10-2004, § 3) 
Sec. 66-104. - U.S. mail delivery service not to be impeded. 
The implementation of the approved mail box location plan should not be done in a manner that impedes the delivery of mail by the United States Postal Service. The county, through its board of commissioners, recognizes the authority and obligation of the United States Postal Service in the delivery of mail, and this division shall not be construed in any manner to the contrary. 
(Amend. of 3-24-2004, § 1) 
Sec. 66-105. - Penalties. 
(a)  Any person violating this division, or any provision hereof, upon conviction, shall be punished as follows: 
By a fine of not less than $250.00 and not more than $1,000.00, and/or a sentence of one to 60 days in the county jail. The magistrate court shall have authority to permit the sentenced party to perform community service in lieu of payment of that portion of a fine imposed above $250.00 at the rate of $6.00 per hour; however, this would not include any statutory imposed fine add-ons. The performance of such community service shall be in compliance with such conditions as the magistrate may order. 
(b)  No person accused of violating this division shall be arrested prior to trial, but any person who fails to appear for trial shall be arrested thereafter on the warrant of the magistrate, and required to post bond for his future appearance. 
(c)  Violations of this division shall be tried upon citations which shall be issued to an alleged violator of any provisions of this division. Such citation shall state the time and place at which the accused is to appear for trial, shall identify the offense with which the accused is charged, shall have an identifying number by which it shall be filed with the court, shall indicate the identity of the accused and the date of service, and shall be signed by the representative of the county who completes and serves it. Said citation may be served by certified mail, return receipt requested. 
(d)  Citations issued hereunder may be tried without a prosecuting attorney, however in the event the prosecuting attorney is needed the county attorney shall serve as the prosecuting attorney. 
(e)  Violations of this chapter shall be tried in the magistrate court of Brantley County, Georgia, and shall be tried in accordance with the Official Code of Georgia, Chapter 15-10. 
(f)  Nothing in this division shall prevent the county board of commissioners from bringing any civil action for injunction, or other proceedings to abate any violation of this division or other state or federal law. No sanction, penalty or remedy prescribed herein shall be considered exclusive of any other remedy, but shall be available in addition to any other sanctions, penalty or remedy provided by law. 
(g)  Each violation of this division shall constitute a separate offense. Every day a violation of this division occurs shall be considered as a separate offense. 
(Ord. of 2-10-2004, § 4) 
Secs. 66-106—66-149. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - ADDRESSING 

Sec. 66-150. - Short title. 
This article shall be known and may be cited as "The Brantley County Addressing Ordinance". 
(Ord. of 5-10-2005, § 1) 
Sec. 66-151. - Definitions. 
As used herein, the following terms, words or phrases and their derivations shall have the meaning that is provided in the National Emergency Number Association (NENA) Standard Guidelines as reference by the United States Postal Service, which is incorporated herein by reference, unless the context clearly indicates otherwise, to-wit: 
Address number shall mean the number assigned to consecutive intervals along a street or road pursuant to the number assignment formula contained herein. 
Display as used herein is the manner the numbers are affixed to a structure or otherwise displayed when affixing to a structure. 
Interval is defined as the distance along a roadway of 5.28 feet, there being 1,000 intervals per mile (5,280 feet). 
Non-compliance is any failure to comply with the provisions of this article including, but not limited to, by way of example: a number out of sequence, odd or even number on wrong side of street, rural box numbers in a 9-1-1 address area, numbers improperly affixed, numbers illegible, numbers unclear, numbers obstructed, numbers not visible, numbers not present, numbers of improper size, numbers not in contrast with immediate background, weatherworn numbers, wrong numbers, and non-approved numbers. 
Number assignment formula: The number assignment formula for Brantley County shall be as follows: 
Beginning from the point of origin a house number shall be assigned for each interval, with each interval on the right side of the roadway as one leaves the point of origin being assigned an even number, and each interval on the left side as one leaves the point of origin being assigned an odd number. Left and right shall be determined from the perspective of a traveler moving away from the road point of origin in a forward motion. The southern and western intersection or entry point of each road will be the point of origin. 
Occupant is any person, firm, entity, partnership, trust, corporation, association or other organization that is occupying or leasing a building or other property for a period exceeding 30 days. 
Owner is any and all persons, firms, entities, partnerships, trusts, corporation, associations, or other organizations that own the fee title to, or have an undivided interest in, any building or property, which is subject to the provisions of this article. 
Point of origin shall mean that end point of a road, which is the starting point for a numbering sequence. 
Primary structure shall include but not be limited to residential building, mobile home park, commercial building, industrial building, office building, public building, utility, communications tower. 
Road or street shall mean any public or private thoroughfare, used for vehicular traffic and/or any easement or right-of-way that provides sole access to more than two parcels or lots. This term shall be defined as the street suffix and shall include, but is not limited to; avenue, drive, way, boulevard, highway, lane, pike or similar street types. 
(Ord. of 5-10-2005, § 2; Ord. of 2-14-2006, § 1) 
Sec. 66-152. - Establishment of name of a street or road. 
(a)  The county addressing coordinator shall assign the names to all public streets or roads within the unincorporated area of the county. 
(b)  The county addressing coordinator, or his/her duly authorized agent, in consultation with the property owner(s), is hereby delegated the authority to assign or approve the name(s) for any private road or street, which provides access to four or more occupied residential or commercial structure, subject to review and approval by the board of commissioners. 
(c)  The chairman of the board of commissioners, or his/her designee, is authorized and directed to cause the placement of a street name sign at street/road intersections presently existing within the county. The initial cost of such signs and the installation thereof shall be at the county's expense. 
(d)  The names assigned to streets and roads within the county and heretofore approved by the board of commissioners shall be compiled in alphabetical index form and same shall be and hereafter known as the "Brantley County Road Name Index". This listing, and as hereafter amended, shall be the official listing of names for streets and roads in Brantley County, Georgia. This listing shall be filed and maintained in the office of the county addressing coordinator. The county addressing coordinator will provide a copy of the county road name index to the office of the board of commissioners whenever changes or updates are made. 
(e)  The county addressing coordinator shall follow this article to assure an orderly, logical and efficient manner of hereafter assigning names to streets and roads, and assigning street address numbers for residential and commercial structures in the county, all in accord with the street addressing system herein set forth. In this matter and in strict accord with this article, the county addressing coordinator is delegated the authority to hereafter assign names to new streets and roads in the county, and to assign the street address to occupied structures located said streets and roads. 
(f)  Road names shall not duplicate road names already assigned, irrespective of road name prefixes or suffixes except for roads located within different corporations. The four cardinal points of the compass may be used as a prefix or suffix to designate portions of a continuous street. 
(g)  A street name shall not be differentiated using the same name by changing the street suffix such as a street or avenue except that those duplicate streets having different suffixes must be directly accessible from the street having the same name with the different suffix. An example would be Birch Court must be accessible from Birch Street. 
(h)  A street shall have only one name throughout its entire length unless approved as an exception by the board of commissioners. 
(Ord. of 5-10-2005, § 3; Ord. of 2-14-2006, § 1) 
Sec. 66-153. - Establishment of a street addressing system. 
(a)  All occupied residential and commercial structures located in the county shall be assigned a street address in accordance with the county number assignment formula. 
(b)  The combination of such an address number and the road or street name shall be the official address of such structure. 
(c)  An application for a building permit, an electrical hook-up, and/or a septic tank installation permit for a new building shall be considered an application for an address assignment. The county department of code enforcement shall coordinate with the county addressing office for the assignment of addresses. Addresses shall be assigned prior to the beginning of any site improvements or construction. The address shall be issued not later than 30 days following identification of address and installed on the structure prior to final inspection from the county department of code enforcement. 
(d)  No street currently shown on a subdivision plat filed with the county or otherwise shall be placed on the county road name index and implemented by a subdivision owner until such name has been submitted to and approved by the county addressing coordinator and added to the county road name index. The county addressing coordinator shall not approve any street or road name already in use, confusingly similar to a name already in use, deemed confusing for purposes of emergency response, or deemed inappropriate by the county addressing coordinator. Any street name that is not approved by the addressing coordinator is subject to appeal and review by the board of commissioners. 
(e)  No new street or road within the county shall be assigned a name on a subdivision plat or otherwise until such name is submitted to and approved by the county addressing coordinator, and added to the county road name index. The county addressing coordinator shall have the authority to refuse to approve any name already in use, confusingly similar to a name already in use, deemed confusing for purposes of emergency response, or deemed inappropriate by the county addressing coordinator. Any street name that is not approved by the addressing coordinator is subject to appeal and review by the board of commissioners. 
(Ord. of 5-10-2005, § 4) 
Sec. 66-154. - Placement and size of address number. 
(a)  Display of number—All structures. All existing structures in the county shall have their address numbers placed at the driveway location which serves the property. The number shall be mounted on a 4 × 4 wood post or a two-inch steel post at the driveway location serving the said property. The signage shall be six inches in height with four-inch Arial font numbers, white reflective in color on a blue background. See attached details showing the address number approved locations. 
(b)  Display of number—Residential structure. Each primary structure shall display the number of the address assigned to that address. The numbers shall be at least six inches in height, and of a durable and clearly visible material. The numbers shall be placed on, above, or at the side of the main entrance so the number is clearly visible from the public right-of-way. Address numbers are to be a contrasting color to the background on which they are mounted. 
(c)  Display of number—Commercial and industrial structure. Address numbers for commercial and industrial structures shall be at least six inches in height. The number shall be placed above or on the main entrance to the structure when possible. If such number is not clearly visible from the public right-of-way, the number shall be placed along a driveway or on a sign visible from the same. Address numbers are to be a contrasting color to the background on which they are mounted. 
(d)  Display of number—Apartments and similar. The address number assigned to a single building number shall be displayed on each assigned structure following the International Property Maintenance Code section 304.3. Numbers and/or letters for individual apartments or units within these complexes shall be displayed on, above, or to the side of the main doorway of each apartment or unit. 
(e)  Display of number—Manufactured home park, trailer park, recreational vehicle park and similar. The address number assigned to a unit within an organized park shall be one address number for the park with each trailer assigned a lot or space number. The lot or space number must be posted and permanently affixed to the lot identifying the lot or space number. The main address to the park must be posted at the entrance of the park. Address numbers are to be a contrasting color to the background on which they are mounted. 
(f)  All cost incurred by a property owner or occupant of a structure where an address number must be displayed to be in compliance with this article shall be at the sole expense of said party. 
(g)  The property owner, occupant or person in charge of any house, building, mobile home, or other structure to which a street number has been assigned in accordance with this article shall display the said street number as specified in this article within 30 days of receiving notification of such number. 
(h)  Whenever any house, building, or structure shall be erected or located after the initial establishment of the uniform street numbering system as provided for herein, then the owner, occupant or person in charge of same shall, within 30 days of receiving notification of the assigned address, display the street number assigned to said structure in accordance with this article. 
(Ord. of 5-10-2005, § 5) 
Sec. 66-155. - Placement and size of street/road name signs. 
(a)  All new street signs erected within the county shall be in conformance with the specifications of this article, unless the Georgia Department of Transportation, Division of Highways or the county board of commissioners grants a variance. 
(b)  Sign specifications. All signs erected shall be in conformance to the Georgia Department of Transportation, Division of Highways as defined in the "Standards for the Design and Installation of Road Name Signing" published March 1999 (Appendix A). In all cases, the posted speed limit shall govern the specification of signs erected per Appendix A. 
(c)  The owner, creator or developer of any new residential or commercial subdivision or other like real estate development shall erect or cause to be erected street name signs in conformance with this article at any and all intersections within such subdivision or development upon construction of any street on or after the effective date of this article, unless, by specific vote of the board of commissioners, such responsibility is assumed by the county. 
(Ord. of 5-10-2005, § 6) 
Sec. 66-156. - Changing the name of a street or road. 
(a)  There shall be and same is hereby imposed a moratorium on the change of any street or road's name for a period of two years following the completion of the address conversion project as now underway in the county. The beginning date of said moratorium shall be established by act of the board of commissioner by way of an amendment to this article. 
(b)  After the moratorium for making any change of a street or road's name has expired, any person desiring to change the name of an existing street or road, shall file a petition with the board of commissioners requesting such a change, which petition must be join in with by the owners of 80 percent of the parcels on the subject street or road. However, such a petition shall not be filed or considered until the county addressing coordinator has confirmed the availability of the proposed name. 
When filing a petition for a street name change, documentation such as a tax bill or deed, showing the ownership of each signatory to the petition must accompany the petition at the time of filing. The tax assessor shall sign off to authenticate that ownerships match the application. 
No petition for a street name change as authorized herein shall be accepted or considered without the petitioner also tendering with the petition a non-refundable deposit in the amount of $250.00. Upon approval of the name change, the petitioner shall be obligated to pay to the county for the actual costs incurred by the name change, such as any legal advertisements, the purchase and installation of new street signs, etc. The cost shall be charged against the said deposit, and should the deposit be insufficient to cover all such cost, then the petitioner shall be liable to the county for such additional cost. 
(c)  If the name of any street or road is changed as herein provided, then, within ten days of such change, the county addressing coordinator shall send notice of such change to the United States Postal Service. 
(Ord. of 5-10-2005, § 7) 
Sec. 66-157. - Map of county roads and streets. 
All parcels of property within the county which shall be given a street number in accordance with this article may be identified and shown on maps maintained by the county addressing coordinator. The maps and explanatory matter thereon may be amended, modified, or changed at the direction of the county addressing coordinator. 
(Ord. of 5-10-2005, § 8) 
Sec. 66-158. - Appeals and amendments. 
(a)  During the initial stage assigning addresses under this article and prior to the completion of the project task, any request concerning road name changes and/or addressing complaints shall be first directed to the county addressing coordinator, which shall be made within 30 days from when the road name and/or address is assigned. If the complaining party and the addressing coordinator can not come to an agreed resolution of the issue, then the complaining party may appeal the decision of the county addressing coordinator to the county board of commissioners for a final disposition of the issue. Provided, however, all such appeals to the board of commissioners must be filed with the board within 30 days of the decision made by the addressing coordinator on the matter. In considering such an appeal, the board of commissioners may, at their discretion, consider oral comments on the matter from the appealing party and the addressing coordinator, or make a decision based solely upon written comments. All such appeals shall be decided by the board of commissioners within 30 days of receiving either the oral or written comments. The decision of the board of commissioners shall be final, and same shall be in writing with a copy of same mailed by the clerk of the board to the appealing party. 
(b)  After the address conversion project has been implemented in the county, any concerns, problems or complaints of a property owner regarding the street naming and numbering system shall be handled on a case by case basis by the county addressing coordinator, subject to appeal to the board of commissioners as set forth in subsection (a) above. 
(Ord. of 5-10-2005, § 9) 
Sec. 66-159. - Notice of violation of ordinance. 
Whenever the county addressing coordinator has reason to believe there exists a non-compliance (violation) of this article, then he/she shall give a written notice of such non-compliance to the person believed to be failing to comply with the article and direct such person to take such necessary action in order to eliminate the violation within 30 days from date of notification. If such person(s) fail to take the necessary action to eliminate the existing violation, then the matter shall be brought to the attention of the county code enforcement officer who shall issue the necessary citation(s) regarding such violations. 
(Ord. of 5-10-2005, § 10) 
Sec. 66-160. - Penalties. 
(a)  Any person violating this article, or any provision hereof, upon conviction, shall be punished as follows: By a fine of not more than $500.00, and/or a sentence of one to 60 days in the county jail. 
(b)  No person accused of violating this article shall be arrested prior to trial, but any person who fails to appear for trial shall be arrested thereafter on the warrant of the magistrate, and required to post bond for his future appearance. 
(c)  Violations of this article shall be tried upon citations which shall be issued to an alleged violator of any provisions of this article. Such citation shall state the time and place at which the accused is to appear for trial, shall identify the offense with which the accused is charged, shall have an identifying number by which it shall be filed with the court, shall indicate the identity of the accused and the date of service, and shall be signed by the representative of the county who completes and serves it. Said citation may be served by certified mail, return receipt requested. 
(d)  Citations issued hereunder may be tried without a prosecuting attorney, however in the event the prosecuting attorney is needed the county attorney shall serve as the prosecuting attorney. 
(e)  Violations of this chapter shall be tried in the magistrate court of Brantley County, Georgia, and shall be tried in accordance with the Official Code of Georgia, Chapter 15-10. 
(f)  Nothing in this article shall prevent the county board of commissioners from bringing any civil action for injunction, or other proceedings to present, correct, or abate any violation of this article or other state or federal law. No sanction, penalty or remedy prescribed herein shall be considered exclusive of any other remedy, but shall be available in addition to any other sanctions, penalty or remedy provided by law. 
(g)  Each violation of this article shall constitute a separate offense. 
(Ord. of 5-10-2005, § 11) 
Chapter 70 - SOLID WASTE[1]

ARTICLE II. - SOLID WASTE MANAGEMENT PLAN[2] 

Footnotes:

Sec. 70-31. - Adoption. 
(a)  The board of commissioners does hereby authorize the adoption of the county solid waste management plan as submitted to and approved by the state department of community affairs June 22, 2006. The complete text is available in the offices of the city. 
(b)  The county commission adopts the solid waste management plan updates and accompanying short-term work program. 
(Res. of 9-14-1993; Res. of 3-9-1999; Res. of 6-22-2006; Res. of 6-15-2017) 
Secs. 70-32—70-60. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - COLLECTION AND LITTER CONTROL[3] 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
State Law reference— Scrap tire disposal restrictions, O.C.G.A. § 12-8-40.1; yard trimmings disposal restrictions, O.C.G.A. § 12-8-40.2; litter control, O.C.G.A. § 16-7-42 et seq.; transporting garbage or waste across state or county boundaries without permission, O.C.G.A. § 36-1-16; littering highways, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-249. 

Sec. 70-61. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms, and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Garbage means household or office waste, to include, paper, cardboard, tin cans, food waste, glass, plastic containers, cloth, fruit and vegetable refuse, and such other nondescript items of household waste as may be otherwise disposable after human use. 
Litter means all sand, gravel, slag, brickbats, rubbish, waste material, refuse, trash, debris, dead animals, furniture, appliances, garbage, or discarded materials of every kind and description. 
(Res. of 5-15-1991, § 2) 
Cross reference— Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 70-62. - Use of waste receptacles. 
No person shall: 
(1)  Deposit, place or leave any items other than garbage in any receptacle (dumpster) provided by the county for the collection of garbage; 
(2)  Dump, deposit, throw, leave or cause the dumping, depositing, throwing, placing or leaving of garbage or litter in the immediate area of any garbage collection receptacle; 
(3)  Place, throw or deposit any animal carcass, or any live animal in any garbage collection receptacle; 
(4)  Place, throw or deposit any burning or smoldering material in any garbage collection receptacle; 
(5)  Set fire to the contents of any garbage collection receptacle; 
(6)  Deposit, place or leave any explosive or spontaneous combustible materials in any garbage collection receptacle; 
(7)  Sort through, scatter or remove any of the garbage which has been placed and left in a garbage collection receptacle. This subsection shall not apply to any county employee or agent who is in the performance of his official duties; 
(8)  Enter, climb in or on, or go into any garbage collection receptacles. This subsection shall not apply to any county employee or agent who is in the performance of his official duties; or 
(9)  Deposit, place or leave any items in a garbage collection receptacle unless that party is a resident of the county. However, this subsection shall not apply to a nonresident who is traveling through the county, and who has not entered the county for the purpose of disposing of garbage. 
(10)  Place, deposit, or leave or cause the placing, depositing or leaving of any motor vehicle tire in any garbage collection receptacle, or in the immediate area of any garbage collection receptacle. 
(Res. of 5-15-1991, § 3; Ord. of 3-12-2002, § 1) 
Sec. 70-63. - Littering prohibited. 
(a)  No person, company or corporation shall dump, deposit, throw, or leave or cause or permit the dumping, depositing, placing, throwing, or leaving of litter or garbage or tires on any property of the county, unless the property or location is designated for same, i.e., garbage collection receptacles, trash cans, and/or the county solid waste transfer site during operating hours, and only such items as are specifically approved for deposit at such locations. 
(b)  Motor vehicle tires may be deposited at the county's solid waste transfer station without being a violation of this section upon payment of the disposal fee as hereafter set forth: 

 
(c)  No person, company, or corporation shall, with intent, dump, deposit, throw or leave or cause or permit, the dumping, depositing, placing, throwing or leaving litter or garbage on private property. 
(d)  A reward of $1,000.00 shall be paid by the county commission to any person who provides information leading to the citation and conviction of any person(s) and/or entity violating this section. 
(Res. of 5-15-1991, § 4; Ord. of 3-12-2002, § 2; Amd. of 3-3-2016(2)) 
Sec. 70-64. - Penalties. 
Any person violating this article, or any provision thereof, upon conviction as heretofore provided in 70-65, Enforcement, the defendant shall be punished by a mandatory penalty of not less than 40, nor more than 100 hours of community service. However, in keeping with a defendant's health status, upon evidence submitted by the defendant, as an alternative punishment, shall be a mandatory fine of not less than $350.00 nor more than $1,000.00. 
(Res. of 5-15-1991, § 6; Ord. of 8-13-1998, § 2; Amend. of 1-13-2009; Amend. of 3-3-2016) 
Sec. 70-65. - Enforcement. 
(a)  The sheriff of the county, any deputies thereof, any agent of the county authorized by the board of commissioners to issue citations for the enforcement of county ordinances, and all other law enforcement officers shall be authorized to issue citations to violators of any provisions of this article. 
(b)  No person accused of violating this article shall be arrested prior to trial, but any person who fails to appear for trial shall be arrested thereafter on the warrant of the magistrate, and required to post bond for his future appearance. 
(c)  Violations of this article shall be tried upon citations which shall be issued to an alleged violator of any sections of this article. Such citation shall state the time and place at which the accused is to appear for trial, shall identify the offense with which the accused is charged, shall have an identifying number by which it shall be filed with the court, shall indicate the identity of the accused and the date of service, and shall be signed by the representative of the county who completes and serves it. The citation may be served by certified mail, return receipt requested. 
(d)  Citations issued under this article may be tried without a prosecuting attorney; however, if the prosecuting attorney is needed, the county attorney shall serve as the prosecuting attorney. 
(e)  Violations of this article shall be tried in the magistrate court of the county and shall be tried in accordance with O.C.G.A. § 15-10-60 et seq. 
(f)  Nothing in this article shall prevent the board of commissioners from bringing any civil action for injunction, or other proceedings to present, correct, or abate any violation of this article or other state or federal law. No sanction, penalty or remedy prescribed in this article shall be considered exclusive of any other remedy, but shall be available in addition to any other sanctions, penalty or remedy provided by law. 
(Res. of 5-15-1991, § 5; Ord. of 8-13-1998, § 1) 
Secs. 70-66—70-90. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - WASTE DISPOSAL FACILITY SITING MORATORIUM[4] 

Footnotes: 
--- (4) --- 
Editor's note— Ord. of April 12, 2005, §§ 1—3, did not specifically amend the Code; hence, inclusion herein as Art. IV, §§ 70-91—70-93, was at the discretion of the editor. See also the Code Comparative Table. 

Sec. 70-91. - Short title. 
This article shall be known and may be cited as the "Brantley County Waste Disposal Facility Siting Moratorium Ordinance." 
(Ord. of 4-12-2005, § 1) 
Sec. 70-92. - Definitions. 
As used in this article, the terms: 
Biomedical waste means any such matter, things or material as described and defined in O.C.G.A. § 12-8-22 to such solid waste. 
Disposal facility means any such facility as described and defined in O.C.G.A. § 12-8-22(8) which code section is incorporated herein as if it were fully set out, and any amendments hereafter made to said code section shall also be made a part hereof. 
Materials recovery facility means a solid waste handling facility that provides for the extraction from solid waste of recoverable materials, materials suitable for use as a fuel or soil amendment, or any combination of such materials. 
Municipal solid waste means all such matter, things or material as described and defined in O.C.G.A. § 12-8-22(18) which code section is incorporated herein as if it were fully set out, and any amendments hereafter made to said code section shall also be made a part hereof. 
Person means those entities and people as described and defined in O.C.G.A. § 12-8-22(22) which code section is incorporated herein as if it were fully set out, and any amendments hereafter made to said code section shall also be made a part hereof. 
Solid waste means all such matter, things or material as described and defined in O.C.G.A. § 12-8-22(33) which code section is incorporated herein as if it were fully set out, and any amendments hereafter made to said code section shall also be made a part hereof. 
Solid waste handling facility means any such facility as described and defined in O.C.G.A. § 12-8-22(35) which code section is incorporated herein as if it were fully set out, and any amendments hereafter made to said code section shall also be made a part hereof. 
(Ord. of 4-12-2005, § 2) 
Sec. 70-93. - Facility siting moratorium. 
No person not presently operating a waste handling facility in Brantley County, Georgia, shall site, locate, operate or apply for any permits required by the State of Georgia or of an agency of the United States of America to site, locate or operate, any solid waste handling, storage or disposal facility; any municipal solid waste disposal facility; any biomedical waste treatment and/or disposal facility; any solid waste thermal treatment technology facility; any hazardous waste treatment handling, storage or disposal facility; any special solid waste handling, storage or disposal facility; or any recovered materials processing facility, for a period of one year from the effective date of this article or until such time as the board of commissioners of the county has adopted and the state has approved the county's revised and updated land use plan and solid waste management plan for the county, as required by the laws of the state, which ever occurs first. 
(Ord. of 4-12-2005, § 3) 
Chapter 74 - TAXATION[1]

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 74-1. - [Waiver of penalties and interest—Ad valorem taxes.] 
(a)  Pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 48-5-242, the board of commissioners may waive in whole or in part, the collection of any amount due to Brantley County, for penalties or interest assessed for failure to comply with the law governing assessment and collection of ad valorem taxes. The tax commissioner shall determine whether or not the default giving rise to the penalty or interest was due to a reasonable cause and not due to gross or willful neglect of the law or of regulations or instructions issued pursuant to law. The tax commissioner may recommend to the board of commissioners the waiver of penalties and interest, in whole or in part. 
(b)  The waiver of penalties or interest in accordance with O.C.G.A. § 48-5-242 and under the provision of this section shall be subject to the following conditions: 
(1)  Only interest that accrues on or after July 1, 2002 may be waived; 
(2)  The taxpayer shall provide a claim in writing, under oath, stating the specific reason for the taxpayer's failure to pay the ad valorem taxes in a timely manner; 
(3)  The tax commissioner advises the board of commissioners that the default giving rise to penalty or interest was not a result of: 
a.  Gross or willful negligence; 
b.  A disregard of law or regulations or instructions issued pursuant to law; 
c.  That the taxpayer has not been delinquent in the payment of other taxes owed to Brantley County or other counties; and 
d.  Taxes and penalties will impose a substantial hardship upon the taxpayer. 
(c)  The board of commissioners will make the final decision as to whether to waive the penalties and interest in whole or in part. 
(Ord. of 9-8-2009, §§ 1—3) 
Editor's note— An ordinance adopted Sept. 8, 2009, §§ 1—3, did not specify manner of inclusion; hence, codification as § 74-1 was at the discretion of the editor. 
Sec. 74-2. - [Minimum acreage to qualify for bona fide conservation use assessment.] 
The requirements to qualify for the current use assessment concerning real properties in Brantley County may be as provided by O.C.G.A. § 48-5-7.4 et seq. 
(Res. of 4-13-2010; Res. of 12-13-2011) 
Editor's note— A resolution adopted April 13, 2010, did not specify manner of inclusion; hence, codification as § 74-2 was at the editor's discretion. 
Sec. 74-3. - [Intergovernmental agreements.] 

 
Editor's note— At the request of the county, intergovernmental agreements have been added to the Code of Ordinances. At the discretion of the editor, these agreements have not been fully set out, but are listed as references only in § 74-3.

ARTICLE II. - LOCAL OPTION SALES TAX 

Sec. 74-31. - Tax imposed. 
There is imposed a one percent retail sales and use tax as provided by O.C.G.A. § 48-8-82 for the Special District of Brantley County, Georgia. 
(Res. of 12-21-1982) 
Sec. 74-32. - [Special sales and use tax.] 
There shall be imposed in Brantley County, Georgia, commencing January 1, 2008, and continuing for a period of 20 consecutive calendar quarters or until the amount of $7,000,000.00 has been raised, a special one-percent sales tax for the purpose of financing the following capital projects, to wit: recreation facilities, to include land, structures and major equipment; a county jail facility; and for road, street and bridge improvement purposes, in the amounts so stated in the referendum question. 
There shall be imposed in Brantley County, Georgia, commencing January 1, 2013, and continuing for a period of 24 consecutive calendar quarters/six years or until the amount of $8,000,000.00 has been raised, a special one-percent sales tax for the purpose of financing the following capital projects, which includes: recreational facility, including irrigation systems, landscaping, parking, structures and major equipment; a county jail; and roads, streets and bridges repair and improvements, which repair and improvements may include sidewalks and bicycle paths. 
(Res. of 9-25-2007; Res. of 12-13-2011) 
Editor's note— A resolution adopted Sept. 25, 2007, did not specify manner of inclusion; hence, codification as § 74-32 was at the editor's discretion. 
Secs. 74-33—74-60. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - FINANCIAL INSTITUTION BUSINESS LICENSE TAX 

Sec. 74-61. - Annual business license tax. 
In accordance with O.C.G.A. § 48-6-93, there is hereby levied for the year 1984, and for each year thereafter, an annual business license tax upon all depository financial institutions located within the county at a rate of 0.25 percent of the gross receipts of such depository financial institutions. The term "gross receipts" means the same as defined in O.C.G.A. § 48-6-93. The term "depository financial institutions" means state and national banks, state building and loan associations, and federal savings and loan associations. 
(Res. of 1-1-1984(1), § 1) 
Sec. 74-62. - Minimum business license tax. 
The minimum annual amount of business license tax due from any depository financial institution pursuant to section 74-61 shall be $1,000.00. 
(Res. of 1-1-1984(1), § 2) 
Sec. 74-63. - Filing of return. 
Pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 48-6-93(c), each depository financial institution subject to an annual business license tax shall file a return of its gross receipts with the board of commissioners on March 1 of the year following the year in which such gross receipts are measured. Such return shall be in the manner and in the form prescribed by the commissioner of the department on the allocation method set forth in O.C.G.A § 48-6-93(d). The board of commissioners shall assess and collect the tax levied pursuant to this article based upon the information provided in such return. 
(Res. of 1-1-1984(1), § 3) 
Sec. 74-64. - Due date of taxes. 
Annual business license taxes levied pursuant to this article shall be due no later than 30 days after filing of the return prescribed by section 74-63 unless extended by the board of commissioners. 
(Res. of 1-1-1984(1), § 4) 
Secs. 74-65—74-90. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - GROSS PREMIUMS TAX ON INSURERS 

Sec. 74-91. - Gross premiums tax on insurance other than life insurance. 
In accordance with O.C.G.A. § 33-8-8.2, there is hereby levied for the year 1984, and for each year thereafter, an annual tax upon each insurer doing insurance business within the unincorporated area of the county, in an amount equal to 2.5 percent of the gross direct premiums received during the calendar year on all insurance, other than life insurance, as defined in O.C.G.A. § 33-3-5(2), (3), (4) and (5). The term "gross direct premiums" means the same as used in O.C.G.A. § 33-8-8.2(a). 
(Res. of 1-1-1984(2), §1) 
Secs. 74-92—74-120. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - SPECIAL DISTRICTS[2] 
Footnotes:
