DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Secs. 74-121—74-140. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - WAYNESVILLE SPECIAL FIRE PROTECTION DISTRICT 

Sec. 74-141. - Tax district created. 
(a)  There is hereby created a special fire tax district within Brantley County which shall be known and cited as the "Waynesville Special Fire Protection District", hereinafter sometimes referred to as "the district". 
(b)  Waynesville Special Fire Protection District shall be as follows: 
Beginning at the Northeast corner of Brantley County; then in a Southerly direction along the Easternmost line of Brantley County where it abuts Glynn County and later Camden County to the point where it intersects the Satilla River; thence in a Northerly direction along the Satilla River to the intersection with a straight line extrapolated from the Coffee County Road; thence Eastward along that line and on through the Coffee County Road to State Highway 110 North and the intersection with the Western boundary of Georgia Militia District #334; thence in a Northeasterly direction along the Western boundary of the Georgia Militia District #334 to the point where it abuts the Wayne County line; thence in a Westerly direction along the Northern line of the Georgia Militia District #334 where is abuts the Wayne county line back to the point of origin at the Northeast corner of Brantley County. 
(Res. of 5-8-1990, § 2; Res. of 9-14-2010, §§ 1, 2) 
Sec. 74-142. - Additional ad valorem tax. 
All properties, both real and personal, located and situated within the boundaries of the district shall be subject to an additional ad valorem tax levy as set annually hereafter by the Board of Commissioners of Brantley County. 
(Res. of 5-8-1990, § 3; Res. of 9-14-2010, § 3) 
Sec. 74-143. - Use of taxes. 
(a)  All ad valorem taxes collected from the additional levy within the district shall be used and appropriated only, to pay the cost of providing additional fire protection services within the district; to construct and maintain facilities for housing fire equipment and personnel within the district; to purchase equipment to be located and used within the district; to pay the cost of training for persons who provide fire protection services within the district; to pay the cost of materials and supplies used for training firefighters assigned to the district; to pay the cost of insurance provided on real and/or personal property located within the district; to pay for such other costs and expenses as may be deemed appropriate and needed for the fire protection services within the district. 
(b)  All properties, both real and personal, purchased from ad valorem tax revenue within the district shall be acquired in the name of "Brantley County, for the benefit of the Waynesville Fire Protection District". All proceeds derived from the sale of any such acquired property, shall be used in the same manner as the taxes levied within the district. 
(Res. of 5-8-1990, §§ 4, 6; Res. of 9-14-2010, §§ 4, 6) 
Sec. 74-144. - Additional tax levy. 
Nothing herein shall require an additional tax levy within the district, as the resolution is permissive and not mandatory. However, should a tax be levied by the board of commissioners within the district, funds collected must be used only for providing fire protection services within the district. Same must be used only for providing fire protection services in addition to such services as then being provided by the board of commissioners in the county which lies outside the district and not in any other special district. 
(Res. of 5-9-1990, § 7; Res. of 9-14-2010, § 7) 
Sec. 74-145. - Fire protection services. 
The providing of the fire protection services as herein contemplated within the district may at the discretion of the board of commissioners, be performed by the Waynesville Volunteer Fire Department Inc., a nonprofit Georgia Corporation, or such other party or parties as may be selected by the board of commissioners from time to time, under such terms and conditions as established by the board of commissioners. Any such services arrangement shall be set forth in a contractual agreement and approved by the board of commissioners. The board shall review the manner in which any such contracted services are being performed on an annual basis when considering the levy to be made within the district. No contract shall be continued with any party not providing the required service which meets the expectation of the Brantley County Commission. 
(Res. of 5-8-1990, § 5; Res. of 9-14-2010, § 5) 
Secs. 74-146—74-170. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - CALVARY SPECIAL FIRE PROTECTION DISTRICT 

Sec. 74-171. - Tax district created. 
(a)  Calvary Special Fire Protection District. There was on August 2, 1977, and is hereby created a special tax district within the county which shall be known and cited as the "Calvary Special Fire Protection District," sometimes referred to in this division as "the district." 
(b)  Boundaries. The boundaries of the Calvary Special Fire Protection District shall be as follows: 
Beginning at a point where the Brantley County-Ware County line joins the Satilla River; thence in an easterly direction along the southern bank of the Satilla River to the point where it joins Big Creek; thence in a southerly direction along Big Creek to a point where it intersects state route 82 (Corridor Z); thence in a westerly direction along state route 82 to the point where it joins the Ware County-Brantley County line; thence in a northerly direction along the Ware County-Brantley County line to the point where it joins the Satilla River. 
(Res. of 2-13-1990, § 2) 
Sec. 74-172. - Additional ad valorem tax. 
All properties, both real and personal, located and situated within the boundaries of the district shall be subject to an additional ad valorem tax levy as set annually by the board of commissioners. 
(Res. of 2-13-1990, § 3) 
Sec. 74-173. - Use of additional taxes. 
(a)  All taxes collected from the additional levy within the district shall be used and appropriated only, to pay the cost of providing additional fire protection services within the district: 
(1)  Construct and maintain facilities for housing fire equipment and personnel within the district; 
(2)  Purchase equipment to be located and used within the district; 
(3)  Pay the cost of training for persons who provide fire protection services within the district; 
(4)  Pay the cost of materials and supplies used for training firefighters assigned to the district; 
(5)  Pay the cost of insurance provided on real and/or personal property located within the district and used to provide fire protection within the district; 
(6)  Pay for such other cost and expenses as may be deemed appropriate and needed for fire protection services within the district. 
(b)  All properties, both real and personal, purchased from taxes collected within the district shall be acquired in the name of the county, for the benefit of the various fire departments located within the district. All proceeds derived from the sale of any such acquired property shall be used in the same manner as the taxes levied within the district. 
(Res. of 2-13-1990, § 4, 6) 
Sec. 74-174. - Additional tax levy. 
Nothing in this division shall require an additional tax levy within the district, as this division is permissive and not mandatory. However, should a tax be levied by the board of commissioners within the district, then the tax must be used only for providing fire protection services in addition to such services as then being provided by the board of commissioners in the county which lie outside the district and not in any other special district. 
(Res. of 2-13-1990, § 7) 
Sec. 74-175. - Fire protection services. 
The providing of the fire protection services, as contemplated in this division, within the district may, at the discretion of the board of commissioners, be performed by the Calvary Volunteer Fire Department, Inc., a nonprofit state corporation, or such other party as may be selected by the board of commissioners from time to time, under such terms and conditions as established by the board of commissioners. Any such services arrangement shall be set forth in a contractual agreement and approved by the board of commissioners. The board shall review the manner in which any such contracted services are being performed on an annual basis when considering the levy to be made within the district. No contract shall be continued with any party not providing the required services. 
(Res. of 2-13-1990, § 5) 
Secs. 74-176—74-200. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 4. - COUNTY SPECIAL FIRE PROTECTION DISTRICT 

Sec. 74-201. - Tax district created. 
(a)  County Special Fire Protection District. There is hereby created a special tax district within the county which shall be known and cited as the "County Special Fire Protection District." 
(b)  Boundaries. The boundaries of the County Special Fire Protection District shall be as follows: 
That certain area of the county described and identified as follows: Beginning at the point where the southernmost point of the 334th General Militia District line intersects with the county boundary line; thence run in south and west directions along the county boundary line to U.S. Highway 82; thence run east along U.S. Highway 82 to Big Creek; thence run northerly along Big Creek to the county line; thence run in east and north directions along the county line to the Satilla River; then run north along the Satilla River to a point where, if extended, County Road 151 would intersect with the Satilla River; thence run along the extended line and then along County Road 151 to its intersection with Georgia Highway 110; thence run south along such Highway 110 to a point where County Road 166 intersects with the county line; thence run southerly along County Road 166 to the point where the road intersects with County Road 167; thence run in a southerly direction along County Road 167 to where the road intersects with Georgia Highway 32; thence run westerly along Georgia Highway 32 to the point where it intersects with the 334th General Militia District line; thence run southerly along the General Militia District line to a point where it intersects with Georgia Highway 110; thence continue in a southerly direction along such General Militia District line to the county line and the point or place of beginning, excluding and excepting all areas located within the incorporated area of the City of Nahunta and the City of Hoboken; this area being presently designated as district 3 on the records of the board of tax assessors of the county. 
(Res. of 9-25-2000, §§ 1, 2) 
Sec. 74-202. - Additional ad valorem tax. 
All properties, both real and personal, located and situated within the boundaries of the district shall be subject to an additional ad valorem tax levy as set annually by the board of commissioners. 
(Res. of 9-25-2000, § 3) 
Sec. 74-203. - Use of additional taxes. 
(a)  All taxes collected from the additional levy within the district shall be used and appropriated only, to pay the cost of providing additional fire protection services within the district: 
(1)  Construct and maintain facilities for housing fire equipment and personnel within the district; 
(2)  Purchase equipment to be located and used within the district; 
(3)  Pay the cost of training for persons who provide fire protection services within the district; 
(4)  Pay the cost of materials and supplies used for training firefighters assigned to the district; 
(5)  Pay the cost of insurance provided on real and/or personal property located within the district and used to provide fire protection within the district; 
(6)  Pay for such other cost and expenses as may be deemed appropriate and needed for fire protection services within the district. 
(b)  All properties, both real and personal, purchased from taxes collected within the district shall be acquired in the name of the county, for the benefit of the various fire departments located within the district. All proceeds derived from the sale of any such acquired property, shall be used in the same manner as the taxes levied within the district. 
(Res. of 9-25-2000, § 4, 6) 
Sec. 74-204. - Additional tax levy. 
Nothing in this division shall require an additional tax levy within the district, as this division is permissive and not mandatory. However, should a tax be levied by the board of commissioners within the district, then the tax must be used only for providing fire protection services in addition to such services as then being provided by the board of commissioners in the county which lie outside the district and not in any other special district. 
(Res. of 9-25-2000, § 7) 
Sec. 74-205. - Fire protection services. 
The providing of the fire protection services, as contemplated in this division, within the district may, at the discretion of the board of commissioners, be performed by certain volunteer fire departments located within the district, or such other party as may be selected by the board of commissioners from time to time, under such terms and conditions as established by the board of commissioners. Any such services arrangement shall be set forth in a contractual agreement and approved by the board of commissioners. The board shall review the manner in which any such contracted services are being performed on an annual basis when considering the levy to be made within the district. No contract shall be continued with any party not providing the required services. 
(Res. of 9-25-2000, § 5) 
Secs. 74-206—74-230. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 5. - SOLID WASTE DISPOSAL TAX DISTRICT 

Sec. 74-231. - Tax district created. 
(a)  Brantley County Solid Waste Disposal Tax District. There is hereby created a special tax district within the county, which shall be known and cited as the "Brantley County Solid Waste Disposal Tax District," sometimes referred to in this division as "the district." 
(b)  Boundaries. The boundaries of the Brantley County Solid Waste Disposal Tax District shall be as follows: 
All of the real property and nonhomestead mobile homes situated, located, lying and being within the unincorporated areas of the county. 
(Res. of 11-19-1991, §§ 1, 2; Amend. of 10-8-2002, § 2) 
Sec. 74-232. - Solid waste disposal fee. 
(a)  Definitions. The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this section, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Residential unit capable of being occupied by humans means a structure that has electrical hookup for any part of the year and is enclosed on four sides and has sewage disposal facilities. Provided, however, a structure being exclusively used for agricultural storage (hay storage, etc.), that is without sewage disposal facilities, shall be an exempt residential or commercial unit. 
(b)  Fee imposed. All real property and nonhomestead mobile homes located and situated within the boundaries of the district shall be subject to the imposition of a solid waste disposal fee. The fee shall be set annually by the board of commissioners and shall be a part of the annual county tax notice when possible or otherwise a supplement thereto. The solid waste disposal fee for the year 2002 on each residential unit capable of being occupied by humans on real property in the district, including each homestead mobile home, shall be in the amount of $85.00; and for the year 2003 on nonhomestead mobile homes located in the district which are capable of being occupied by humans, in the amount of $85.00; and in the amount of $85.00 for each commercial unit (a structure presently being used for or capable of being used for commercial/business operations) located on real property within the district, that has not contracted with some permitted solid waste disposal company for a period of 12 months covering the succeeding year (2003), for the disposal of solid waste from such commercial establishment (upon providing proof of such contracted disposal service, the fee shall be removed from such commercial unit). 
(c)  Exemption. A mobile home park (a defined area of land that is owned by an individual, husband and wife, partnership or corporation where at least 12 mobile homes are located and the park owner has obtained a business license from the county for a mobile home park business) shall be considered a commercial unit for exemption purposes as to all mobile homes located in the park, if such mobile home park has provided a solid waste collection container (dumpster) of at least six cubic yards for 12 mobile homes and an additional yard capacity for each additional two mobile homes. 
(Res. of 11-19-1991, § 3; Amend. of 12-3-2002, § 3) 
Sec. 74-233. - Use of fees. 
All fees collected from the solid waste disposal fee within the district shall be used and appropriated only, to pay the cost of disposal of solid waste generated within the county, and the necessary incidental related matters associated therewith, to include but not limited to the following: 
(1)  The purchase of garbage disposal dumpsters; 
(2)  The purchase, maintenance and operation of equipment for the collection of solid waste from solid waste dumpsters (this specifically does not include door-to-door collection); 
(3)  Transportation cost to the disposal site or transfer site; 
(4)  Any charges by way of a tipping fee for the disposal of solid waste; and 
(5)  For such other cost and expenses as may be deemed needed and appropriate from time to time by the board of commissioners in order to collect and dispose of the solid waste generated within the county. 
(Res. of 11-19-1991, § 4) 
Sec. 74-234. - Fee levy. 
Nothing in this division shall require a fee to be levied within the district as this division is permissive and not mandatory. However, should a fee be levied by the board of commissioners within the district, the fee must be used only for providing sanitation disposal services within the district as specifically set forth in this division, and none of the fees collected may be appropriated for any other purposes. 
(Res. of 11-19-1991, § 6) 
Sec. 74-235. - Solid waste disposal services. 
In order to provide the solid waste disposal service, as contemplated in this division, within the district, the board of commissioners may, at the discretion of the board of commissioners, enter into a contract with other parties who will receive the solid waste generated within the county and dispose of the solid waste in accordance with the appropriate laws and regulations, and charge the county for such disposal. Any such solid waste disposal arrangements shall be set forth in a contractual agreement and approved by the board of commissioners. The board shall review the expenses incurred for the disposal of solid waste within the county on an annual basis when considering the annual fee to be imposed within the district. 
(Res. of 11-19-1991, § 5) 
Sec. 74-236. - Fees due. 
All fees imposed within the district, as contemplated by the terms of this division, shall be due and payable on the same date as ad valorem taxes assessed in the county become due, and such fees shall be a lien against the nonhomestead mobile home and/or the real property upon which the residential or commercial unit is physically located, as provided for by O.C.G.A. §§ 48-2-56 and 12-8-39.3. Further, it is provided that the tax commissioner of the county shall be the officer charged with the enforcement and collection of any and all fees imposed under this division. 
(Res. of 11-19-1991, § 7; Amend. of 10-8-2002, § 7) 
Secs. 74-237—74-240. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 6. - NAHUNTA SPECIAL FIRE PROTECTION DISTRICT 

Sec. 74-241. - Tax district created. 
(a)  There is hereby created a special fire tax district within Brantley County which shall be known and cited as the "Nahunta Special Fire Protection District", hereinafter sometimes referred to as "the district". 
(b)  The boundaries of Nahunta Special Fire Protection District shall include all unincorporated areas of Brantley County as defined by the following border: 
Beginning at the Northwest corner of the District where the Satilla River intersects with Georgia Militia District #1565 which is a point on the Satilla River due North of the intersection of Petty Crossing and Raybon Rock Road West; thence traveling West and later South along the Satilla River to a point where it intersects the Charlton County Border at the intersection of Georgia Militia District #1354; thence Westerly along the Northern border of Georgia Militia District #1354 to its intersection with Georgia Militia District #1534; thence to the North along the Eastern border of Georgia Militia District #1534 until it intersects the Satilla River which was the point of origin. 
(Res. of 5-13-2003(1), §§ 1, 2; Res. of 9-14-2010, §§ 1, 2) 
Sec. 74-242. - Additional ad valorem tax. 
All properties, both real and personal, located and situated within the boundaries of the district shall be subject to an additional ad valorem tax levy as set annually hereafter by the Board of Commissioners of Brantley County. 
(Res. of 5-13-2003(1), § 3; Res. of 9-14-2010, § 3) 
Sec. 74-243. - Use of tax revenue. 
(a)  All ad valorem taxes collected from the additional levy within the district shall be used and appropriated only, to pay the cost of providing additional fire protection services within the district; to construct and maintain facilities for housing fire equipment and personnel within the district; to purchase equipment to be located and used within the district; to pay the cost of training for persons who provide fire protection services within the district; to pay the cost of materials and supplies used for training firefighters assigned to the district; to pay the cost of insurance provided on real and/or personal property located within the district; to pay for such other costs and expenses as may be deemed appropriate and needed for the fire protection services within the district. 
(b)  All properties, both real and personal, purchased from ad valorem tax revenue within the district shall be acquired in the name of "Brantley County, for the benefit of the Nahunta Fire Protection District". All proceeds derived from the sale of any such acquired property, shall be used in the same manner as the taxes levied within the district. 
(Res. of 5-13-2003(1), §§ 4, 6; Res. of 9-14-2010, §§ 4, 6) 
Sec. 74-244. - Additional tax levy. 
Nothing herein shall require an additional tax levy within the district, as the resolution is permissive and not mandatory. However, should a tax be levied by the board of commissioners within the district, funds collected must be used only for providing fire protection services within the district. Same must be used only for providing fire protection services in addition to such services as then being provided by the board of commissioners in the county which lies outside the district and not in any other special district. 
(Res. of 5-13-2003(1), § 7; Res. of 9-14-2010, § 7) 
Sec. 74-245. - Fire protection services. 
The providing of the fire protection services as herein contemplated within the district may at the discretion of the board of commissioners, be performed by the Nahunta Volunteer Fire Department Inc., a nonprofit Georgia Corporation, or such other party or parties as may be selected by the board of commissioners from time to time, under such terms and conditions as established by the board of commissioners. Any such services arrangement shall be set forth in a contractual agreement and approved by the board of commissioners. The board shall review the manner in which any such contracted services are being performed on an annual basis when considering the levy to be made within the district. No contract shall be continued with any party not providing the required service which meets the expectation of the Brantley County Commission. 
(Res. of 5-13-2003(1), § 5; Res. of 9-14-2010, § 5) 
Secs. 74-246—74-250. - Reserved.

District line intersects with the County boundary line, thence run in a south and then west directions along the County boundary line to the Satilla River; then run North along the Satilla River to a point where, if extended, County Road 151 would intersect with the Satilla River; thence run along said extended line and then along County Road 151 to its intersection with Georgia Highway 110; thence run South along said Highway 110 to a point where the centerline of said Highway intersects with the 334 th G.M. District line; thence run South along the 334 th G.M. District line to its southern point and the POINT OR PLACE OF BEGINNING.

DIVISION 10. - EMERGENCY MEDICAL SERVICE OPERATION AND MAINTENANCE SPECIAL FEE DISTRICT 

Sec. 74-281. - Creation. 
(a)  There is hereby created a special fee district within the county, which shall be known as the "county emergency medical service operation and maintenance special fee district", hereafter sometimes referred to as "the District". 
(b)  The boundaries of the "county emergency medical service operation and maintenance special fee district" shall be as follows: 
All of the real property lying, being and situate within the county wide geographical boundaries of Brantley County, Georgia, which shall include the incorporated and the unincorporated areas. 
(Ord. of 12-6-2012; Amend. of 8-8-2013, § 1, 2) 
Sec. 74-282. - Fees. 
All parcels of real property (excluding cemeteries) located and situated within the boundaries of the district, every residential structure being used as a residence or capable of being used as a residence which would include utilities, every commercial structure being used as a business or capable of being used as a business, or being used for storage or capable of being used for storage, every mobile home or mobile device or structure being used as a residence or capable of being used as a residence which would include utilities, and every parcel of 25 acres or more with no improvements thereon, shall be subject to the levying of an emergency medical operation and maintenance fee. The fee shall be set annually by the board of commissioners of the county and shall be a part of the annual the county real property and personal property tax notice from the office of the county tax commissioner, when possible or otherwise a supplement thereto. The initial emergency medical service operation and maintenance fee shall be as follows: for the year 2012 shall be $20.53 for every parcel in the district (excluding cemeteries); a fee of $75.70 for every commercial structure; a fee of $75.70 for every mobile home or mobile device or structure being used as a residence; and a fee of $75.70 for every parcel of 25 acres or more without any improvements thereon. 
All fees collected from the county emergency medical service operation and maintenance fee within the district shall be used and appropriated only, to pay for county operation and maintenance needs relating to the emergency medical service to the county's citizens within the unincorporated area of the county. 
(Ord. of 12-6-2012; Amend. of 8-8-2013, §§ 3, 4) 
Sec. 74-283. - Contracts. 
The board of commissioners may, at the discretion of the board, upon a majority vote, enter into valid contracts with such entities that may provide technical assistance and/or services relating to the operation and maintenance of the emergency medical service in accordance with appropriate laws and regulations, and shall be able to charge the county for said technical assistance and/or services. Any such contract shall be set forth in a contractual written agreement, approved by a majority vote of the board of commissioners in a public meeting of the said board. The board of commissioners shall review the emergency medical service operation and maintenance needs on an annual basis when considering the annual fee to be imposed within the district. 
(Ord. of 12-6-2012; Amend. of 8-8-2013, § 5) 
Sec. 74-284. - Additional fees. 
Nothing herein shall require a fee to be levied within the district as this article allows the board of commissioners to set a fee on an annual basis for the categories of properties set out in section 74-283. However, should a fee be levied by the board on an annual basis within the district, the same must be used only for the operation and maintenance of the emergency medical service within the district as specifically set forth herein, and none of the fees collected may be appropriated for any other purposes. 
(Ord. of 12-6-2012; Amend. of 8-8-2013, § 6) 
Sec. 74-285. - Additional ad valorem tax. 
Any fees imposed within the district as contemplated by the terms of this article shall be due and payable on the same date as ad valorem taxes on real property and personal property taxes assessed in the county become due. If said fee or fees as may be applicable to a residential taxpayer, is not paid as to any of the particular categories heretofore set forth, the following shall be applicable: 
(1)  In the event that a taxpayer contends that the taxpayer's property does not meet the classification assignment of the respective fee at the time the taxpayer pays the real property taxes and/or personal property taxes to the office of the county tax commissioner, then at that time, the office of the county tax commissioner shall inform the taxpayer by a written notice that the taxpayer shall have 15 days from the date of the receipt of the written notice from the office of the county tax commissioner as provided in this paragraph, to file a written appeal to the county manager setting forth the particular basis of the taxpayer's objection to the payment of the fee or fees as the case may be. The notice form shall provide for written receipt signed by the taxpayer of the notice of the right to appeal the taxpayer's contention with regard to the property classification to the county manager. 
(2)  The county manager, upon receipt of a timely written appeal, shall review the written appeal, and within 15 days after the receipt of the said written appeal as measured from the county's date stamp reflecting the date of receipt of the written appeal, notify in writing the taxpayer by first class mail at the taxpayer's last known address, as to whether the appeal is allowed or denied. 
(3)  If the appeal is allowed, the taxpayer shall be relieved of the payment of the fee or fees as the case may be. 
(4)  If the appeal is denied, the written notice to the taxpayer as set out in paragraph (2) shall notify the taxpayer that the taxpayer shall have the right to request to meet with the county manager to review the taxpayer's appeal, which meeting shall be recorded for the record. At the end of the meeting with the county manager, the county manager shall, within five days of the said meeting, advise the taxpayer in writing by first class mail to the taxpayer's last known address of the county manager's decision as to the appeal. 
(5)  In the event the county manager shall determine, either initially upon the receipt of a written appeal or after the hearing as heretofore provided, that the taxpayer's appeal is denied and the fee or fees is payable, and if the taxpayer refuses to pay the fee or fees as are applicable, the county manager shall notify the county magistrate court of the taxpayer's refusal to pay and the taxpayer shall be fined the sum of $200.00 plus the payment of the court costs. The magistrate court shall notify the taxpayer in writing by first class mail at the taxpayer's last known address that if the fee or fees as may be applicable are not paid within ten days of the date of the notice, that the taxpayer shall be summoned to the magistrate court and subject to being fined the sum of $200.00) plus the court costs for the failure to pay the fee or applicable fees as provided pursuant to this article. 
(Ord. of 12-6-2012; Amend. of 8-8-2013, § 7) 
Secs. 74-286—74-300. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VI. - ENERGY EXCISE TAX 

Sec. 74-301. - Definitions. 
As used in this ordinance, the terms: "dealer;" "energy;" "local sales and use tax;" and "purchaser" shall have the same meanings as provided in O.C.G.A. § 48-13-110. 
(Ord. of 11-8-2012) 
Sec. 74-302. - Imposition; rate; remitting; recovery; liabilities. 
In accordance with the provisions of O.C.G.A. § 48-13-110 et seq., there is imposed within the territorial limits of the special district created pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 48-13-111, an excise tax on the sale, use, storage, or consumption of energy when such sale, use, storage, or consumption would have constituted a taxable event for purposes of sales and use tax under O.C.G.A. § 48-8-1 et seq. but for the exemption in O.C.G.A. § 48-8-3.2. 
(Ord. of 11-8-2012) 
Sec. 74-303. - Excise tax rate; phase-in. 
(a)  Such excise tax shall be levied and collected by the governing authority of Brantley County pursuant to O.C.G.A. §§ 48-13-112 and 48-13-114 and as provided in this section. 
(b)  Except as otherwise provided in this section, the rate of such excise tax shall be phased in over a four-year period as follows: 
(1)  For the period commencing January 1, 2013, and concluding at the last moment of December 31, 2013, such excise tax shall be at a rate equivalent to 25 percent of the total amount of local sales and use tax in effect in such special district that would be collected on the sale, use, storage, or consumption of energy but for the exemption in O.C.G.A. § 48-8-3.2; 
(2)  For the period commencing January 1, 2014, and concluding at the last moment of December 31, 2014, such excise tax shall be at a rate equivalent to 50 percent of the total amount of local sales and use tax in effect in such special district that would be collected on the sale, use, storage, or consumption of energy but for the exemption in O.C.G.A. § 48-8-3.2; 
(3)  For the period commencing January 1, 2015, and concluding at the last moment of December 31, 2015, such excise tax shall be at a rate equivalent to 75 percent of the total amount of local sales and use tax in effect in such special district that would be collected on the sale, use, storage, or consumption of energy but for the exemption in O.C.G.A. § 48-8-3.2; and 
(4)  On or after January 1, 2016, such excise tax shall be at a rate equivalent to 100 percent of the total amount of local sales and use tax in effect in such special district that would be collected on the sale, use, storage, or consumption of energy but for the exemption in O.C.G.A. § 48-8-3.2. 
(c)  In accordance with O.C.G.A. § 48-8-3.2 (c)(4), if a project of regional significance under O.C.G.A. § 48-8-3(92) is started in the special district, it shall not be subject to the phase-in period contained in paragraphs (1), (2), and (3) of subsection (b) of this section, and the sale, use, storage, or consumption of energy in connection therewith shall be subject to the rate specified in paragraph (4) of subsection (b) of this section notwithstanding the January 1, 2016 limitation in that paragraph (4). 
(d)  (1)  Following such initial imposition during the phase-in time period, on or after January 1, 2016, the rate of the excise tax levied and collected by the governing authority of Brantley County shall be directed by O.C.G.A. § 48-13-112(d). Such rate shall be controlled by the maximum amount of local sales and use tax in effect in the special district, but in no event more than two percent. 
(2)  In the event the total rate of local sales and use taxes in effect in the special district decreases from two percent to one percent, the rate of the excise tax under this ordinance shall likewise be reduced at the same time such local sales and use tax rate reduction becomes effective. 
(3)  In the event the total rate of local sales and use taxes in effect in the special district increases from one percent to two percent, the rate of the excise tax under this ordinance shall likewise be increased at the same time such local sales and use tax rate increase becomes effective. 
(Ord. of 11-8-2012) 
Sec. 74-304. - Imposition; remittance; recovery. 
In accordance with O.C.G.A. §48-13-112(c), such excise tax shall be: 
(1)  Imposed only at the time sales and use tax on the sale or use of such energy would have been due and payable under O.C.G.A. § 48-8-30 but for the exemption under O.C.G.A. § 48-8-3.2; 
(2)  Due and payable in the same manner as would be required under O.C.G.A. § 48-8-1 et seq., except as other provided in O.C.G.A. § 48-8-110 et seq.; 
(3)  A debt of the purchaser of energy until it is paid and shall be recoverable at law in the same manner as authorized for the recovery of other debts; 
(4)  Remitted to the governing authority of Brantley County by the dealer collecting such excise tax; and 
(5)  A liability of the dealer at the applicable rate on the charges actually collected or the amount of excise taxes collected from purchasers, whichever is greater. 
(Ord. of 11-8-2012) 
Sec. 74-305. - Exemption certificates. 
(a)  The governing authority of Brantley County, or the collecting officer appointed under section 74-308 of this article, shall make diligent efforts to identify all energy providers and purchasers in the special district and to ascertain whether such a purchaser has completed a uniform exemption certificate provided from the website of the Georgia Department of Revenue seeking to qualify such purchaser for the exemption under O.C.G.A. § 48-8-3.2. Such certificate shall be utilized by such governing authority or collecting officer for the purpose of determining the applicability of the excise tax under this ordinance. 
(b)  An energy provider shall be authorized to rely upon such uniform exemption certificates. No penalty shall attach to such provider for failure to collect the excise tax under this ordinance when it has properly collected and remitted local sales and use taxes on such energy where the purchaser would have qualified for the uniform exemption certificate but failed to apply for such certificate or where the purchaser received such certificate but failed to file it with the energy provider. 
(Ord. of 11-8-2012) 
Sec. 74-306. - Commencement of collections. 
The excise tax imposed pursuant to this ordinance shall become effective on January 1, 2013, and shall be due and payable to the governing authority of Brantley County monthly on or before the twentieth day of every month and each respective month in which such taxes are collected, and payment shall be accompanied by a return for the preceding monthly period showing the gross sales and purchases arising from all sales and purchases taxable under this ordinance during the preceding calendar month. 
(Ord. of 11-8-2012) 
Sec. 74-307. - Allocation, distribution, and expenditure of proceeds. 
(a)  Pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 48-13-114 (b), the excise tax proceeds shall be allocated and distributed by the governing authority of Brantley County at the end of each calendar month. An amount equal to one percent of such proceeds collected by Brantley County shall be paid into the general fund of Brantley County to defray the costs of collection and administration. 
(b)  The remainder shall be distributed in accordance with the intergovernmental agreement as required under O.C.G.A. § 48-13-114 (b) and (c). Within 30 days following the end of each calendar month, the remainder shall be distributed to the general fund of Brantley County and the general fund of each participating municipality in accordance with the applicable provisions of O.C.G.A. § 48-13-114 (c)(1) or (2) as follows: 
(1)  If two local sales and use taxes are in effect in the special district, an amount equal to one-half of the proceeds shall be distributed to the general fund of Brantley County and the general fund of each participating municipality located in the county according to the same proportionate share as specified under the distribution provisions of the first local sales and use tax and an amount equal to one-half of the proceeds of the excise tax shall be distributed to the general fund of Brantley County and the general fund of each participating municipality located in such county according to the same proportionate share as specified under the distribution provisions of the second local sales and use tax; or 
(2)  If only one such local sales and use tax is in effect in the special district, then the proceeds of the excise tax shall be distributed to the general fund of Brantley County and the general fund of each participating municipality located in the county according to the same proportionate share as specified under the distribution provisions of the local sales and use tax. 
(c)  Except as provided in subsection (a) of this section, proceeds of the excise tax deposited in the general fund of Brantley County may be expended for any lawful purpose as determined by the governing authority of Brantley County. 
(Ord. of 11-8-2012) 
Sec. 74-308. - Administrative provisions; audits; examinations; collecting officer. 
(a)  The governing authority of Brantley County shall be authorized to designate a collecting officer for collection and administration of the excise tax under this ordinance. 
(b)  The collecting officer shall be authorized to provide for procedures necessary to the proper implementation of this ordinance, including, but not limited to, periodic auditing of dealers collecting and remitting the excise tax. The collecting officer, or the designee of the collecting officer, is specifically authorized to examine the books, papers, records, financial reports, equipment,, or other facilities of any purchaser which is required to remit the excise tax under this ordinance. 
(c)  In accordance with O.C.G.A. § 48-13-118, as part of the audit report required under O.C.G.A. § 36-81-7, the auditor shall include, in a separate schedule, a report of the revenues pertaining to the excise tax under this ordinance. 
(Ord. of 11-8-2012) 
Chapter 78 - TELECOMMUNICATIONS[1] 
Footnotes:

Cross reference— Businesses, ch. 26. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL

ARTICLE II. - CABLE TELEVISION FRANCHISE[2] 
Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference— Regulation of cable television systems by local governments, O.C.G.A. § 36-18-1 et seq.; municipalities prohibited from granting franchise for cable television within unincorporated area of county, O.C.G.A. § 36-18-3; avoiding or attempting to avoid charges for use of cable television service, O.C.G.A. § 46-5-2. 

DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 78-31. - Franchise necessary to operate business. 
It shall be unlawful for any person, to operate or attempt to operate any business or undertaking for the transmission by cable and distribution of television energy in the county without first obtaining a franchise from the board of commissioners. 
(Ord. of 3-14-1989, § 1) 
Sec. 78-32. - Granting of nonexclusive franchise. 
Any grant to a nonexclusive franchise to erect, maintain and operate in, over, along, across and upon the streets, roads, lanes, avenues, sidewalks, alleys, bridges, highways and other public ways or appurtenance or portions thereof, together with any and all extensions and additions thereto, for the sole purpose of transmission of cable and distribution of television energy for sale to the inhabitants of the county, shall be substantially in the form set forth in division 2 of this article. 
(Ord. of 3-14-1989, § 2) 
DIVISION 2. - CABLE TELEVISION FRANCHISE FORM[3] 
Cable Television Franchise 
This Franchise Agreement made and entered into this ____________ day of ____________ 20 ____________ , by and between BRANTLEY COUNTY, GEORGIA, acting by and through its Board of Commissioners, hereinafter referred to as Franchiser, and ____________ its successors and assigns, hereinafter referred to as Franchise. 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
Editor's note— Printed herein is the cable television franchise form which was adopted as part of the ordinance of 3-14-1989 which regulates cable television operations in the county. Obvious misspellings and punctuation errors have been corrected without notation. In order to facilitate indexing, catchlines have been added by the editor. 

Sec. 1. - Granting of rights. 
That for and in consideration of the faithful performance and observation of the conditions and reservations hereinafter specified, the right is hereby granted to Franchisee, its successors, assigns, designees, to erect, maintain and operate television transmission and distribution facilities and additions thereto in, under, over, along, across and upon the roads, streets, lanes, avenues, sidewalks, alleys, bridges and other public rights-of-way in that portion of Brantley County, Georgia, set forth herein as the "Franchise area," which area is described in Schedule "A" attached hereto, for the purpose of transmission and distribution of television impulses and television energy for a period of twenty (20) years from the date hereof, with the right of Franchisee to renew this franchise for an additional ten (10) year term. 
Sec. 2. - Definition. 
Whenever used herein, the word television shall mean a system for transmission of audio signals and visual images by means of electrical impulses. 
Sec. 3. - Approval of proposal. 
As a condition precedent for the granting of this franchise, Franchisee shall present for approval by the County Commission, in a public meeting following notification of such meeting, its proposal for providing cable television service within the franchise area as well as documentation of its legal character, financial and technical qualifications for providing such service. 
Sec. 4. - Pole erection and maintenance. 
The poles used for Franchisee's distribution system shall be those erected and maintained by Georgia Power Company, Okefenokee Rural Electric Membership Corporation, and Southern Bell Telephone Company, when and where practicable. Provided mutually satisfactory rental agreements cannot be entered into with said companies following a good faith effort on the part of Franchisee to obtain such agreements, Franchisee shall have the right to erect and maintain its own poles as may be necessary for the proper construction and maintenance of the television distribution system, with the approval of locating such poles retained by the County Commission. Further, the Franchisee shall have the right to run its transmission cable underground along the roads, streets, lanes, avenues, sidewalks, alleys, and other such public rights-of-way of Brantley. 
Sec. 5. - Transmission and distribution equipment and appurtenances; location; erection; maintenance. 
Franchisee's transmission and distribution system poles, wires, and appurtenances shall be located, erected and maintained so as not to interfere with the lives of persons or to interfere with new improvements this County may deem proper to make, or to unnecessarily hinder or obstruct the free use of the roads, streets, alleys, bridges, and other public property. The removal of poles to avoid such interference will be at Franchisee's expense. Construction and maintenance of the transmission and distribution system, including house connections, shall be in accordance with the provisions of the National Electrical Safety Code, as amended, and such applicable laws, ordinances and regulations of the United States of America, State of Georgia, or the County of Brantley, affecting same, which may be presently in effect or hereafter made. 
Sec. 6. - Installation of house drop hardware. 
Installation of house drop hardware shall be uniform throughout the County except that Franchisee shall be free to change its hardware and installation procedure as the art progresses. 
Sec. 7. - Underground service wires. 
In those areas where telephone-electric service wires are underground, Franchisee shall place its cable and services lines underground. 
Sec. 8. - Consideration of public in maintenance and operation. 
In the maintenance and operation of its television transmission and distribution system in the roads, streets, alleys, and other public places and in the course of any new construction of any new construction of additions to its facilities, Franchisee shall proceed so as to cause the least possible inconvenience to the general public; any opening or obstruction in the roads, streets, or other public places made by Franchisee in the course of its operations shall be made only after having obtained prior written permission from the County to do so and shall be guarded and protected at all times by the placement of adequate barriers, fences, or boardings, the bounds of which during period of dusk and darkness shall be clearly designated by appropriate warning lights. 
Sec. 9. - County-owned and/or County-controlled property. 
All work in any way necessitated by the business of Franchisee which may involve the opening, breaking or tearing up a portion of a road, street, sidewalk, or other part of County-owned or County-controlled property shall be done and repaired in the manner approved by the County Commission and may be done by the County at the expense of the cable operator if mutually agreed upon by the County Commission and Franchisee. 
Sec. 10. - Existing television reception. 
Installation shall be maintained so as not to interfere with television reception in existence. 
Sec. 11. - Forfeiture. 
The distribution system of Franchisee to be hereinafter installed shall not be abandoned, transferred or assigned, either in whole or in part, without the consent of the County Commissioners. In the event of the failure of Franchisee to commence construction of its cable system within 180 days after the granting of this franchise, or in the event of the failure of Franchisee to render cable television service (in this case, cable television service shall mean thirty (30%) percent of that portion of the county within the Franchise area, is receiving cable television on a regular basis) to the Franchise area and the inhabitants thereof as contemplated and provided for by this Franchise within a period of one year from the date construction begins, the County Commission may, after giving ninety (90) days notice to Franchisee, declare this franchise forfeited and/or require Franchisee to forfeit the surety bond required by Section 15 of this franchise agreement. Failure to comply by reason of circumstances beyond the reasonable control of Franchisee, which circumstances could not be anticipated at the time of acceptance of these terms shall not be sufficient grounds for the County to declare a forfeiture. 
Sec. 12. - Renewal at termination of franchise period. 
In the event Franchisee fails to renew its option at the termination of the franchise period, or in the event the franchise is forfeited due to the failure of Franchisee to fully comply with all terms and conditions of this agreement, or upon transfer or assignment of the franchise, the distribution system of Franchisee shall be placed up for sale at fair market value and the County of Brantley shall have first option of refusal on the purchase of the system. 
Sec. 13. - Protection; liabilities. 
Franchisee shall indemnify, protect and save harmless the County from and against all losses, physical damage to property, and bodily injury or death to persons including payments made under any worker's compensation law which may arise out of or be caused by the erection, maintenance, presence, use or removal of attachments on poles within the County of Brantley by any act of Franchisee. Franchisee shall carry insurance to protect the parties hereto from and against all claims, demands, actions, judgments, costs, expenses and liabilities which may arise or result directly or indirectly from or by reason of such loss, injury, or damage. The amounts for such insurance against liability due to physical damage to property shall not be less than One Hundred Thousand Dollars ($100,000.00) as to any one accident and against liability due to bodily injury or to death of persons not less than Three Hundred Thousand Dollars ($300,000.00) as to any one accident. Franchisee shall also carry such insurance as is deemed necessary to protect it from all claims under any worker's compensation laws as may be applicable to Franchisee. All insurance required by this agreement shall be and remain in full force and effect for the entire life of this agreement. Said policy or policies of insurance or a certified copy thereof shall be submitted for approval by the County attorney and then kept on file by the County Clerk with a signed copy of this Franchise. 
Sec. 14. - County's use of poles. 
Franchisee hereby grants to the County free of any expense joint use of any and all poles owned by Franchisee for any legal County purpose insofar as it may be done without interfering with free use and enjoyment of Franchisee's own wires and fixtures and County shall hold Franchisee harmless from any and all action, causes of action or damage directly caused by the County's use of the poles of Franchisee. 
Sec. 15. - Surety bond. 
At the time this franchise becomes effective, Franchisee shall furnish a bond to the County in the amount of Ten Thousand Dollars ($10,000.00) in such form with surety as shall be acceptable to the County, guaranteeing payment of all sums which may at any time become due from Franchisee to the County under the terms of this franchise (except such sums as are covered by the insurance provided in Section 13) and further guaranteeing the faithful performance of all the obligations of Franchisee under the terms of this franchise. 
Sec. 16. - Single outlet furnished to county; no charge. 
In consideration of the granting of this franchise to Franchisee as aforesaid, Franchisee will furnish without installation charge or monthly service fee a single outlet to the County, the specific location to be designated by the Commissioners within the Franchise area. 
Sec. 17. - Franchise fee. 
In further consideration of the granting of this franchise to Franchisee, Franchisee shall pay to Brantley County, no later than the 1st day of March each year following initiation of service, during the first ten (10) years of the Franchise an amount equal to three percent (3%) of the gross of all cable service revenues and 4 percent (4%) during the next ten (10) years of the franchise. Should Franchisee desire to exercise an option for renewal of additional years, then the franchise fee will be negotiated at that time. Revenues to include but not limited to subscriber revenues, advertising, pay cable, lease channel revenues, installation fees, disconnect and reconnect fees, and equipment rental of Franchisee derived from cable television operations within the Franchise area of Brantley County during the previous months. The County Commissioners shall have the right to inspect the records of Franchisee at any reasonable time for the purpose of ascertaining accurately what the actual gross receipts of Franchisee may have been for cable television service for past years and/or for the present year. 
Sec. 18. - Condition of installations. 
All installations by Franchisee shall be made in good, substantial and safe condition and shall be maintained in such condition at all times. Franchisee shall during each year of this agreement submit to the Board of Commissioners an annual performance report which shall be sufficient to ascertain Franchisee's compliance with F.C.C. technical standards and the quality of Franchisee's overall performance. Such report shall summarize all subscriber complaints and their resolution and said report shall be submitted to the County Commissioners on or before the regular Board of Commissioners meeting for the month of March of each year. 
Sec. 19. - Refusal of renewal; poor service. 
In the event such reports indicate that Franchisee is not providing a quality service consistent with F.C.C. rules or that subscriber complaints are so numerous or unresolved as to indicate a poor quality service, the County Commissioners may refuse to renew this Franchise with Franchisee. 
Sec. 20. - Annual financial report. 
Franchisee shall, during each year of this agreement, submit to the Board of Commissioners an annual financial report which shall be sufficient to ascertain the financial condition of Franchisee. Such report shall be submitted to the County Commissioners on or before the first day of June of each year. 
Sec. 21. - Compliance with regulations. 
Franchisee shall at all times be in full compliance with all F.C.C. regulations as amended pertaining to cable television systems. Franchisee shall furthermore at all times be in full compliance with all existing federal, state and local laws, ordinances, statutes as are applicable to the operation of a cable television system. No part of this agreement shall be construed as a waiver of any local, state or federal law or as a limit of liability. 
Sec. 22. - Proposal; compliance with terms. 
In addition to all rights, duties, obligations, and agreements contained in this franchise, Franchisee shall provide the Board of Commissioners with its cable service proposal which shall be attached to this agreement and Franchisee shall comply with each and every term and condition of the proposal in addition to the terms of this agreement, provided said terms of the proposal are not in conflict with provisions of this Franchise. Said proposal shall be incorporated herein by reference thereto and is expressly made a part hereof. 
APPROVED, ACCEPTED AND AGREED TO THIS ____________ day of ____________ , 20 ____________ . 

 
SCHEDULE "A" 
The description of the geographical area of Brantley County in which the franchise is granted. 
IN WITNESS WHEREOF, Brantley County, Georgia, has caused its official hands and seal to be placed hereon the day and year first above written. 

 
Chapter 82 - TRAFFIC AND VEHICLES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference— Offenses and miscellaneous provisions, ch. 54. 
State Law reference— Preventing or disrupting lawful procession, O.C.G.A. § 16-11-34; deposit of driver's license for violations of laws pertaining to traffic and motor vehicles, O.C.G.A. § 17-6-11; authority of county to regulate traffic in unincorporated areas, O.C.G.A. § 36-1-20; prosecution of traffic offenses, O.C.G.A. § 40-13-1 et seq.; traffic offenses triable on complaint without indictment except in superior courts, report of disposition, O.C.G.A. § 40-13-3; uniform rules of the road, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-1 et seq.; alteration of speed limits by local authorities, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-183; stopping, standing and parking, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-200 et seq.; Parking Law for Persons with Disabilities, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-220 et seq.; bicycles and play vehicles, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-290 et seq.; authority to regulate or prohibit stopping, standing or parking, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-371(a)(1); authority to regulate or prohibit processions or assemblages on the highways, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-371(a)(3); power of local authorities generally, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-371; adoption of uniform rules of the road by local authorities, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-372; funeral processions, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-76; operation of motorcycles and motor vehicles in parades, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-7; sirens, whistles and bells prohibited on vehicles, O.C.G.A. § 40-8-70(b); responsibility of railroad employees for obstructing crossings, O.C.G.A. § 46-8-197; authority to provide devices to control the flow of traffic, Ga. Const. art. IX, § II, ¶ III(a)(4). 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 82-1. - Uniform rules of the road adopted. 
(a)  Pursuant to O.C.G.A. §§ 40-6-372—40-6-376, O.C.G.A. §§ 40-6-2—40-6-395, known as the uniform rules of the road, and the definitions contained in the O.C.G.A. § 40-1-1 are adopted as and for the traffic regulations of the county with like effect as if recited in this section. 
(b)  Unless another penalty is expressly provided by state law, every person convicted of a violation of any provision of this section shall be punished in accordance with section 1-12. 
Sec. 82-2. - Speed detection devices. 
The board of commissioners approve and desire the procurement of and use of appropriate vehicle speed detection devices by the county sheriff's department. 
(Res. of 2-12-1985)
